Ruling on Silver Coins: Predominant Silver or Alloy
States rulings on coins where silver is predominant vs. where alloy is predominant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi predominance criterion to classify silver coins for zakat and determine the applicable zakat rules.

Core Idea
A coin’s zakat treatment depends on whether silver or alloy is the predominant component by weight.

This passage presents a foundational Hanafi rule for determining the zakat obligation on silver coins. Because coinage often contains alloy, the school does not treat all coins as pure silver. Instead, a simple test of predominance (al-ghalib) is used: if the coin contains more than 50% silver, it falls under the rulings of silver; if alloy predominates, it is treated as merchandise (tijarah). We will study the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn states two cases: (a) when silver predominates, and (b) when alloy predominates. Note that 'predominant' means more than 50% by weight.
This is a quantitative criterion, not based on common name.
2
Apply the legal consequence
For silver-predominant coins, they are treated as silver: subject to silver nisab (200 dirhams weight) and 2.5% zakat. For alloy-predominant, they are merchandise: zakat is based on market value and combined with other trade goods.
3
Recall the nisab thresholds
Silver nisab is 200 dirhams weight. Trade nisab is 200 dirhams value (or equivalent). Understand the difference between weight-based and value-based nisab.
4
Examine the proof
The hadith from Ali (ra) in Abu Dawud establishes the zakat rate for silver: one-fortieth (2.5%). This proof applies when the coin is treated as silver. The predominance rule itself is based on the general Hanafi principle that a thing takes the ruling of its predominant component.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۹۲] (۴) وان كان الغالب على الورق الفضة فهو في حكم الفضة [۴۹۳] (۵) واذا كان الغالب درهما فخذ منها درهما (الف) (دار قطنی ۳ ، باب لیس فی الکسرشی و ج ثانی ص ۸۰ نمبر ۶ ۸۸ ارسفن البیھقی ، باب ذكر الخير الذي روى في وقص الورق ج رابع ص ۲۲۸، نمبر ۷۵۲۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو سو درہم کے بعد جب تک چالیس درہم نہ ہو جائے تو اس کسر میں کچھ لازم نہیں ہے۔ البتہ چالیس درہم ہو جائے تو اس میں ایک درہم ہے۔ ابوداؤد میں ہے۔ عن علی ... هاتو اربع العشور من كل اربعین درهما درهم (ابو داؤد شریف ص ۲۲۷ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) (۴۹۱) (۳) اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دو سو درہم سے جو کچھ زیادہ ہو تو اس کی زکوۃ اس کے حساب سے ہوگی۔ مثلا دو سو درہم سے ایک درہم زیادہ ہو گیا تو ایک درہم میں ایک درہم کا چالیسواں حصہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور دس درہم میں ایک درہم کی چوتھائی لازم ہوگی۔ ے ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عاصم بن حمزة وعن الحارث الاعور عن على رضى الله عنه قال زهير احسبه عن النبي الله قال هاتو ربع العشور من كل اربعين درهما در هم وليس عليكم شيء حتى تتم مائتي درهم فاذا كانت مانتي درهم ففيها خمسة دراهم فمازاد فعلى حساب ذلك (ب) (ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ص ۲۲۷ نمبر ۲ ۱۵۷ار سن البیھقی ، باب وجوب ربع العشر في نصابها و فیما زاد علیه وان قلت الزيادة ج رابع ص ۲۲۷، نمبر ۷۵۲۱ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دو سو درہم سے جو کچھ زیادہ ہو اس کی زکوۃ اس کے حساب سے لازم ہوگی۔ اس لئے ہر روپیہ میں اس کے حساب سے چالیسواں حصہ لازم ہوگی کلیکیولیٹر سے چالیسواں حصہ 0.025 ہوگا۔
(4) And if the predominant (component) of the waraq (silver coins) is silver, then it is in the ruling of silver. (5) And if the predominant (component) is alloy, then it is in the ruling of merchandise. (a) (Dar Qutni, etc.) From this hadith it is understood that after two hundred dirhams, until it reaches forty dirhams, nothing is obligatory on that fraction. However, when it reaches forty dirhams, then one dirham is due. In Abu Dawud: from Ali: 'Give one-fortieth: from every forty dirhams, one dirham.' (Abu Dawud) (491) (3) And the two associates (Sahibayn) said: Whatever exceeds two hundred dirhams, its zakat is according to its calculation. For example, if one dirham exceeds two hundred dirhams, then on that one dirham, one-fortieth of a dirham is obligatory. And on ten dirhams, one-quarter of a dirham is obligatory. Their evidence is the hadith from 'Asim ibn Hamza and from al-Harith al-A'war from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who said (as reported by Zuhayr I think) from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Give one-fortieth; from every forty dirhams, one dirham. And nothing is due on you until you complete two hundred dirhams. So when you have two hundred dirhams, then five dirhams are due. And whatever exceeds, then its zakat is according to that calculation.' (b) (Abu Dawud, etc.) In this hadith, it is stated that whatever exceeds two hundred dirhams, its zakat is obligatory according to its calculation. Therefore, on every rupee, one-fortieth is obligatory. According to a calculator, one-fortieth is 0.025.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings regarding the nature of silver coins (waraq). The first ruling (4): If the predominant metal in the coin is silver (i.e., the coin is more than 50% silver), then the coin is treated as silver for zakat purposes. This means it is subject to the nisab of silver (200 dirhams weight) and the zakat rate of 2.5%. The second ruling (5): If the predominant component is alloy (ghalab), i.e., the coin is less than 50% silver, then it is treated as merchandise (tijarah). This means its zakat is based on its commercial value, and one must look at whether the total value of such coins reaches the nisab of trade goods (which is also 200 dirhams value). The Urdu commentary explains that pure silver is not used for coinage due to softness, so alloys are common. The criterion is the predominance of silver or alloy. The text also includes a hadith from Dar Qutni and Abu Dawud, which seems more relevant to the previous lesson but is included here as part of the continuous commentary. The key takeaway is that the zakat treatment of coins depends on their silver content.

Key Terms
الورق (al-waraq): Silver coins or unminted silver; also used for dirhams.
الغالب (al-ghalib): The predominant component by weight (more than 50%) in a coin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dirham coin is 40% silver and 60% alloy, how is it treated for zakat?
A) As silver
B) As merchandise
C) Only the silver portion is subject to zakat
D) It is exempt from zakat

Key Takeaway
The zakat obligation on a coin depends on whether its predominant component is silver (treated as silver) or alloy (treated as merchandise).

Coins with Predominant Silver – Zakat Ruling
Ruling on mixed silver coins with predominant silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mixed silver coins and apply the criterion of predominance to determine their zakat treatment.

Core Idea
If silver is more than half the coin, the whole coin is treated as silver for zakat.

Minted coins often contain alloy for hardness. This passage provides the Shari'ah criterion: if silver is predominant (al-ghalib), the coin is ruled as silver; if alloy is predominant, it is treated as trade goods. Understanding this distinction ensures correct zakat calculation on such coins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object
The subject is a mixed silver coin (dirham) containing both pure silver and alloy (e.g., copper).
Pure silver is too soft for minting, so alloy is added.
2
Determine the predominant metal
Predominance (al-ghalib) means more than 50% by weight. Assess whether silver or alloy constitutes the majority.
If silver is exactly 50%, the ruling is contested? The passage implies majority is needed.
3
Apply the rule
If silver is predominant, the entire coin falls under the ruling of silver (hukm al-fidda). If alloy is predominant, it falls under the ruling of trade goods ('urud).
This classification determines zakat calculation.
4
Calculate zakat for silver treatment
When treated as silver, zakat is wajib at 2.5% of the total weight of the coins, provided the total weight reaches the nisab of silver (approx. 612.36 g).
The entire weight is considered, not just the pure silver content.
5
Calculate zakat for trade goods treatment
When treated as 'urud, zakat is due on the market value of the coins as merchandise if that value reaches the nisab of silver or gold.
The coins are valued at their market price, not by metal content.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان الغالب على الورق الفضة فهو في حكم الفضة. اگر غالب چاندی ہے تو وہ چاندی کے حکم میں ہے۔ درہم اور دنا نیر بنانے کے لئے خالص چاندی کام نہیں آتی بلکہ اس میں کچھ نہ کچھ کھوٹ ڈالنا پڑتا ہے تا کہ سخت ہو جائے اور درہم یا دنا نیر ڈھال سکے اس لئے اصل معیار یہ رکھا گیا ہے کہ زیادہ چاندی یا سونا ہوتو وہ مکمل چاندی اور سونے کے حکم میں ہیں۔ اور اگر زیادہ کھوٹ ہو تو وہ سامان کے حکم میں ہے۔ الورق : چاندی سکہ۔
And if the predominant metal in silver coins is silver, then it is in the ruling of silver. If the majority is silver, then it is in the ruling of silver. For making dirhams and dinars, pure silver is not used; rather some alloy is added to make it hard and to mint dirhams or dinars. Therefore the standard is that if silver or gold is predominant, they are in the ruling of pure silver and gold. And if the alloy is predominant, then they are in the ruling of trade goods. Al-waraq: silver coin.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on mixed silver coins (dirhams). Since minted coins often contain alloy (copper or other metals) for hardness, the Shari'ah gives a criterion to decide their zakat treatment: if the coin's content is predominantly pure silver, it is considered silver (waraq) and its zakat is calculated based on the total weight of the coin as if it were pure silver. The commentator explains the reason for mixing: pure silver is too soft for minting. If the alloy is more than 50%, the coin is treated as a trade good ('urud), not as silver. The term 'al-waraq' is defined as silver coin.

Key Terms
الغالب (al-ghalib): The predominant element by quantity (more than 50%).
العروض (al-'urud): Trade goods or commodities subject to zakat as merchandise.
الورق (al-waraq): Silver coin or silver currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A dirham weighs 3 grams and is 60% silver and 40% copper. How is it treated for zakat?
A) As silver (waraq) because silver is predominant
B) As trade goods ('urud) because it contains alloy
C) As a coin but exempt from zakat
D) Only the silver portion is considered

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mixed silver coins are treated as silver for zakat only if silver is the predominant metal; otherwise they are trade goods.

Zakat on Excess Over 200 Dirhams: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for excess over 200 dirhams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat on the excess over 200 silver dirhams and calculate the zakat due according to each position.

Core Idea
For the Sahibayn, every extra dirham over 200 is zakatable proportionally; for Abu Hanifa, no zakat until the excess reaches 40 dirhams.

This passage presents a fascinating disagreement within the Hanafi school itself. While both sides agree that zakat is wajib on silver dirhams reaching the nisab of 200, they differ on how the excess beyond 200 is treated. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue for proportional zakat from the very first extra dirham, citing a hadith from Ali. Abu Hanifa, based on another hadith from Mu'adh, holds that the excess is exempt until it forms a new complete nisab increment of 40 dirhams. Understanding this dispute illuminates the role of hadith interpretation and the use of istihsan in Hanafi methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State clearly what each side holds regarding zakat on amounts between 200 and 239 dirhams. Sahibayn: zakat on every extra dirham. Abu Hanifa: no zakat on the excess until it reaches 40 dirhams.
Both agree on the nisab of 200 and the rate of 2.5%.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Read the hadith from Ali transmitted by the Prophet: 'Give a quarter of a tenth from every forty dirhams... And what exceeds, its zakat is proportionally.' Identify the operative phrase 'fama zad fa 'ala hisabi dhalik'.
This hadith is recorded in Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Read the hadith from Mu'adh cited in the marginal note: 'Do not take anything from the fraction; when silver reaches two hundred dirhams, take five dirhams; and do not take anything from what exceeds until it reaches forty dirhams.'
This hadith is also recorded in the same sources.
4
Analyze the reconciliation
Understand that the Sahibayn interpret the Mu'adh hadith as referring to the starting nisab, not the incremental excess. They argue that the Ali hadith is explicit and general, covering any increase.
The two hadiths are not necessarily contradictory if reconciled properly.
5
Calculate the practical difference
For a person with 210 dirhams, compute zakat under each view. Sahibayn: 5 dirhams for 200 + (10 × 0.025) = 0.25 = 5.25 dirhams. Abu Hanifa: only 5 dirhams until 240 dirhams.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابو يوسف و محمد مازاد على المائتين فزكوته بحسابه. اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دو سو درہم سے جو کچھ زیادہ ہو تو اس کی زکوۃ اس کے حساب سے ہوگی۔ مثلا دو سو درہم سے ایک درہم زیادہ ہو گیا تو ایک درہم میں ایک درہم کا چالیسواں حصہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور دس درہم میں ایک درہم کی چوتھائی لازم ہوگی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عاصم بن حمزة وعن الحارث الاعور عن على رضى الله عنه قال زهير احسبه عن النبي الله قال هاتو ربع العشور من كل اربعين درهما در هم وليس عليكم شيء حتى تتم مائتي درهم فاذا كانت مانتي درهم ففيها خمسة دراهم فمازاد فعلى حساب ذلك (ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی زکوۃ السائمة ص ۲۲۷ نمبر ۲ ۱۵۷ار سن البیھقی ، باب وجوب ربع العشر في نصابها و فیما زاد علیه وان قلت الزيادة ج رابع ص ۲۲۷، نمبر ۷۵۲۱ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دو سو درہم سے جو کچھ زیادہ ہو اس کی زکوۃ اس کے حساب سے لازم ہوگی۔ اس لئے ہر روپیہ میں اس کے حساب سے چالیسواں حصہ لازم ہوگی کلکیولیٹر سے چالیسواں حصہ 0.025 ہوگا۔ حاشیه : (الف) جب حضرت معادا کو یمن کی طرف بھیجا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ کسر میں کچھ نہ لینا، جب چاندی دو سو درہم ہو جائیں تو ان میں پانچ درہم لو، اور جو زیادہ ہو جائے ان میں سے کچھ مت لو۔ یہاں تک کہ چالیس درہم ہو جائے، اور جب چالیس درہم پہنچ جائے تو ان میں ایک درہم لو (ب) آپ نے فرمایا اؤ چالیسواں حصہ، ہر چالیس درہم میں سے ایک درہم ، اور تم پر کچھ نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ دو سو درہم پورے ہو جائیں۔ پس جب کہ دو سو درہم ہوں تو ان میں پانچ درہم ہیں۔ اور جو زیادہ ہو تو اس کی زکوۃ اس کے حساب سے ہوگی۔
And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: What exceeds two hundred, its zakat is proportionally. And the Sahibayn said: Whatever exceeds two hundred dirhams, its zakat is according to its calculation. For example, if one dirham exceeds two hundred, then one fortieth of a dirham is due. And for ten dirhams, one quarter of a dirham is due. Their evidence is this hadith from 'Asim ibn Hamza and al-Harith al-A'war from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) — Zuhair said, I think from the Prophet (peace be upon him) — he said: Give a quarter of a tenth from every forty dirhams, one dirham, and nothing is due from you until two hundred dirhams are complete. When there are two hundred dirhams, in them is five dirhams. Then what exceeds, its zakat is proportionally. (Abu Dawud, chapter on zakat of grazing animals, p. 227, no. 1572; al-Bayhaqi, chapter on obligation of quarter-tenth in its nisab and what exceeds it even if the increase is little, vol. 4, p. 227, no. 7521). In this hadith, whatever exceeds two hundred dirhams, its zakat is due proportionally. Therefore, for each rupee, one-fortieth is due; one-fortieth is 0.025. Marginal note (a): When the Prophet sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he said: Do not take anything from the fraction; when silver reaches two hundred dirhams, take five dirhams from them; and do not take anything from what exceeds until it reaches forty dirhams; and when it reaches forty, take one dirham from them. (b): He said: Give a quarter of a tenth; from every forty dirhams, one dirham; and nothing is due from you until two hundred dirhams are complete. So when there are two hundred dirhams, in them are five dirhams. And what exceeds, its zakat is proportionally.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the zakat on an amount of silver dirhams exceeding the nisab of 200. The matn states the view of Abu Hanifa's two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), who hold that any excess over 200 dirhams is subject to zakat at the same rate of 1/40 (2.5%) from the very first extra dirham. They base this on a hadith from Ali transmitted by the Prophet that says: 'What exceeds is according to that account.' The commentator explains that if one has 201 dirhams, zakat is due on the one extra dirham (1/40 of a dirham). The hadith is quoted in full. The marginal note (hasheeya) adds another hadith from Mu'adh indicating the opposing view (attributed to Abu Hanifa) that no zakat is due on the excess until it reaches 40 dirhams (i.e., the 'break' point for a full nisab increment). This shows the two positions within the Hanafi school: the Sahibayn's view that zakat applies to any increase proportionally, and Abu Hanifa's view that the increase is ignored until it forms a new nisab increment of 40.

Key Terms
الورق (al-waraq): Silver currency (coins minted from silver).
الكسر (al-kusr): The fraction or excess amount of silver dirhams below a complete nisab increment (40 dirhams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, how much zakat is due on 210 silver dirhams?
A) 5 dirhams
B) 5.25 dirhams
C) 5.375 dirhams
D) No zakat until 240 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on zakat for excess silver dirhams: the Sahibayn require proportional zakat from the first extra dirham, while Abu Hanifa only requires it when the excess reaches 40 dirhams.

Zakat on Coins with Predominant Alloy and the Inherent Zakatability of Gold/Silver
Ruling on alloy coins and the inherent zakatability of gold/silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for coins with predominant alloy and explain why gold and silver do not require trade intention for zakat.

Core Idea
Gold and silver are inherently zakatable; coins with more alloy are trade goods unless extracted pure metal reaches nisab.

This lesson tackles two intertwined zakat rulings. First, how to treat coins where the base metal outweighs the silver? Second, why are gold and silver zakatable even without the intention to trade? The passage resolves both by looking at the underlying substance (haqiqah) and the Shari'ah's classification of precious metals as inherently growing wealth (mal nami).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage covers two separate but related rulings: (A) coins where the alloy (base metal) is predominant, and (B) the general rule that gold and silver are zakatable without trade intention.
These are listed sequentially in the text; the second point is a general note.
2
Ruling on predominant alloy coins
When a coin has more than 50% alloy, it is classified as a trade good ('urud), not as silver. However, if the silver content can be extracted and reaches the nisab (200 dirhams), zakat becomes wajib because the underlying reality (haqiqah) is considered.
The text gives an example of extracting 200 dirhams of silver from a bulk of low-grade coins.
3
General rule: Gold and silver are mal nami
Unlike other trade goods, gold and silver do not require the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah) for zakat to be wajib. The Shari'ah has declared them inherently growing wealth (mal nami).
This means possession of gold/silver for a full lunar year at or above nisab triggers zakat, regardless of trade intent.
4
Understand the concept of mal nami
Mal nami is property that is capable of increase or is inherently considered growing. Gold and silver are considered nami by the Shari'ah, not by actual growth, because they are a medium of exchange and store of value.
This is a key distinction: other items (like livestock) are nami due to reproduction, but gold/silver are nami by legal classification.
5
Apply the conditions for zakat
For gold and silver to be zakatable: (1) they must reach nisab (85g gold or 595g silver), (2) a full lunar year (haul) must pass, and (3) they must be owned absolutely. The intention of trade is not a condition.
For the alloy coin scenario, these conditions apply to the extracted pure silver, not to the raw coin.

واذا كان الغالب عليه الغش فهو في حكم العروض و يعتبر ان تبلغ قيمتها نصابا . کھوٹ غالب ہے لیکن اس میں سے چاندی نکالی جائے تو اندازہ ہے کہ دو سو درہم تک کی چاندی نکلے گی اور نصاب تک پہنچ جائے گی تو اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اگر چہ کھوٹ غالب ہونے کی وجہ سے سامان کے حکم میں ہے لیکن اندر کی چاندی نکالی جائے تو وہ نصاب تک پہنچ رہی ہے تو حقیقت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے زکوۃ واجب کریں گے۔ ون سونے اور چاندی میں تجارت کی نیت کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ بغیر اس کے بھی ان میں زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ شریعت نے بغیر تجارت کی نیت کے بھی ان کو مال نامی بڑھنے والا مال قرار دیا ہے۔
And if the predominant (element) in coins is alloy, then it is in the ruling of trade goods, and it is considered that its value reaches the nisab. Alloy is predominant, but if silver is extracted from it, then it is estimated that 200 dirhams' worth of silver will come out, and it will reach the nisab, then zakat is wajib on it. Because, although due to the predominance of alloy it is in the ruling of trade goods, when the inner silver is extracted and reaches nisab, then considering the reality, we will make zakat wajib. And gold and silver do not require the intention of trade. Without it, zakat is wajib on them. Because the Shari'ah has declared them to be inherently growing wealth (mal nami) even without the intention of trade.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This lesson covers two related points. First, if a coin has more than 50% alloy (copper, nickel, etc.), it is treated as a trade good ('urud) rather than as silver. However, if the silver content can be extracted and the resulting pure silver reaches the nisab (200 dirhams weight), then zakat becomes wajib because the underlying reality is taken into account. The commentator gives an example: if from a large quantity of low-grade coins one can extract 200 dirhams of pure silver, zakat is due. This shows that the ruling considers both the apparent classification (trade good) and the actual substance. Second, the passage adds an important rule for gold and silver: unlike other trade goods, zakat on gold and silver is not conditional upon the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah). They are considered inherently 'growing wealth' (mal nami) by the Shari'ah, so zakat is obligatory whenever they reach nisab and a lunar year passes, regardless of whether the owner intends to trade or not. This distinguishes gold and silver from merchandise, which requires trade intention to be zakatable.

Key Terms
الغش (al-ghash): Alloy or impurity mixed with gold or silver in coins; the base metal (e.g., copper) used to harden the coin.
مال نامی (mal nami): Growing wealth; property that increases or is capable of increase, such as livestock, gold, silver, and trade goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true regarding zakat on gold in the Hanafi school?
A) Gold is zakatable only if it is intended for trade
B) Gold is zakatable without trade intention
C) Gold is never zakatable
D) Gold is zakatable only if it is in the form of coins

Key Takeaway
Gold and silver are inherently zakatable without trade intention; coins with predominant alloy are treated as trade goods unless extracted pure metal reaches nisab.

Nisab of Gold and First Ruling with Hadith Proof
First ruling of gold zakat: nisab and amount due with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab of gold in mithqal and the amount of zakat due, and explain the hadith proof that establishes this ruling.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold is wajib only when you own 20 mithqal (approx. 85g) for a full year, and the rate is 2.5% (half mithqal).

This passage establishes the foundational ruling for zakat on gold. It defines the minimum threshold (nisab) and the obligatory amount. The ruling is supported by a hadith from Ali (ra) which directly links the nisab of gold to twenty dinars and the due amount to half a dinar. Understanding this ruling is essential for calculating zakat correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the obligation of zakat for gold. It states the threshold (nisab) of 20 mithqal and the amount due: half a mithqal.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ali (ra) narrated by Asim bin Damra and al-Harith al-A'war is cited as proof.
The hadith is ahad (isolated), which affects its authority.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit mention of 'twenty dinars' establishes the nisab, and 'half a dinar' establishes the rate. The imperative formulation indicates obligation.
4
Note the hukm level
Based on this ahad hadith, the Hanafi school rules that zakat on gold is wajib (obligatory), not fard, because the proof is zanni al-thubut.
Fard would require a mutawatir or qat'i proof.
5
Confirm the zahir al-riwayah position
This ruling is the standard Hanafi position as recorded in the zahir al-riwayah (six core books of Imam Muhammad).
There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

Chapter of Zakat of Gold. 494 (1) There is no zakat on less than twenty mithqal of gold. So when it is twenty mithqal and a year passes over it, then in it is half a mithqal. Chapter of Zakat of Gold. The gold until may Allah bless him. [494] (1) There is no zakat on less than twenty mithqal of gold. So when we have twenty mithqal and a year passes over it, then in it is half a mithqal of zakat. In a hadith, from Asim bin Damra and al-Harith al-A'war from Ali from the Prophet (ﷺ) ... and nothing is upon you, i.e., until you have twenty dinars. So when you have twenty dinars and a year passes over it, then in it is half a dinar, and whatever exceeds is according to that calculation. (al-Dawud, Sunan, chapter on zakat of grazing animals, p. 228 no. 1573; al-Bayhaqi, chapter on nisab of gold and amount due, vol. 4, p. 232 no. 7534) From this hadith it is known that if there is twenty mithqal of gold, then half a mithqal is wajib, which is one-fortieth.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on zakat of gold. It states the first ruling: no zakat is due on gold weighing less than twenty mithqal (approximately 85 grams). When the gold reaches twenty mithqal and a lunar year passes while it remains in possession, then zakat becomes wajib at half a mithqal, which is one-fortieth (2.5%). The author then provides a hadith narrated by Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) as proof. The hadith states that there is no zakat on gold until it reaches twenty dinars, and when it reaches that and a year passes, zakat is half a dinar. The Arabic text of the hadith is quoted partially. The author concludes that this shows the nisab is twenty mithqal and the amount due is one-fortieth.

Key Terms
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight for gold and silver; one mithqal is approximately 4.25 grams.
دينار (dinar): A gold coin; one dinar is equivalent to one mithqal of gold.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on gold is wajib at the rate of 2.5% only when the gold reaches the nisab of 20 mithqal (approx. 85g) and a full lunar year passes.

Zakat on Excess Gold: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of excess gold: threshold vs. proportional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on zakat of excess gold beyond 20 mithqal, explain the thamarah al-khilaf, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, excess gold below 4 mithqal is exempt; for the Sahibayn, every fraction incurs zakat proportionally.

This passage introduces a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the zakat of gold. While 20 mithqal is the nisab, scholars differ on whether additional gold requires a minimum threshold before zakat becomes due. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for accurate calculation of zakat on gold savings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab
The base nisab for gold is 20 mithqal. At this amount, zakat is due at 2.5% (half a mithqal).
A mithqal is approximately 4.25 grams.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, no zakat is due on any excess gold until the excess itself reaches a minimum of 4 mithqal (i.e., total 24 mithqal). Then zakat on that 4 mithqal is 2 qirat (half a mithqal).
This is analogous to the ruling for silver, where a threshold applies to excess.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that zakat is wajib on any excess gold, however small, at the same rate of 2.5%. So if one has 21 mithqal, zakat is due on 1 mithqal.
They rely on the general command and a hadith: 'and whatever exceeds is according to that calculation.'
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
For someone with 21 mithqal: Abu Hanifa says no extra zakat (only 0.5 mithqal on the base 20); Sahibayn say extra zakat of 0.025 mithqal (2.5% of 1).
The difference is small but recurring annually.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
In later Hanafi practice, the view of the Sahibayn is preferred (mufta bihi). Thus, zakat on any fractional excess is obligatory.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text

[۴۹۵] (۲) ثم فى كل اربعة مثاقيل قيراطان وليس فيما دون اربعة مثاقيل صدقة عند ابي حنيفة وقالا مازاد على العشرين فزكوته بحسابها
[۴۹۵] (۲) پھر ہر چار مثقال میں دو قیراط زکوۃ ہے اور چار مثقال سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہیں مثقال پر جو کچھ زیادہ ہو تو اس کی زکوۃ اس کے حساب سے ہے۔ اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہیں، مثقال کے بعد جب تک چار مثقال سونا نہ ہو جائے کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ چار مثقال میں دو قیراط سونا لازم ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک میں مثقال سونے سے جتنا بھی زیادہ ہو گا اس میں اسی حساب سے زکوۃ واجب ہوتی چلی جائے گی ۔ دونوں کے دلائل باب زکوۃ الفضہ میں گزر چکے ہیں۔
[495] (2) Then for every four mithqal, two qirat, and there is no zakat on less than four mithqal according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Whatever exceeds twenty, its zakat is according to its calculation. [495] (2) Then for every four mithqal, two qirat of zakat, and there is no zakat on less than four mithqal according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: Whatever is in excess of a mithqal, its zakat is according to its calculation. It has passed above that according to Abu Hanifa, after twenty mithqal, until four mithqal of gold is reached, nothing is wajib. In four mithqal, two qirat of gold become wajib. And according to the Sahibayn, however much is in excess of a mithqal, zakat is wajib in it according to the same calculation. The proofs of both have passed in the chapter of zakat of silver.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat on gold exceeding the nisab of 20 mithqal. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, no zakat is due on any excess until the additional gold reaches 4 mithqal (i.e., a total of 24 mithqal), and then the zakat on that 4 mithqal is 2 qirat (which is half a mithqal, i.e., 2.5% of the additional amount). So if one has 21 mithqal, no zakat on the extra 1 mithqal; at 23 mithqal, still no zakat on the extra 3 mithqal; only at 24 mithqal does zakat become due on the 4 mithqal excess. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that any amount exceeding 20 mithqal, even 1 mithqal, incurs zakat proportionally at the rate of 2.5%. The author notes that the proofs for both views have already been discussed in the chapter on zakat of silver.

Key Terms
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 1 qirat equals 1/4 mithqal approximately. Two qirat = 1/2 mithqal.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two disciples: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation; for gold it is 20 mithqal (approx. 85g).
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight used for gold; 1 mithqal ≈ 4.25g. 20 mithqal = 85g.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half a mithqal for the first 20 mithqal plus zakat on the extra 3 mithqal proportionally
B) Half a mithqal only; no zakat on the extra 3 mithqal
C) Half a mithqal plus an additional 2 qirat for the extra 4 mithqal
D) No zakat at all because the total is not a multiple of 20

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that zakat is wajib on any excess gold above 20 mithqal proportionally, not merely when the excess reaches 4 mithqal.

Zakat on Gold: Nisab and Rate
First ruling on zakat of gold with nisab and rate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab of gold for zakat and calculate the zakat due at the rate of 2.5% per lunar year.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold becomes wajib at 20 mithqal (85 g) and above, at a rate of 2.5% per year.

Zakat is one of the pillars of Islam, and gold has been a primary form of wealth. This lesson establishes the minimum threshold (nisab) for gold and the exact amount due. We will examine the textual proof from the hadith and understand the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage governs zakat on gold. The ruling is that zakat is not due below 20 mithqal; at 20 mithqal, half a mithqal (2.5%) is wajib after one lunar year.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ali (ra) is cited, transmitted via 'Asim ibn Damurah and al-Harith al-A'war. It is recorded in Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi.
The hadith provides the nisab and rate.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith states: 'When you have twenty dinars and a year passes, half a dinar is due.' The word 'due' indicates obligation. The ratio is 1/40th, and for any excess, it is proportionate.
The imperative implies wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school follows this hadith; other schools may differ on the exact weight of the mithqal but accept the nisab. Intra-Hanafi, Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree on this ruling.
No major dispute within the school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text does not present a tarjih; the ruling is consensus among the Hanafi imams. The authority is zahir al-riwayah.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Zakat is not due on less than twenty mithqals of gold. So when it reaches twenty mithqals and a year passes over it, then half a mithqal is due. Then for every four mithqals, two qirats, and there is no zakat on less than four mithqals according to Abu Hanifa. And both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: whatever increases above twenty, its zakat is in proportion. The chapter on zakat of gold. In twenty mithqals of gold there is no zakat, so when twenty mithqals are present and a year passes, half a mithqal is due. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the zakat of gold. It establishes that zakat is not obligatory on less than twenty mithqals of gold. When exactly twenty mithqals are possessed for a full lunar year, one-half mithqal (i.e., 1/40th or 2.5%) must be given as zakat. The proof is a hadith from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi, which states the same for dinars (gold coins). The footnote clarifies the meaning of the hadith. This is the standard Hanafi position.

زکوۃ (zakah): Obligatory charity on wealth; one of the five pillars.

Zakat on Excess Gold: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat calculation for excess gold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on zakat for gold above 20 mithqal and apply the mufta bihi position to calculate zakat on any excess.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: zakat on excess gold due only in 4-mithqal increments; Sahibayn: any excess is zakatable proportionally.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement about how to calculate zakat on gold when the amount exceeds the nisab of 20 mithqal. Imam Abu Hanifa held that no zakat is due on the excess until it reaches a complete 4 mithqal, while his two major disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, ruled that any increase, however small, is zakatable proportionally. The proofs for each view were earlier discussed in the chapter on silver zakat. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for accurate zakat calculation in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the shared ruling on 20 mithqal
First, recall that all Hanafi imams agree that 20 mithqal of gold is the nisab and zakat of 1/20 (2 qirat per mithqal) is wajib on it. This passage addresses the excess above 20.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, no zakat is due on any amount below 4 mithqal above 20. Once a full 4 mithqal accumulates, zakat of 2 qirat (1/20th) is due. Thereafter, the same rule applies: increments of 4 trigger zakat.
This treats the excess like a new nisab threshold.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that any increase above 20 mithqal, no matter how small, is zakatable at the same proportional rate (2.5% / 1/20). The entire amount above 20 is subject to zakat.
This is the majority view across madhahib.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi works (e.g., Al-Hidayah, Al-Durr al-Mukhtar) adopt the Sahibayn's view as the mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa). In practice, zakat on gold above 20 mithqal is calculated proportionally on the total excess.
The text itself does not state tarjih, but the school's later preference is clear.

Source Text

Then for every four mithqals, two qirats, and there is no zakat on less than four mithqals according to Abu Hanifa. And both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: whatever increases above twenty, its zakat is in proportion. It has passed above that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, after twenty mithqals, until four mithqals of gold are not present, nothing is due. For four mithqals, two qirats of gold are due. According to the Two Companions, from twenty mithqals of gold, however much increases, zakat becomes due in that proportion. The evidences of both have passed in the chapter on zakat of silver.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on zakat for amounts above the nisab. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that after twenty mithqal, no zakat is due until another complete four mithqal is accumulated; then on four mithqal, two qirat (1/20th) is due. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that any increase above twenty mithqal, no matter how small, is zakatable proportionally at 2.5%. The text notes that the proofs for both positions have been discussed in the chapter on silver zakat. This difference affects practical calculation: under Abu Hanifa, if one has 21 mithqal, only 20 are zakatable; under the Sahibayn, all 21 are zakatable.

Key Terms
قيراط (qirat): A unit of measurement; here 1/20th of a mithqal. Two qirat = 1/10th mithqal.
صاحبين (sahibayn): The two major disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that zakat on any excess gold above 20 mithqal is due proportionally at 2.5%, following the Sahibayn.

Zakat on Gold and Silver Jewelry: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on zakat for gold/silver jewelry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on zakat for gold and silver jewelry and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, all gold and silver—jewelry included—is subject to zakat; the Shafi'i exception for adornment is rejected.

Zakat on gold and silver is a foundational obligation, but a key disagreement arises when these metals are fashioned into jewelry or utensils. Where the Hanafi school sees continued liability, one Shafi'i view exempts ornamental items. Understanding this dispute clarifies how each school weighs general principles versus specific practices.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what exactly the Hanafi school rules regarding zakat on gold and silver jewelry, bullion, and utensils.
The ruling is that zakat is wajib in all forms.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (in one of his sayings) exempts jewelry from zakat.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith of Aisha (ra) who did not pay zakat on the jewelry of orphan girls under her care.
The hadith is cited as a practice implying permissibility.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school rebuts this proof: the hadith may not be general, or Aisha may have paid later.
The Hanafi position relies on the general command for zakat on gold and silver.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis obligate zakat on jewelry; the Shafi'i view does not.
This affects millions of Muslims who own gold jewelry.

Source Text

سونے اور چاندی کے ڈلے، ان دونوں کے زیور اور ان دونوں کے برتن میں زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ سونا اور چاندی کسی حال میں ہو، چاہے درہم اور دینار کی شکل میں ہو، ڈلے کی شکل میں ہو یا برتن اور زیور کی شکل میں ہو ہر حال میں حنفیہ کے نزدیک زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ اس کی دلیل باب زکوۃ الفضۃ کے شروع میں گزر چکی ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے ایک قول میں زیور میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان عائشة زوج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كانت على بنات اخيها يتامي في حجرها لهن الحلي فلا تخرج منه الزكوة (الف) ( سنن بیھقی باب من قال لا زكوة في المحلى ج رابع ص ۲۳۲ نمبر ۷۵۳۵)

And on gold and silver bullion, their jewelry, and utensils made from them, zakat is obligatory. On gold and silver lumps, their jewelry, and their utensils, zakat is obligatory. Gold and silver in any form, whether in the form of dirhams and dinars, lumps, or utensils and jewelry, in every case according to the Hanafis zakat is obligatory. Its proof has passed at the beginning of the chapter on zakat of silver. And Imam al-Shafi'i in one of his sayings: there is no zakat on jewelry. Their proof is this hadith: 'Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, used to look after her brother's daughters who were orphans under her care; they had jewelry, so she did not take zakat out of it.' (Reference) Footnote: (ب) Aisha looked after her brother's daughters who were orphans and in her lap. They had jewelry, so Aisha did not pay zakat on it.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on zakat on gold and silver jewelry. The Hanafi school holds that zakat is obligatory on gold and silver in any form, including bullion, jewelry, and utensils. The proof is analogical: if it is gold or silver, it is subject to zakat regardless of form. Imam al-Shafi'i (in one view) exempts jewelry from zakat, citing the practice of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who did not pay zakat on her orphan nieces' jewelry. The Hanafis respond that Aisha's action is not necessarily evidence for permissibility; she may have paid later or it may not be general. The Hanafi position is based on the general command for zakat on gold and silver, and the fact that jewelry can be melted down, so it retains its value as wealth.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Bullion or raw ore of gold or silver, not minted into coins.
حلية (hilyah): Jewelry or ornaments made from gold or silver.
آنية (aniyah): Utensils made of gold or silver.

Zakat on Trade Goods: Obligation When Value Reaches Nisab
First ruling on zakat of trade goods: obligation when value reaches nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on zakat of trade goods and identify the condition that triggers the obligation.

Core Idea
Trade goods are zakatable when their value reaches nisab and a year passes.

This lesson examines the obligation of zakat on goods acquired for trade. The classical Hanafi text establishes that zakat becomes wajib when the market value of such goods reaches the nisab threshold. We will trace the proof from the Sunnah and clarify the precise conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. The act is paying zakat on trade goods (urud al-tijarah). The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
The passage begins with 'Al-zakatu wajibatun fi 'urud al-tijarah'.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited. The passage quotes a hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet commanded giving charity from goods prepared for sale.
Two narrations: Abu Dawud and al-Daraqutni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The command (amr) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The phrase 'min alladhi nu'iddu lil-bay' specifies that it applies to goods intended for sale, i.e., trade goods.
The command is explicit, and the subject is trade goods.

Chapter on Zakat of Trade Goods. Zakat is obligatory on trade goods whatever they may be when their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. Zakat is obligatory on trade goods of whatever type, when they reach the nisab of silver or gold. Any trade goods, their value will be assessed, whether by gold or by silver. If this value equals the nisab of gold or silver and a year passes, then zakat is obligatory. In a hadith: from Samurah ibn Jundub, he said: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah used to command us to give charity from what we prepare for sale.' (Reference) And in al-Daraqutni: from Samurah... 'and he used to command us to pay charity from the slave prepared for sale.' From this hadith it is learned that zakat is obligatory on trade goods, but goods not for trade are not subject to zakat. Footnote: (ا) He used to command us to pay zakat on that which is prepared for sale. (ب) Samurah ibn Jundub said: He commanded us to pay zakat on the slave prepared for sale, i.e., for trade.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on zakat of trade goods. It establishes that zakat is obligatory on any goods intended for trade (not for personal use) when the market value reaches the nisab of silver or gold (whichever is lower? The text says whichever reaches nisab). The proof is from Sunnah: hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet commanded zakat on items prepared for sale. Another narration includes slaves prepared for sale. This shows trade goods are subject to zakat. The footnote clarifies the meaning of the hadith. Non-trade goods (e.g., personal items) are not subject to zakat.

Key Terms
عروض التجارة (urud al-tijarah): Goods acquired for the purpose of trade, not for personal use.
ورق (waraq): Silver coins or silver in general.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on trade goods is wajib when their value reaches nisab and a year passes, based on the Prophet's command to give charity from what is prepared for sale.

Valuing Trade Goods: The More Beneficial Metal
Ruling on how to value trade goods for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for valuing trade goods for zakat and apply it to determine when zakat becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Trade goods are valued by whichever metal (gold or silver) benefits the poor more—ensuring maximum zakat.

When calculating zakat on trade goods, the owner must determine their value in terms of gold or silver. The Hanafi school specifies that the valuation should use the metal that is more beneficial to the poor, meaning the one that yields a higher zakat liability or makes nisab more likely to be reached. This principle protects the rights of the poor and ensures zakat is not evaded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the valuation (taqwim) of trade goods for zakat. The ruling is that it must be done with the metal (gold or silver) that is more beneficial to the poor.
This is a wajib step; incorrect valuation may invalidate the zakat calculation.
2
Understand the rationale
The phrase 'more beneficial to the poor' means choosing the metal that gives a higher valuation (or a lower nisab threshold) so that zakat becomes obligatory sooner or in a larger amount.
Gold nisab is lower than silver nisab; using gold typically gives a higher zakat amount.
3
Apply the rule
For trade goods, calculate the market value in gold and in silver. Compare the two valuations. Use the one that yields a higher zakat (or makes nisab more likely). If either valuation reaches nisab, zakat is wajib.
The owner does not have a choice; the rule is imposed for the benefit of the poor.
4
Confirm the source
The text references Bukhari and Abu Dawud, indicating the proof for zakat on trade goods is established elsewhere.
This passage is a ruling statement; the detailed proof is in earlier chapters.

Source Text

When calculating zakat, the owner should value the trade goods by whichever of gold or silver gives a lower nisab (or more beneficial to the poor? The text says 'more beneficial for the poor', which means the valuation should be in the metal that gives a higher zakat amount? Actually, more beneficial to the poor is to have the valuation yield a higher zakat, so the owner might choose the metal that results in a lower valuation to reduce zakat? Hanafi fiqh: The owner should value the goods by whichever metal (gold or silver) is more beneficial to the poor, i.e., the one that gives a higher zakat value. This is to protect the right of the poor. The proof for zakat by valuation is referenced from earlier chapters.

Nisab at Both Ends of the Year: Temporary Deficit Does Not Drop Zakat
Ruling on temporary deficit not dropping zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that zakat is based on nisab at the beginning and end of the year and apply the exception of total loss.

Core Idea
Zakat depends on nisab at start and end; a middle dip is ignored unless total loss.

This lesson presents a core Hanafi principle in zakat: only the beginning and end of the lunar year are considered for nisab. A temporary decrease during the year does not break the haul (annual cycle). However, if the entire nisab is lost, the year resets. This ruling facilitates zakat calculation for fluctuating wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zakat on wealth. The ruling: zakat is wajib (obligatory) when conditions are met.
Zakat is one of the five pillars.
2
State the condition of nisab stability
The key condition: nisab must be complete at both ends of the lunar year (beginning and end). A temporary deficit in the middle does not cancel zakat.
Hanafis do not require nisab throughout the year.
3
Distinguish between temporary deficit and total loss
If nisab drops but wealth remains, zakat is still due at year-end. If all wealth is destroyed (total loss), the haul resets, and a new year begins when nisab is regained.
Total loss means the entire nisab wealth is gone, not just reduced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۴۹۹ (۳) واذا كان النصاب كاملا في طرفي الحول فنقصانه فيما بين ذلك لا يسقط الزكوة 
اگر نصاب سال کے دونوں کناروں میں کامل ہو تو سال کے درمیان نقصان ہونا زکوۃ ساقط نہیں کرتا۔ مثلا رمضان میں کسی مال کا مکمل نصاب ہے اور محرم میں نصاب سے کم ہو گیا پھر رمضان میں نصاب مکمل ہو گیا تو زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر در میان سال میں مکمل ہی نصاب کا مال ختم ہو گی تو چونکہ بالکل جڑ سے مال نہیں رہا اس لئے اب جب سے نصاب ہوگا اس وقت سے زکوۃ کا
And if the nisab is complete at both ends of the year, then its decrease in between that does not drop the zakat. If the nisab is complete at both ends of the year, then a decrease in the middle does not drop zakat. For example, in Ramadan one has complete nisab, and in Muharram it becomes less than nisab, then in Ramadan it becomes complete again, then zakat becomes obligatory. Yes, if in the middle of the year the entire nisab wealth is destroyed, then since the wealth has completely disappeared, from then when nisab is reached anew, zakat is (calculated anew).
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the condition of nisab stability for zakat. The key principle: zakat is based on the possession of nisab at the beginning and end of the lunar year. A temporary drop below nisab during the year does not break the haul (annual cycle). The example: if one has complete nisab in Ramadan, then in Muharram it falls below, then by Ramadan it is again at nisab, zakat is due for that year. However, if the entire nisab is lost (e.g., all wealth destroyed, not just decreased), then the haul resets, and a new year begins when nisab is regained.

Key Terms
طرفا الحول (tarafay al-hawl): The beginning and the end of the lunar year for zakat calculation.
نصاب (nisab): Minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone has 200 dirhams (nisab) in Shawwal, drops to 150 in Muharram, and returns to 200 in the next Shawwal, what is the zakat ruling?
A) Zakat is not due because the nisab was not maintained
B) Zakat is due on the amount at the end of the year
C) Zakat is due because nisab was present at both ends
D) Zakat is due only on the 150 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Zakat remains wajib if nisab is complete at both ends of the lunar year; a temporary deficit in the middle does not drop the obligation.

Valuing Trade Goods for Zakat: The Poor's Benefit
Ruling on valuation method for zakat on trade goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how trade goods must be valued for zakat and explain why the valuation must be based on what is more beneficial for the poor.

Core Idea
Trade goods are valued at whichever metal (gold or silver) benefits the poor more.

This lesson covers a key principle in zakat on trade goods ('urud al-tijara). The Hanafi school mandates that when paying zakat on trade goods, the owner must value the goods in a way that maximizes benefit to the recipients. This means choosing the higher valuation between gold and silver, ensuring the poor receive a larger amount. The ruling is based on the general evidence for valuation in zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage rules that trade goods must be valued by what is more beneficial for the poor and needy.
This is a directive, not optional.
2
Understand the two metals
The valuation is made using gold or silver—whichever gives a higher value for the goods.
If gold is higher, value in gold; if silver is higher, value in silver.
3
Apply to nisab
Once the valuation reaches the nisab threshold (value of 20 mithqal gold or 200 dirhams silver), zakat becomes wajib.
Nisab is calculated based on the chosen metal.
4
Note the wisdom
The purpose is to maximize the benefit for the poor, ensuring they receive the highest possible zakat amount.
This reflects the spirit of zakat as a welfare institution.
5
Recognize the proof
The proof for valuation in zakat on trade goods is established from earlier evidences (e.g., hadith and consensus).
The valuation method itself is derived from the principle of maslahah (public interest).

Source Text

يقومها بما هو انفع للفقراء والمساكين منها [۴۹۸] (۲) سامان تجارت کی قیمت لگائی جائے گی اس چیز سے جو فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے زیادہ نفع بخش ہو۔ سونا یا چاندی جو فقراء اور مساکین کے لئے زیادہ نفع بخش ہو اس سے سامان تجارت کی قیمت لگائی جائے گی ۔ اور وہ قیمت نصاب تک پہنچ جائے تو اس کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ کسی چیز کی قیمت لگا کر زکوۃ دینے کی دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
He values it by what is more beneficial for the poor and needy from them. (2) The trade goods will be valued by whatever is more beneficial for the poor and needy. The trade goods will be valued by gold or silver whichever is more beneficial for the poor and needy. And if that value reaches the nisab, zakat is obligatory. The proof for giving zakat by valuation has passed before.

Commentary
This passage explains the method of valuation for trade goods. The scholar states that the valuation should be based on whichever metal (gold or silver) yields a greater benefit for the poor. For example, if gold price is high, value in gold; if silver price is higher, value in silver. The proof for valuation is from previously mentioned evidences (such as the hadith on valuation). This ensures that the poor receive the maximum benefit from the zakat.

Key Terms
يقومها (yuqawwimuha): He values it; the act of determining the monetary value of trade goods.
انفع للفقراء والمساكين (anfa' lil-fuqara' wal-masakin): More beneficial for the poor and needy; refers to choosing the higher valuation among gold or silver.

Nisab at Both Ends of the Year
Ruling on nisab continuity for zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that zakat remains obligatory if nisab is complete at both ends of the year, and apply it to scenarios of mid-year fluctuations and total destruction.

Core Idea
Zakat depends on nisab at start and end; mid-year drops do not break obligation.

Many assume that any dip in wealth during the year cancels the zakat obligation. The Hanafi school clarifies that only the beginning and end of the lunar year matter. A temporary decrease mid-year does not waive zakat, provided nisab is complete at both ends. However, if the entire nisab wealth is destroyed, the year resets. This lesson unpacks that rule and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the obligation of zakat on wealth. The ruling is that zakat is wajib when nisab is present at both ends of the lunar year.
Nisab at start initiates the obligation; nisab at end confirms it.
2
Examine the condition: nisab at both ends
The condition for zakat to be due is that the wealth reaches nisab at the beginning and the end of the year. Mid-year fluctuations are irrelevant.
This is a facilitative ruling to avoid hardship from constant recalculations.
3
Recognize the exception: total destruction
If the entire wealth is destroyed (e.g., lost, stolen, or consumed), the year resets. Zakat obligation begins anew when nisab is regained.
Partial decrease does not reset; only complete disappearance triggers restart.
4
Apply the rule to concrete scenarios
Use the example from the text: If nisab is full in Ramadan, drops in Muharram, and returns by Ramadan, zakat is due. If the wealth completely vanishes in Muharram, a new year starts from the date nisab returns.
The ruling emphasizes continuity and ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا كان النصاب كاملا في طرفي الحول فنقصانه فيما بين ذلك لا يسقط الزكوة [۴۹۹] (۳) اگر نصاب سال کے دونوں کناروں میں کامل ہو تو سال کے درمیان نقصان ہونا زکوۃ ساقط نہیں کرتا۔ ات مثلا رمضان میں کسی مال کا مکمل نصاب ہے اور محرم میں نصاب سے کم ہو گیا پھر رمضان میں نصاب مکمل ہو گیا تو زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر در میان سال میں مکمل ہی نصاب کا مال ختم ہو گی تو چونکہ بالکل جڑ سے مال نہیں رہا اس لئے اب جب سے نصاب ہوگا اس وقت سے زکوۃ کا مہینہ شروع ہوگا۔ شروع میں نصاب ہونا زکوۃ کے انعقاد کے لئے ہے اور اخیر میں نصاب ہونا زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے ہے، اور درمیان میں کمی بیشی ہوتی رہتی ہے اس لئے اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا۔
And if the nisab is complete at both ends of the year, its decrease in between does not waive zakat. (3) If the nisab is complete at both ends of the year, then a deficiency in between does not drop the zakat. For example, in Ramadan someone has a complete nisab of wealth, and in Muharram it decreases below nisab, then in Ramadan it becomes complete again, so zakat is obligatory. However, if during the year the entire nisab wealth is destroyed, then because the wealth is completely gone, from when the nisab occurs again, the month of zakat will start. Having nisab at the beginning is for the inception of zakat, and having nisab at the end is for zakat becoming obligatory, and in between increases and decreases occur, so they are not considered.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage clarifies the temporal condition of nisab. The ruling states that zakat remains obligatory as long as the nisab is complete at the beginning and end of the lunar year. A temporary drop below nisab mid-year does not break the obligation. However, if the entire capital is destroyed and disappears completely, then the obligation resets and a new year begins when nisab is regained. The commentary uses the example of Ramadan to Ramadan: if nisab is full in Ramadan, decreases in Muharram, and returns in Ramadan, zakat is due. The rationale is that nisab at the start establishes the obligation's inception, nisab at the end confirms its completion, and fluctuations in between are disregarded for the sake of continuity.

Key Terms
طرفي الحول (tarafay al-hawl): Both ends of the lunar year; i.e., the beginning and the end.
نقصانه فيما بين ذلك (nuqsanuhu fima bayna dhalik): A decrease in nisab occurring during the middle of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The obligation resets from the time nisab returns

Key Takeaway
Zakat obligation hinges on nisab at the start and end of the year; mid-year dips do not break it, only total destruction resets the year.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Adding Gold and Silver Values for Nisab
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining gold and silver for nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on combining gold and silver for zakat nisab and evaluate the practical consequence of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa adds gold and silver by value; the Sahibayn add by weight — the difference determines zakat obligation.

This passage presents one of the classic intra-Hanafi disagreements in zakat law. When a person owns both gold and silver, and neither alone reaches the nisab threshold, can they be combined to complete the nisab? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on the method of combination. This lesson unpacks the two positions, their underlying reasoning, and the practical ruling for a person who owns a mix of gold and silver.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The issue is whether gold and silver can be combined to complete the zakat nisab when neither alone reaches the threshold. The method of combination—by value or by weight—is contested.
Both metals are zakatable, but they have different nisab values: 20 mithqal (85g) for gold, 200 dirhams (595g) for silver.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position (damm bil-qimah)
Abu Hanifa holds that gold and silver can be combined by their monetary value. Thus, if the sum of their values equals the nisab of one (e.g., 200 dirhams), zakat becomes wajib.
This view treats both as currency; value is the common measure.
3
State the Sahibayn's position (damm bil-ajza')
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that gold and silver must be combined by weight (parts). Each metal is considered separately; only if the weight of gold reaches 10 mithqal or silver reaches 100 dirhams can they complement each other.
This view treats each metal as a distinct genus; zakat is on the weight of each.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Take a person who has 100 dirhams (half niṣāb of silver) and 9 mithqal of gold (value 100 dirhams). According to Abu Hanifa, the total value is 200 dirhams, so zakat is wajib. According to the Sahibayn, the gold weight is less than 10 mithqal, so nisab is not completed; no zakat.
The practical difference is clear: zakat obligation changes based on the method.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Although the passage does not state a preferred view, the later Hanafi authorities generally rely on Abu Hanifa's opinion. In fatwa, combining by value is the operative ruling.
Always check the context: if the student intends to give fatwa, the mufta bihi should be applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۵۰۰ (۴) ويضم قيمة العروض الى الذهب والفضة وكذلك يضم الذهب الى الفضة بالقيمة حتى يتم النصاب عند ابي حنيفة [ ۵۰۱] (۵) وقالا لا يضم الذهب الى الفضة بالقيمة ويضم بالاجزاء. و سامان تجارت کی بھی قیمت لگائی جائے گی اور اس کو سونے یا نقد چاندی کے ساتھ ملا کر نصاب پورا ہو جائے تو زکوۃ واجب کریں گے۔ ۵۰۱] (۵) صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ سونے کو چاندی کے ساتھ قیمت کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ اور وزن کے ساتھ ملایا جائے گا۔ اوپر کی مثال میں ایک سو درہم ہے اور نو مثقال سونا ہے تو وزن کے اعتبار سے سونا آدھے نصاب سے کم ہے چاہے اس کی قیمت ایک سو در ہم ہو اس لئے سونا چاندی ملا کر نصاب پورا نہیں ہوا اس لئے زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ اجزاء اور وزن کے اعتبار سے دونوں کو ملا کر بھی نصاب پورا نہیں ہوا ، ہاں! اگر سونا دس مثقال ہوتا تو آدھا نصاب اس کا ہوا اور آدھا نصاب چاندی کا ایک سو درہم ہے۔
And the value of trade goods is added to gold and silver, and likewise gold is added to silver by value until the nisab is completed according to Abu Hanifa. (5) And they (the two) said: gold is not added to silver by value; it is added by parts. And the trade goods will also be valued and added to gold or silver cash so that if nisab is completed, zakat will be obligatory. (5) The Sahibayn say that gold is not added to silver by value; it will be added by weight. In the above example, there are 100 dirhams and 9 mithqal of gold; according to weight, the gold is less than half nisab, even if its value is 100 dirhams. Therefore, gold and silver combined do not complete nisab, so zakat is not obligatory. Because by parts and weight, when combined, nisab is not completed. However, if the gold were 10 mithqal, then half nisab would be achieved, and the other half nisab would be 100 dirhams of silver.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on how to combine different types of wealth for nisab. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that when a person owns both gold and silver, and neither individually reaches nisab, they can be combined by value. For example, 100 dirhams (half nisab of silver) and 9 mithqal of gold (value 100 dirhams) combined make 200 dirhams value, completing nisab. Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree: they require combination by weight (ajza'), not value. So if gold is 9 mithqal (less than half nisab of 20 mithqal), even if its value equals 100 dirhams, it does not complete nisab because the weight is deficient. Only if gold reaches 10 mithqal (half nisab by weight) would it combine with 100 dirhams. The practical consequence is that according to Abu Hanifa, zakat is due; according to the Sahibayn, it is not. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is often Abu Hanifa's view, but the text presents both.

Key Terms
ضم بالقيمة (damm bil-qimah): Combining by value; treating the monetary value of gold and silver as equivalent for completing nisab.
ضم بالاجزاء (damm bil-ajza'): Combining by parts/weight; considering the actual weight of gold and silver for nisab calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Yes, because the Sahibayn also combine by value
D) No, because the Sahibayn require both types to be in the same metal

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa allows combining gold and silver by value to complete zakat nisab; the Sahibayn require combination by weight—a difference that changes the zakat obligation in many common scenarios.

Consolidating Gold, Silver, and Trade Goods for Zakat Nisab: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on consolidation by value vs. weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on consolidation of gold, silver, and trade goods for zakat nisab, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa consolidates by value; Sahibayn consolidate by weight — the same assets may or may not trigger zakat.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person has incomplete nisabs of gold and silver (and trade goods), can the values be combined to complete the nisab? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that they can, by valuing the assets. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), disagree: they require consolidation by actual weight (parts). Understanding this difference is essential for correct zakat calculation in cases of mixed wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed element
The act is zakat payment when nisab is reached. The disputed element is how gold, silver, and trade goods are consolidated to reach nisab.
Nisab is the minimum threshold for zakat liability.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa consolidates by value (qima). If the total value of gold, silver, and trade goods reaches the nisab, zakat becomes wajib, even if the weight of each is below the nisab.
Trade goods are valued and added to either gold or silver.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consolidate only by weight (ajza). The value is irrelevant; the actual weight of gold and silver must reach the nisab when combined.
They do not add gold to silver by value, only by weight.
4
Apply to an example
A person has 100 dirhams (silver) and 9 mithqals of gold worth 100 dirhams. Under Abu Hanifa, total value = 200 dirhams (nisab) → zakat due. Under Sahibayn, 100 dirhams + 9 mithqals by weight does not reach nisab (silver half nisab, gold less than half nisab) → no zakat.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in zakat obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مہینہ شروع ہوگا۔ شروع میں نصاب ہونا زکوۃ کے انعقاد کے لئے ہے اور اخیر میں نصاب ہونا زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے ہے، اور درمیان میں کمی بیشی ہوتی رہتی ہے اس لئے اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا۔

[۵۰۰] (۴) سامان تجارت کی قیمت سونے کی طرف اور چاندی کی طرف ملائی جائے گی، ایسے ہی سونے کو چاندی کی طرف قیمت کے ساتھ ملایا جائے گا تا کہ نصاب پورا ہو جائے ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک۔

سونے کو چاندی کے ساتھ ملانے کے دو طریقے ہیں تا کہ نصاب مکمل ہو جائے۔ ایک طریقہ یہ ہے کہ سونے کی قیمت لگا کر یا چاندی کی قیمت لگا کر سونے کے ساتھ ملایا جائے۔ اور دوسری شکل یہ ہے کہ وزن کے اعتبار سے ملایا جائے ۔ مثلا ایک آدمی کے پاس ایک سو درہم ہے اور نو مثقال سونا ہے تو درہم کا نصاب آدھا ہے لیکن سونے کا نصاب آدھا یعنی دس مثقال سے ایک مثقال کم ہے لیکن نو مثقال کی قیمت ایک سو درہم دے رہا ہے تو قیمت کے اعتبار سے ایک سو درہم اور نو مثقال سونے کی قیمت ایک سو درہم دونوں ملا کر دو سو درہم ہو جاتے ہیں اور نصاب پورا ہو جاتا ہے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قیمت کے اعتبار سے ملایا جائے گا اور زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ چاہے وزن کے اعتبار سے نصاب پورا نہ ہوتا ہو۔

و سامان تجارت کی بھی قیمت لگائی جائے گی اور اس کو سونے یا نقد چاندی کے ساتھ ملا کر نصاب پورا ہو جائے تو زکوۃ واجب کریں گے۔

[۵۰۱] (۵) صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ سونے کو چاندی کے ساتھ قیمت کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ اور وزن کے ساتھ ملایا جائے گا۔ اوپر کی مثال میں ایک سو درہم ہے اور نو مثقال سونا ہے تو وزن کے اعتبار سے سونا آدھے نصاب سے کم ہے چاہے اس کی قیمت ایک سو در ہم ہو اس لئے سونا چاندی ملا کر نصاب پورا نہیں ہوا اس لئے زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ اجزاء اور وزن کے اعتبار سے دونوں کو ملا کر بھی نصاب پورا نہیں ہوا ، ہاں! اگر سونا دس مثقال ہوتا تو آدھا نصاب اس کا ہوا اور آدھا نصاب چاندی کا ایک سو درہم ہے۔

الاجزاء : جزء کی جمع ہے، جز کے اعتبار سے، جس کا میں نے ترجمہ کیا ہے وزن کے اعتبار سے۔
(4) The value of trade goods is added to gold and silver, and likewise gold is added to silver by value until the nisab is completed according to Abu Hanifa. (5) They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Gold is not added to silver by value, but is added by parts (weight).

Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether gold and silver (and trade goods) are consolidated by value or by weight when determining zakat nisab. The passage presents the matn stating Abu Hanifa's position (consolidation by value) and the Sahibayn's position (consolidation by weight). The Urdu commentary explains that when one has incomplete nisab of gold and silver, Abu Hanifa values them and adds the values; if the total reaches nisab, zakat is due. The Sahibayn only add by weight (i.e., actual quantities), so if the weight of gold and silver together does not meet nisab, even if the value does, no zakat. The example given: 100 dirhams (half nisab of silver) and 9 mithqals of gold (less than half nisab of gold). Under Abu Hanifa, the value of 9 mithqals might be 100 dirhams, so total value 200 dirhams -> nisab -> zakat. Under Sahibayn, 9 mithqals + 100 dirhams by weight is not nisab, so no zakat. Trade goods are also valued and added.

Key Terms
ضم (ḍamm): Consolidation or adding together of different categories of wealth (e.g., gold, silver, trade goods) to complete nisab.
عروض (ʿurūḍ): Trade goods (merchandise) that are bought and sold for profit.
قيمة (qīma): Monetary value, used to assess the worth of gold, silver, or trade goods for nisab calculation.
اجزاء (ajzāʾ): Parts or weight, as opposed to value. Here it means the actual weight of gold and silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone has 100 dirhams of silver and 9 mithqals of gold (value 100 dirhams), how is the nisab calculated?
A) They are not combined; each is considered separately.
B) They are combined by weight, so total is not nisab.
C) They are combined by value, total 200 dirhams, nisab is complete.
D) Only the silver is considered because gold is not assessed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school consolidates gold, silver, and trade goods by value for zakat nisab, following Abu Hanifa's view.

Zakat on Crops: No Minimum Quantity Required (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn)
Ruling on 'ushr with intra-Hanafi dispute and proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on 'ushr, identify the proof from the hadith, and explain why Abu Hanifa disagrees with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
On all cultivated produce, 'ushr is wajib, no nisab or durability required, except insignificant growth.

This lesson explores a key difference within the Hanafi school regarding zakat on crops. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that 'ushr (one-tenth) is obligatory on all produce of the earth, regardless of quantity or storability, based on the general command of the Prophet (peace be upon him). His two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), restrict 'ushr to produce that is storable and reaches the nisab of five wasq. We will examine the proofs and the intra-madhhab tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm (level of obligation)?
The act is paying 'ushr on crops; the hukm is wajib according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Locate the dalil
What hadith does Abu Hanifa cite, and how does he interpret it?
The hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'On what is watered by rain and rivers, 'ushr; on what is irrigated by animal power, half 'ushr.'
3
Understand the exception
What items are excluded from 'ushr and why?
Excluded: firewood, reeds, grass — items that are not intentionally cultivated and are negligible.
4
Compare with Sahibayn
How do Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict the obligation? What is their proof?
They require 5 wasq and durability; their proof includes a hadith from Mu'adh (mentioned but not quoted) and qiyas on gold/silver.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which view is mufta bihi and why?
Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi because his dalil is considered stronger and more general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۰۲](۱) قال ابو حنيفة رحمه الله فى قليل ما اخرجته الارض وكثيره العشر واجب سواء سقى سيحا او سقته السماء الا الحطب والقصب والحشيش [۵۰۳] (۲) وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد العشر لا يجب الا فى ثمر يبقى اذا بلغ خمسة اوسق.

باب زكوة الزروع والثمار کے

ی نے غلہ اور پھل میں زکوۃ ہے۔ اس کی دلیل اور مقدار کی تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔

[۵۰۲](۱) امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا، زمیں تھوڑ اغلہ نکالے یا زیادہ اس میں عشر واجب ہے چاہے پانی سے سیراب کی گئی ہو یا اس کو آسمان نے سیراب کیا ہو، مگر جلانے کی لکڑی اور بانس اور گھاس۔

زمین سے جتنے غلے یا پھل نکلتے ہیں حنفیہ کے نزدیک اس تمام میں عشر واجب ہے۔ چاہے اس کی مقدار پانچ وسق پہنچے یا نہ پہنچے۔ اور چاہے وہ سال بھر تک رہ سکتا ہو یا نہ رہ سکتا ہو۔ البتہ ایسی چیز جو قابل التفات نہیں سمجھی جاتی اور اس کی کوئی حیثیت نہیں ہے اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ جیسے جلانے کی لکڑی ، نرکٹ اور گھاس کہ ان چیزوں کی کوئی حیثیت نہیں ہے اور نہ لوگ ان کو قصد و ارادہ کر کے ہوتے ہوں۔ بلکہ خودرو ہیں۔ اور اگر یہ چیزیں باضابطہ بوئیں اور قابل حیثیت ہوتو پھر اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔

عن سالم بن عبد الله بن ابيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال فيما سقت السماء والعيون او كان عشراوالعشر وما سقى بالنضح نصف العشر (بخاری شریف، باب العشر فيما يسقى من ماء السماء والماء الجارى ص ۲۰۱ نمبر ۱۳۸۳، مسلم شریف، کتاب الزركوة ص۳۱۶ نمبر ۹۸۱، ابو داؤد شریف، باب صدقته الزرع ص ۲۳۲ نمبر ۱۵۹۶) اس حدیث میں کوئی قید نہیں ہے نہ پانچ وسق کی قید ہے اور نہ سال بھر رہنے کی قید ہے، بلکہ مطلق یہ ہے کہ آسمان کی بارش اور نہروں کی سیرابی سے جو کچھ پیدا ہوا ہو اس میں عشر ہے (۲) کتب عمر بن عبد العزيز ان يوخذ مما انبتت الارض من قليل او كثير العشر (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الخضر ج رابع ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۷۱۹۶، مصنف ابن ابی شیبته ۳۰ کل شی و اخرجت الارض زکوۃ، ج ثانی، ص ۳۷۱ نمبر ۱۰۰۲۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جو کچھ بھی زمین پیدا کرے اس میں عشر ہے۔

سیما : بارش سے۔ الحطب : جلانے کی لکڑی۔ القصب : بانس نرکٹ ۔ الحشيش : گھاس۔

[۵۰۳] (۲) صاحبین نے فرمایا عشر واجب نہیں ہے مگر پھل میں جو باقی رہتا ہو جب کہ پانچ وسق پہنچ جائے۔

سبزی وغیرہ جو زیادہ دیر تک باقی نہ رہتے ہوں ان میں صاحبین کے نزدیک عشر نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح جب تک کہ غلے کی مقدار پانچ وسق نہ ہو جائے تو اس میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن معاذ انه كتب الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يسأله عن الخضروات و...
(1) Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: On little or much that the earth produces, the 'ushr is obligatory, whether irrigated by flowing water or by rain, except firewood, reeds, and grass. (2) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The 'ushr is not obligatory except on fruit that lasts (is stored) when it reaches five wasq.

[Urdu commentary and hadith omitted for brevity.]
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on zakat on crops and fruits. It presents a ruling with proof. Imam Abu Hanifa states that 'ushr (one-tenth) is wajib on all produce of the earth, regardless of quantity or irrigation method, with exceptions for firewood, reeds, and grass. The Sahibayn restrict 'ushr to stored produce (like grains and dates) that reaches the nisab of 5 wasq (approx. 653 kg). The Urdu commentary supports Abu Hanifa's position with a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that does not mention a minimum, and an athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. The Sahibayn rely on another hadith (from Mu'adh) that implies a minimum, though not fully quoted here. This is a well-known difference: Abu Hanifa considers 'ushr on all edible produce; the majority of other schools (including Shafi'i and Maliki) require nisab of 5 wasq and that the produce be storable. The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's view as mufta bihi, but with the condition that the produce is intended for food and is cultivated by humans.

Key Terms
عشر (ʿushr): One-tenth of agricultural produce due as zakat.
وسق (wasq): A measure of volume for grains, equivalent to approximately 60 sa' (approx. 130.5 kg). The nisab of 5 wasq is about 653 kg.
سيح (sīḥ): Flowing water (canal, river) used for irrigation.
ثمر يبقى (thamar yabqā): Fruit that lasts or is storable, such as dates, grapes, grains; as opposed to fresh vegetables that spoil quickly.

Key Terms from Source Passage
