A) Wheat from a rain-fed field
B) Cucumbers from a canal-irrigated farm
C) Firewood collected from a forest
D) Dates from a rain-fed tree

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, 'ushr is wajib on all cultivated produce, little or much, based on the general hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Sahibayn: 'Ushr Requires Nisab and Storability
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions for 'ushr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required by the Sahibayn for 'ushr to be wajib, identify the two hadiths they cite as evidence, and distinguish this position from Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
Sahibayn restrict 'ushr to storable crops reaching 5 wasq; for them, perishables and small amounts are exempt.

This passage presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two leading disciples of Abu Hanifa, who differ from their teacher on the conditions for 'ushr (zakat on crops). They impose two requirements: the crop must be storable (thamara baqiya) and must reach the nisab of 5 wasq. Their evidence comes from specific hadiths that limit zakat obligations. Understanding this intra-Hanafi dispute is crucial because later Hanafi practice often adopted the nisab condition for practical ease, and it reflects the school's internal reasoning diversity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Read the opening sentence: 'لا يجب العشر الا فيما له ثمرة باقية اذا بلغت خمسة اوسق'. The Sahibayn state that 'ushr is not wajib except for produce that is storable and reaches 5 wasq.
Note the negative limitation: 'not wajib except'.
2
Extract the two conditions
Condition 1: 'له ثمرة باقية' – the produce must have a lasting, storable fruit. Condition 2: 'بلغت خمسة اوسق' – it must reach the volume of 5 wasq.
Vegetables and perishables fail condition 1; small quantities fail condition 2.
3
Analyze the first proof
The text cites the hadith of Mu'adh (رضي الله عنه) where the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'ليس فيها شيء' (there is nothing on vegetables). This excludes perishable items from 'ushr.
This hadith is from Tirmidhi and is used to prove that vegetables are not subject to 'ushr.
4
Analyze the second proof
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (رضي الله عنه) states: 'ليس فيما اقل من خمسة اوسق صدقة' (no zakat on less than 5 wasq). This sets a minimum threshold for any zakat, including 'ushr.
This hadith is in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud. It establishes the nisab.
5
Contrast with Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that 'ushr is wajib on all produce regardless of quantity or storability, based on a general hadith: 'whatever the sky waters, 'ushr is due'. The dispute is thus about the interpretation of these hadiths.
The Sahibayn's view aligns with the majority of other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) that require nisab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله لا يجب العشر الا فيما له ثمرة باقية اذا بلغت خمسة اوسق
صاحبین نے فرمایا عشر واجب نہیں ہے مگر پھل میں جو باقی رہتا ہو جب کہ پانچ وسق پہنچ جائے۔
سبزی وغیرہ جو زیادہ دیر تک باقی نہ رہتے ہوں ان میں صاحبین کے نزدیک عشر نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح جب تک کہ غلے کی مقدار پانچ وسق نہ ہو جائے تو اس میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن معاذ انه كتب الى النبي الا الله يسأله عن الخضروات و هي البقول فقال ليس فيها شيء (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی زکوۃ الخضروات ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۶۳۸ سفن سليم من الملحقي ، باب الصدقة فيما يزرعه الآدمیون ج رابع ص ۲۱۶، نمبر ۷۴۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبزیوں میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ اور پانچ وثق ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي سعيد الخدري عن النبی الا الله قال ليس فيما اقل من خمسة اوسق صدقة (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب لیس فیما دون خمسته اوسق صدقته ص ۲۰۱ نمبر ۱۴۸۴ر مسل شریف، باب الزکوۃ ص ۳۱۶ نمبر ۹۷۹ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب ماتجب فيه الزكوۃ ص ۲۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۵۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پانچ وسق سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ یہ حدیث کئی مرتبہ پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: 'Ushr is not wajib except for that which has a lasting fruit when it reaches five wasq. [Urdu commentary:] The Sahibayn said: 'Ushr is not wajib except for fruit that remains (storable) when it reaches five wasq. Vegetables and similar items that do not last long are not subject to 'ushr in their view. Similarly, until the grain quantity reaches five wasq, there is no 'ushr. Their proof is the hadith: Mu'adh wrote to the Prophet (peace be upon him) asking about vegetables, and he said, 'There is nothing (zakat) on them.' [Tirmidhi] This hadith indicates that vegetables have no 'ushr. And the proof for five wasq is the hadith: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said, 'There is no zakat on less than five wasq.' [Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud] This hadith indicates that less than five wasq has no zakat. This hadith has passed several times before.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on zakat of crops, which constitutes an intra-Hanafi dispute. They require two conditions for 'ushr to be wajib: (1) the produce must be storable (i.e., can be kept for a period, not perishable like vegetables), and (2) it must reach the nisab of five wasq. Vegetables and perishable items are exempt even if they reach five wasq. The proof they offer is twofold: First, the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet said there is no zakat on vegetables (al-buqul). Second, the well-known hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that no zakat is due on less than five wasq. This latter hadith is used to establish the nisab threshold. The commentator notes that this hadith has appeared previously, indicating its importance. This position directly opposes Abu Hanifa's view that no nisab is required. Students should note that although the Sahibayn differ from Abu Hanifa, their view is also part of the Hanafi school and has weight, especially in later fatwa practice where the nisab condition is often adopted for practical ease.

Key Terms
ثمرة باقية (thamaratun baqiyah): Storable fruit or produce that can be kept for a period without spoiling, as opposed to perishable vegetables.
وسق (wasq): A measure of volume equal to 60 sa', used as the nisab threshold for crops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The crop must be storable and reach 5 wasq
C) The crop must be irrigated by rain and exceed 5 wasq
D) The crop must be a grain and harvested by the owner

Key Takeaway
Sahibayn require 'ushr only on storable crops reaching 5 wasq; their evidence comes from specific hadiths that limit zakat obligations.

Definition of Wasq: Sixty Sa'
Defining the wasq as 60 sa' by the Prophet's sa'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of one wasq as 60 Prophet's sa', and explain why the weight equivalent varies by grain type.

Core Idea
The wasq is a fixed volume of 60 sa'; the weight depends on the grain.

Zakat on agricultural produce requires knowing the nisab, which is five wasq. But what exactly is a wasq? This lesson defines the wasq as a volumetric measure of 60 sa' by the Prophet's standard. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly calculating zakat obligations for different crops.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition
The passage states that a wasq equals 60 sa' by the sa' of the Prophet (peace be upon him). This is the foundational definition.
2
Understand the sa' as a volumetric measure
The sa' is a volume, historically measured with a vessel. Modern weight equivalents are approximate because grains differ in density.
Barley, wheat, and mung beans have different weights per sa'.
3
Convert wasq to sa' and to weight
Five wasq (nisab) equals 300 sa'. Using the given conversions, estimate the weight threshold for zakat. For wheat, approximately 1061.4 kg.
Keep in mind the approximations.
4
Memorize the evidence (athar)
The passage cites Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The wasq is sixty sa'.' This is a foundational evidence from the Companions.
This athar is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) والوسق ستون صاعا بصاع النبي عليه السلام.
(۵۰۴) (۳) وسق ساتھ ضاع ہے حضور کے ضاع ہے۔ ایک وسق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوا تو پانچ وسق کے تین سو (300) صاع ہوئے۔ صاع سے وزن کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ ایک برتن میں جو یا گیہوں یا ماش ڈال دیں جو ایک صاع کی مقدار ہو اس کو صاع کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے آج کل دودھ وغیرہ برتن میں ناپ کر دیتے ہیں۔ لیکن اب اس زمانے میں یہ ساری چیزیں کیلو سے وزن کرنے لگے ہیں۔ چونکہ گیہوں، جو اور ماش مختلف قسم کے بھاری ہوتے ہیں اس لئے وزن کے اعتبار سے ہر غلہ الگ الگ وزن کا ہوگا۔ تاہم ایک صاع جو 3.538 کیلو کا ہوتا ہے۔ اور گیہوں 4.498 کیلو اور ماش 4.9726 کیلو ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی چار کیلونو سو بہتر گرام ہوتا ہے۔ اس اعتبار سے تین سو صاع جو 1061.40 کیلو ہو گا ۔ یعنی دس کو نیٹل ، اکسٹھ کیلو اور چالیس گرام ہوگا۔ اور تمام کا لیٹر 2.94 ہوتا ہے۔ عن ابي سعيد قال الوسق ستون صاعا (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۳۸ فی الوسق کم ھو ؟ ، ج خانی ج۳۷۰ نمبر ۱۰۰۱۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ وسق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوتا ہے۔
(3) And the wasq is sixty sa' by the sa' of the Prophet (peace be upon him). [Urdu commentary:] (504)(3) A wasq is sixty sa' of the Prophet's sa'. So one wasq is 60 sa', thus five wasq is 300 sa'. The method of measuring a sa' is to fill a vessel with barley, wheat, or mung beans to the volume of one sa'; that is called a sa'. Just as today milk etc. is measured by vessel. But nowadays these things are weighed by kilogram. Since wheat, barley, and mung beans vary in density, the weight of each grain is different. However, one sa' of barley is about 3.538 kg, wheat 4.498 kg, and mung beans 4.9726 kg (i.e., 4 kg 972 grams). So 300 sa' would be 1061.40 kg, i.e., 10 quintals, 61 kg, 40 grams. And one sa' in liters is 2.94 liters. From Abu Sa'id: 'The wasq is sixty sa'' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10011). This effect shows that a wasq is sixty sa'.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of a key term in zakat al-zuru': the wasq. It states authoritatively that one wasq equals sixty sa' measured by the sa' of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary in Urdu clarifies that five wasq (the nisab according to Sahibayn) thus equals 300 sa'. The passage then explains how to conceptualize a sa': it is a volumetric measure of the Prophet's time, traditionally filled with grains like barley, wheat, or mung beans. Since grains have different densities, the weight equivalent varies; the passage provides approximate modern metric conversions: approximately 3.5 kg for barley, 4.5 kg for wheat, and 5 kg for mung beans per sa'. Consequently, five wasq in wheat is about 1061.4 kg. The passage also cites the athar of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the wasq is sixty sa', confirming the definition. For students, this is a memorization anchor: 1 wasq = 60 sa', and knowing the sa' in modern measures is crucial for practical application of zakat on crops.

Key Terms
الوسق (al-wasq): A unit of volume equal to 60 sa', used as the nisab for crops in zakat.
الصاع (al-sa'): A volumetric measure used by the Prophet; approximately 2.94 liters or 3.5-5 kg depending on grain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Quran
B) Hadith of the Prophet
C) Athar of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri
D) Consensus

Key Takeaway
A wasq is a fixed volume of 60 Prophet's sa'; the weight equivalent varies by grain density.

The Nisab of Ushr on Produce: Five Awsuq and the Definition of Sa'
Explains the obligation, nisab, and definitions for 'ushr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab for 'ushr, define a wasq and a sa', and explain the intra-Hanafi reconciliation on the weight of the sa'.

Core Idea
Ushr is due only on lasting produce reaching five awsuq; the sa' is a fixed volume despite different weight definitions.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on the nisab for 'ushr (the 10% tithe on agricultural produce). You will learn the definition of the wasq and sa', the evidence from hadith, and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the weight of the sa'—a dispute that is reconciled through the common unit of ustars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The passage states 'ushr is fard (obligatory) only on produce that has a lasting fruit (thamar baqiyah) when it reaches five awsuq.
'Ushr is a type of zakat on agricultural produce.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud).
This hadith establishes the minimum threshold (nisab) for 'ushr.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the negation of obligation ('la sadaqata') indicates that zakat/'ushr is not due below this amount. The phrase 'five awsuq' sets the specific nisab.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice; it is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
4
Define the measures: wasq and sa'
A wasq is defined as 60 sa' by the Prophet's sa'. Thus, 5 awsuq = 300 sa'. The sa' is a volume measure, not a weight, but the passage provides modern equivalents for convenience.
The sa' for 'ushr is the same sa' used for sadaqat al-fitr.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sa' weight
Imam Abu Hanifa said 1 sa' = 8 Iraqi ratls (20 ustars each) = 160 ustars. The Sahibayn said 1 sa' = 5.33 Madani ratls (30 ustars each) = 160 ustars. Both agree on 160 ustars, so there is no practical difference.
This reconciliation is cited from al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Radd al-Muhtar.

يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله لا يجب العشر الا فيما له ثمرة باقية اذا بلغت خمسة اوسق [۵۰۴](۳) والوسق ستون صاعا بصاع النبي عليه السلام.
هي البقول فقال ليس فيها شيء (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی زکوۃ الخضروات ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۶۳۸ سفن سليم من الملحقي ، باب الصدقة فيما يزرعه الآدمیون ج رابع ص ۲۱۶، نمبر ۷۴۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبزیوں میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ اور پانچ وثق ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي سعيد الخدري عن النبی الا الله قال ليس فيما اقل من خمسة اوسق صدقة (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب لیس فیما دون خمسته اوسق صدقته ص ۲۰۱ نمبر ۱۴۸۴ر مسل شریف، باب الزکوۃ ص ۳۱۶ نمبر ۹۷۹ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب ماتجب فيه الزکوۃ ص ۲۲۴ نمبر ۱۵۵۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پانچ وسق سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ یہ حدیث کئی مرتبہ پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ (۵۰۴) (۳) وسق ساتھ ضاع ہے حضور کے ضاع ہے۔ ایک وسق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوا تو پانچ وسق کے تین سو (300) صاع ہوئے۔ صاع سے وزن کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ ایک برتن میں جو یا گیہوں یا ماش ڈال دیں جو ایک صاع کی مقدار ہو اس کو صاع کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے آج کل دودھ وغیرہ برتن میں ناپ کر دیتے ہیں۔ لیکن اب اس زمانے میں یہ ساری چیزیں کیلو سے وزن کرنے لگے ہیں۔ چونکہ گیہوں، جو اور ماش مختلف قسم کے بھاری ہوتے ہیں اس لئے وزن کے اعتبار سے ہر غلہ الگ الگ وزن کا ہوگا۔ تاہم ایک صاع جو 3.538 کیلو کا ہوتا ہے۔ اور گیہوں 4.498 کیلو اور ماش 4.9726 کیلو ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی چار کیلونو سو بہتر گرام ہوتا ہے۔ اس اعتبار سے تین سو صاع جو 1061.40 کیلو ہو گا ۔ یعنی دس کو نیٹل ، اکسٹھ کیلو اور چالیس گرام ہوگا۔ اور تمام کا لیٹر 2.94 ہوتا ہے۔ عن ابي سعيد قال الوسق ستون صاعا (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۳۸ فی الوسق کم ھو ؟ ، ج خانی ج۳۷۰ نمبر ۱۰۰۱۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ وسق ساٹھ صاع کا ہوتا ہے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک صاع 8 رطل کا ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن یہ رطل چھوٹا ہے، یہ 20 استار کا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک 5.33 یعنی پانچ طل اور ایک تہائی رطل کا ایک صاع ہوتا ہے، لیکن یہ رطل بڑا ہے یعنی 30 استار کا ایک رطل ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کو استار سے ضرب دیں تو حاصل 160 استار ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے دونوں رطلوں کے صا میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔
در مختار میں عبارت یوں ہے۔ فقال الطرفان : ثمانية ارطال بالعراقي وقال الثاني خمسة ارطال وثلث، وقيل لاخلاف لان الثاني قدره برطل المدينة، لانه ثلاثون استار و العراقي عشرون واذا قابلت ثمانية بالعراقي بخمسة وثلث بالمديني وجدتهما سواء (ردالمحتار على الدر المختار، مطلب في تحرير الصارع والمد والمن والرطل، ج ثالچ میں ۳۷۳) اس عبارت میں ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا عراقی رطل بیس استار کا ہے اور صاحبین کا دینی رطل تمیں استار کا ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کا حاصل ایک قسم کا صاع ہے۔ و رطل عراقی 442.25 گرام اور رطل مدنی 663.41 گرام کا ہوتا ہے۔ ساتھ صاع کا ایک وسق ہوتا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک پانچ وسق میں عشر یعنی دسواں حصہ لازم ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ پانچ وسق میں 30 صاع اور بیسواں حصہ ہو تو 15 صاع لازم ہوگا۔
احسن الفتاوی میں ہے کہ ایک صاع 3.538 کیلو اور آدھا صاع 1.769 کیلو ہوگا یعنی ایک کیلو اور 769 گرام ہوگا۔ یہی آدھا صاع صدقۃ الفطر میں لازم ہوتا ہے۔ اس کو لیسٹر سے نا پیں تو 2.94 لیٹر ہو گا۔
Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them): 'Ushr is not obligatory except on produce that has lasting fruit when it reaches five awsuq. And the wasq is sixty sa' by the sa' of the Prophet, peace be upon him. As for vegetables, he said: There is nothing on them. (Hadith from Tirmidhi) From this hadith, it is known that there is no 'ushr on vegetables. And the proof for five awsuq is the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: There is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) From this hadith, it is known that there is no zakat on less than five awsuq. This hadith has passed many times before. (504) (3) A wasq is with a sa' (measure) of the Prophet (peace be upon him). One wasq equals sixty sa', so five wasq equal three hundred sa'. The method of weight with sa' is: a vessel in which barley, wheat, or mung beans are placed equal to a sa' is called a sa'. As today milk etc. is given in vessels. But nowadays all these things are weighed in kilograms. Since wheat, barley, and mung beans are of different weights, each grain will have a different weight. However, one sa' is 3.538 kg, wheat 4.498 kg, and mung 4.9726 kg, i.e. four kilograms nine hundred seventy-two grams. Accordingly, three hundred sa' would be 1061.40 kg, i.e. ten quintals, sixty-one kilograms, forty grams. And the liter of all is 2.94. From Abu Sa'id: al-wasq sittun sa'an (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba). From this effect it is known that a wasq is sixty sa'.
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one sa' is 8 ratls. But this ratl is small, it is 20 ustars. According to the Sahibayn, one sa' is 5.33 ratls (five and one-third ratls), but this ratl is large, i.e. one ratl is 30 ustars. So when multiplied by ustars, the product is 160 ustars. Therefore there is no difference between the sa' of the two ratls.
In al-Durr al-Mukhtar the wording is: 'So the two parties said: eight Iraqi ratls. And the other said: five and one-third ratls. And it is said there is no dispute because the latter estimated it by the Madani ratl, for it is thirty ustars, while the Iraqi is twenty. When you compare eight by Iraqi with five and one-third by Madani, you find them equal.' (Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar, section on tahreef of sa', mud, mann, ratl). In this wording, Imam Abu Hanifa's Iraqi ratl is twenty ustars and the Sahibayn's Madani ratl is thirty ustars. So the product of both is one type of sa'. And the Iraqi ratl is 442.25 grams and the Madani ratl is 663.41 grams. A wasq consists of sixty sa'. And according to the Sahibayn, one-tenth (tithe) is obligatory on five awsuq. The result is that on five awsuq, 30 sa' and one-twentieth portion, so 15 sa' become obligatory.
In Ahsan al-Fatawa, one sa' is 3.538 kg and half a sa' is 1.769 kg, i.e. one kilogram and 769 grams. This half sa' is obligatory in sadaqat al-fitr. If measured in liters, it is 2.94 liters.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states the Hanafi position (from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that 'ushr (tithe) is obligatory only on produce that has a lasting fruit (thamar baqiyah) and reaches the nisab of five awsuq. Vegetables like greens are excluded, as per the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal where the Prophet said 'there is nothing on them.' The nisab of five awsuq is proven by the famous hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq.' A wasq is defined as 60 sa' by the sa' of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The sa' is a volume measure, not a weight, but the commentator provides modern weight equivalents for convenience: one sa' of barley is about 3.538 kg, wheat 4.498 kg, and mung beans 4.9726 kg. The passage then addresses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the weight of a sa'. Imam Abu Hanifa said one sa' equals 8 Iraqi ratls, each of 20 ustars (total 160 ustars). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said one sa' equals 5.33 Madani ratls, each of 30 ustars (also 160 ustars). Thus, when converted to the common unit of ustars, both positions are identical. The author cites al-Durr al-Mukhtar to confirm no real difference. The modern equivalent of one sa' is about 3.538 kg based on Ahsan al-Fatawa, which is used for sadaqat al-fitr. Note that the sa' for 'ushr is the same. The passage also notes that according to the Sahibayn, the specific amount of 'ushr on five awsuq is 30 sa' and a twentieth portion (since five awsuq = 300 sa', one-tenth is 30 sa', plus a small adjustment?), but the text says '30 sa' one-twentieth' which may be a misstatement; the correct is one-tenth (10%) of the harvest, which on five awsuq (300 sa') would be 30 sa'.

Key Terms
عشر ('ushr): The mandatory 10% tithe on agricultural produce from land watered naturally (e.g., rain).
وسق (wasq): A volume measure equal to 60 sa' by the Prophet's sa'.
صاع (sa'): A volume measure for dry goods; the Prophet's sa' is the standard. The author describes it as a vessel of specific capacity.
رطل (ratl): A weight measure used to define the sa'. There are two types: Iraqi ratl (20 ustars) and Madani ratl (30 ustars).
استار (ustar): A small weight measure, used to reconcile the differences in ratl definitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the nisab for 'ushr on produce with lasting fruit?
A) 300 sa'
B) 5 awsuq, which equals 300 sa'
C) 160 ustars
D) 60 sa'

Key Takeaway
Ushr is only due on lasting produce reaching the nisab of 5 awsuq (300 sa'), and the sa' is a fixed volume measure reconciled to 160 ustars in weight.

Nisab for Zakat on Silver and Gold: Weight Conversions
Defines the classical weight standards for dirham and dinar and provides conversions to modern units.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab of silver and gold in classical units (dirhams/dinars) and convert them to modern metric weights.

Core Idea
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams (612.36 g); for gold, 20 dinars (87.48 g). These are distinct and independent thresholds.

This passage lays out the exact weights of the dirham and dinar as used in classical Hanafi fiqh for determining zakat obligations. Knowing these values is essential for correctly calculating whether one’s wealth of gold or silver meets the nisab. The text also provides conversions to Indian traditional units (rattī, māsha, tolah) and to grams, making it practical for modern application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the silver nisab
Find that the nisab for silver is 200 dirhams and note its weight equivalents in mithqāl, grams, and Indian units.
2
Identify the gold nisab
Find that the nisab for gold is 20 dinars (20 mithqāl) and note its weight equivalents.
3
Understand the conversion ratio
10 dirhams = 7 mithqāl, so 1 dirham = 0.70 mithqāl. Similarly, 1 dinar = 1 mithqāl.
4
Convert to grams
Using 1 dirham = 3.061 g, 200 dirhams = 612.36 g. Using 1 dinar = 4.374 g, 20 dinars = 87.48 g.
5
Recognize the legal consequence
Zakat becomes wajib when one possesses silver of at least 612.36 g or gold of at least 87.48 g (or equivalent value in mixed currency).
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
درہم کا وزن
ہندوستان میں سونا اور چاندی کے وزن کے لئے رقی، ماشہ اور تولہ چلتے تھے اس لئے ان کا حساب اس طرح ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت معاذ نے حضور کولکھا اور سبزیوں کے بارے میں پوچھا تو آپ نے فرمایا اس میں کچھ نہیں ہے ( ب ) آپ نے فرمایا پانچ وسق سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے

8 رتی = ایک ماشہ اور 12 ماشہ = ایک تولہ یعنی 96 رتی کا ایک تولہ ہوتا ہے۔ ایک درہم کا وزن ایک مثقال سے تھوڑا کم ہے۔ دس درہم ملا ئیں تو سات مثقال ہوتا ہے۔ اس کو وزن سبعہ کہتے ہیں۔ کلکو لیٹر میں اس طرح لکھتے ہیں (0.70 مثقال ) چونکہ 200 درہم میں زکوۃ لازم ہے اس لئے 200 کو 0.70 سے ضرب دیں تو 140 مثقال ہوتے ہیں۔ یعنی 140 مثقال چاندی ہو تو زکوۃ لازم ہوگی۔
ایک درہم کا وزن 25.20 رتی ہوتا ہے یا 3.15 ماشہ یا 0.26 تولہ یا 3.061 گرام ہوتا ہے۔ 200 درہم جو نصاب زکوۃ ہے اس کا وزن 5040 رتی ہوتا ہے یا 630 ماشہ یا 52.50 تولہ یا 612.36 گرام ہوتا ہے۔ قیراط کے اعتبار سے ایک درہم کا وزن 14 قیراط ہوتا ہے۔ اور 200 درہم کا وزن 2800 قیراط ہوگا۔
(دینار کا وزن)
ایک دینار ایک مثقال کا ہوتا ہے اس لئے ایک دینار 36 رتی کا ہوگا یا4.50 ماشہ یا 0.375 تولہ یا 4.374 گرام وزن کا ہوگا۔ 20 مثقال یعنی 20 دینار سونے میں زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے اس کا وزن 720 رتی یا 90 ماشہ یا 7.50 تولہ یا 87.48 گرام ہوگا۔ قیراط کے اعتبار سے ایک دینار کا وزن 20 قیراط ہوتا ہے۔ اور 20 دینار کا وزن 400 قیراط ہوتا ہے۔
1000 گرام کا ایک کیلوگرام ہوتا ہے۔
Weight of dirham: In India, rattī, māsha, and tolah were used for weighing gold and silver. So their calculation is as follows. Footnote (a): Mu'adh wrote to the Prophet (peace be upon him) about vegetables, and he said: There is nothing on them. (b) He said: There is no zakat on less than five awsuq.
8 rattī = 1 māsha, and 12 māsha = 1 tolah, i.e. 96 rattī make 1 tolah. The weight of one dirham is slightly less than one mithqāl. Ten dirhams equal seven mithqāls. This is called the weight of sab'ah. In calculators, it is written as (0.70 mithqāl). Since zakat is obligatory on 200 dirhams, multiply 200 by 0.70 to get 140 mithqāls. That is, when silver reaches 140 mithqāls, zakat becomes wajib.
One dirham weighs 25.20 rattī, or 3.15 māsha, or 0.26 tolah, or 3.061 grams. The 200 dirhams that are the nisab of zakat weigh 5040 rattī, or 630 māsha, or 52.50 tolah, or 612.36 grams. According to qirat, one dirham weighs 14 qirat. And 200 dirhams weigh 2800 qirat.
(Weight of dinar): One dinar is one mithqāl, so one dinar will be 36 rattī, or 4.50 māsha, or 0.375 tolah, or 4.374 grams. Zakat is wajib on 20 mithqāls i.e. 20 dinars of gold. Its weight is 720 rattī, or 90 māsha, or 7.50 tolah, or 87.48 grams. According to qirat, one dinar weighs 20 qirat. And 20 dinars weigh 400 qirat.
1000 grams make one kilogram.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage provides the legal definitions and weight conversions for the nisab of zakat on silver and gold. It is a definition_ruling lesson. The text explains that in the Indian subcontinent, traditional weights were rattī, māsha, and tolah. The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams, which is equivalent to 140 mithqāls (since 10 dirhams = 7 mithqāls at a rate of 0.70 mithqāl per dirham). In modern grams, 200 dirhams weigh 612.36 grams (using 3.061 g per dirham). For gold, the nisab is 20 dinars (20 mithqāls), which weighs 87.48 grams. The passage also gives equivalents in qirat (one dirham = 14 qirat, one dinar = 20 qirat). This is not a dispute passage; it is a straightforward statement of the established Hanafi positions (based on Zahir al-Riwayah) for zakat on currency. The author includes footnotes that repeat earlier hadiths about vegetables and the nisab of wasq, but the main body focuses on weights. The practical takeaway: zakat on silver becomes wajib when one possesses 612.36 grams of silver (or its value), and on gold when one possesses 87.48 grams of gold.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A silver coin; its weight is defined as 0.70 mithqāl (3.061 grams). 200 dirhams form the nisab for silver zakat.
دينار (dinar): A gold coin equal to one mithqāl (4.374 grams). 20 dinars form the nisab for gold zakat.
مثقال (mithqāl): A unit of weight for gold and silver; used as a standard. 10 dirhams = 7 mithqāls.
رتی (rattī): A small Indian weight; 8 rattī = 1 māsha, 96 rattī = 1 tolah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the weight of one dirham according to the passage?
A) 3.061 grams
B) 4.374 grams
C) 0.70 mithqāl
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams (612.36 g) and for gold is 20 dinars (87.48 g); these are the fixed thresholds for zakat obligation in the Hanafi school.

Zakat Nisab: Weights of Silver, Gold, Sa'a, and Wasq
Defining nisab weights for zakat calculations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab thresholds for silver, gold, and agricultural produce in both traditional and modern units, and explain the resolution of the sa'a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Precise nisab weights: 200 dirhams (612.36g) for silver, 20 dinars (87.48g) for gold, 5 wasqs (300 sa'as) for produce.

Zakat obligations depend on knowing the exact nisab thresholds. This lesson defines the weights and measures used by the Hanafi school for dirham, dinar, mithqal, sa'a, and wasq, including an intra-school difference on the sa'a that is resolved mathematically. The modern gram equivalents enable accurate calculation in today's context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic units
Familiarize yourself with the traditional weight units: rati, masha, tola, and their relationships (8 rati = 1 masha, 12 masha = 1 tola). Then learn the dirham (3.061g) and mithqal (4.374g) and the ratio of 10 dirhams = 7 mithqal.
This establishes the foundation for all nisab calculations.
2
Determine the nisab thresholds for silver and gold
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams (612.36g). For gold, it is 20 mithqal/dinars (87.48g). Note that 200 dirhams weigh 140 mithqal, but the nisab is counted by number of coins, not weight equivalence.
The nisab for silver and gold are separate: 200 dirhams of silver or 20 dinars of gold.
3
Explore the sa'a dispute and its resolution
Imam Abu Hanifa defines the sa'a as 8 Iraqi ratls (20 istars each), while the Sahibayn define it as 5.33 Medinan ratls (30 istars each). By converting to istars, both equal 160 istars, so there is no practical difference in volume.
The apparent disagreement arises from using different ratl standards, not from a difference in the actual sa'a.
4
Apply modern equivalents to the sa'a and wasq
The text gives two modern weights: according to Ahsan al-Fatawa, 1 sa'a = 3.538 kg; according to Dur al-Mukhtar, 1 sa'a = 1040 dirhams = 3.18344 kg. The author prefers the former for caution. One wasq = 60 sa'as; the nisab for 'ushr is 5 wasqs = 300 sa'as = 1061.40 kg (using Ahsan al-Fatawa).
For sadaqat al-fitr, half a sa' is due: 1.769 kg or 1.591 kg depending on the calculation followed.
5
Summarize the nisab for zakat and 'ushr
Compile all thresholds: silver nisab = 200 dirhams (612.36g); gold nisab = 20 mithqal (87.48g); agricultural nisab = 5 wasqs (300 sa'as). These are conditions for zakat obligation.
The text also presents a quick-reference table at the end.

امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک صاع 8 رطل کا ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن یہ رطل چھوٹا ہے، یہ 20 استار کا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک 5.33 یعنی پانچ طل اور ایک تہائی رطل کا ایک صاع ہوتا ہے، لیکن یہ رطل بڑا ہے یعنی 30 استار کا ایک رطل ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کو استار سے ضرب دیں تو حاصل 160 استار ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے دونوں رطلوں کے صا میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔

Book of Zakat. 8 rati = one masha and 12 masha = one tola, i.e., 96 rati make one tola. The weight of one dirham is slightly less than one mithqal. Ten dirhams added together become seven mithqal. This is called weight of seven. In calculator it is written as (0.70 mithqal). Since zakat is obligatory on 200 dirhams, multiply 200 by 0.70, resulting in 140 mithqal. That is, if one has 140 mithqal of silver, zakat becomes obligatory. The weight of one dirham is 25.20 rati, or 3.15 masha, or 0.26 tola, or 3.061 grams. The weight of 200 dirhams, which is the nisab of zakat, is 5040 rati, or 630 masha, or 52.50 tola, or 612.36 grams. In terms of qirat, the weight of one dirham is 14 qirat, and the weight of 200 dirhams will be 2800 qirat. (Weight of Dinar) One dinar equals one mithqal, therefore one dinar will be 36 rati, or 4.50 masha, or 0.375 tola, or weight of 4.374 grams. Zakat becomes obligatory on 20 mithqal, i.e., 20 dinars of gold. Its weight will be 720 rati, or 90 masha, or 7.50 tola, or 87.48 grams. In terms of qirat, the weight of one dinar is 20 qirat, and the weight of 20 dinars is 400 qirat. 1000 grams make one kilogram. (Weight of Sa'a) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one sa'a is 8 ratls. But this ratl is small; it is 20 uqiyas? no, 20 istars. And according to the Sahibayn, one sa'a is 5.33, i.e., five and one-third ratls, but this ratl is large, i.e., one ratl is 30 istars. Therefore, multiplying both by istars gives 160 istars. Hence there is no difference between the two ratls' sa'a. In Dur al-Mukhtar the text is: 'The two parties said: eight ratls by Iraqi (measure), and the second said five ratls and one-third, and it is said there is no difference because the second measured it by the Medinan ratl, for it is thirty istars, and the Iraqi is twenty. And when you compare eight by Iraqi to five and one-third by Medinian, you find them equal.' (Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Dur al-Mukhtar, chapter on clarification of sa'a, mudd, mann, and ratl, vol. 3, p. 373). This text says that Imam Abu Hanifa's Iraqi ratl is twenty istars, and the Sahibayn's Medinan ratl is thirty istars. Therefore, the result of both is one type of sa'a. And the Iraqi ratl is 442.25 grams, and the Medinan ratl is 663.41 grams. One wasq is sixty sa'as. And according to the Sahibayn, one-tenth (ushr) is obligatory on five wasqs. The result is that in five wasqs there are 300 sa'as, and one-twentieth would be 15 sa'as obligatory. In Ahsan al-Fatawa, it is stated that one sa'a is 3.538 kg, and half a sa'a is 1.769 kg, i.e., one kg and 769 grams. This half sa'a is obligatory in sadaqat al-fitr. If measured with a liter, it is 2.94 liters. One wasq, i.e., 60 sa'as, is 212.28 kg. And five wasqs, i.e., 300 sa'as, is 1061.40 kg, which is called ten quintals, sixty-one kg, and forty grams. (Ahsan al-Fatawa, vol. 4, p. 416). However, in Dur al-Mukhtar it is written that one sa'a is 1040 dirhams. The text is: 'The sa'a that is considered is that which contains one thousand and forty dirhams of mung beans and lentils.' (Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Dur al-Mukhtar, chapter of sadaqat al-fitr, vol. 3, p. 374). From this it is understood that the weight of one sa'a is one thousand forty dirhams. And the weight of one dirham is 3.061 grams. Therefore, the weight of one sa'a is 1040 x 3.061 = 3183.44 grams. And half a sa'a is 1.591 kg. That is, half a sa'a is one kg, five hundred and ninety-one grams. For caution, I have written the calculation of Ahsan al-Fatawa. And Allah knows best what is correct. Nisab and weights at a glance (Formula). How many equals how many: 8 rati = one masha; 12 masha = one tola; 11.664 grams = one tola; 0.218 grams 11 = one qirat; 4.374 grams = one mithqal; 442.25 grams = one ratl; 3538 grams = one sa'a; 1769 grams = half sa'a; 1000 grams = one kg; 3.061 grams = one dirham; 612.36 grams = nisab of silver; 4.374 grams = one dinar; 87.48 grams = nisab of gold.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari is a detailed exposition of the weights and measures used in Zakat calculations. The author begins by defining the basic weight units: rati, masha, and tola, establishing that 8 rati = 1 masha and 12 masha = 1 tola. He explains that a dirham weighs slightly less than a mithqal, with 10 dirhams equaling 7 mithqal (weight of seven). Since the nisab of silver is 200 dirhams, he multiplies to get 140 mithqal. Modern metric equivalents are provided: one dirham = 3.061 grams, so nisab of silver = 612.36 grams. Similarly, for gold: one dinar equals one mithqal (4.374 grams), and nisab of gold is 20 dinars = 87.48 grams. He then addresses the weight of the sa'a, noting a well-known ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Imam Abu Hanifa says one sa'a = 8 Iraqi ratls (20 istars each), while the Sahibayn say one sa'a = 5.33 Medinan ratls (30 istars each). The author demonstrates that both equal 160 istars, so there is no actual difference in the sa'a's volume. He cites Dur al-Mukhtar confirming this equivalence. The author then gives modern metric equivalents: Iraqi ratl = 442.25g, Medinan ratl = 663.41g. He explains the wasq: 1 wasq = 60 sa'as, and the nisab for 'ushr (tithe on agricultural produce) is 5 wasqs = 300 sa'as. He notes that according to the Sahibayn, one-tenth is due on 5 wasqs. He then presents the sa'a weight according to Ahsan al-Fatawa: 3.538 kg, and half sa'a (for sadaqat al-fitr) as 1.769 kg. There is also a different calculation from Dur al-Mukhtar where the sa'a is defined as 1040 dirhams (3.18344 kg). The author expresses a preference for the calculation of Ahsan al-Fatawa for caution. Finally, he provides a summary table of all the weights for easy reference. This passage is essential for correctly determining zakat obligations in both traditional and modern units.

Key Terms
درہم (dirham): A silver coin and unit of weight. One dirham = 3.061 grams in the text. The nisab for zakat is 200 dirhams (612.36 grams).
صاع (sa'a): A volume measure used for zakat al-fitr and agricultural 'ushr. According to the text, Imam Abu Hanifa: 8 Iraqi ratls; Sahibayn: 5.33 Medinan ratls; both equal 160 istars. Modern weight: 3.538 kg per Ahsan al-Fatawa or 3.18344 kg per Dur al-Mukhtar.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that makes zakat obligatory. Silver: 200 dirhams (612.36 g). Gold: 20 mithqal/dinars (87.48 g). Agricultural produce: 5 wasqs (300 sa'as).
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight for gold. 1 mithqal = 4.374 grams (36 rati) in the text. Used to define the gold dinar and the nisab of gold (20 mithqal).
وسق (wasq): A measure of agricultural produce. 1 wasq = 60 sa'as. The nisab for 'ushr is 5 wasqs = 300 sa'as (approx. 1061.40 kg).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the weight of the nisab of silver in grams?
A) 200 grams
B) 612.36 grams
C) 87.48 grams
D) 3.061 grams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi nisab thresholds are precisely defined: 200 dirhams (612.36g) for silver, 20 mithqal (87.48g) for gold, and 5 wasqs (300 sa'as) for agricultural produce, with the sa'a consistently equivalent to 160 istars despite an apparent intra-school dispute.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Modern Nisab Values for Silver, Gold, and Crops
Conversion tables for zakat nisab to modern weights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi zakat nisab for silver, gold, and crops in modern metric units, and calculate the zakat due by dividing the nisab by 40.

Core Idea
Silver nisab: 612.36g; Gold nisab: 87.48g; Crop nisab: 1061.40 kg — memorize these modern equivalents.

This passage provides the crucial conversion from classical weight measures (dirham, dinar, wasq) to grams and kilograms. As a student of Hanafi fiqh, you need to know these modern equivalents to determine zakat obligations today. We will focus on the three main nisab categories: silver, gold, and agricultural produce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab for silver
The passage states silver nisab is 200 dirhams. One dirham = 3.061g. Multiply: 200 × 3.061 = 612.36g. This is the threshold for zakat on silver.
2
Identify the nisab for gold
Gold nisab is 20 dinars. One dinar = 1 mithqal = 4.374g. Multiply: 20 × 4.374 = 87.48g. This is the threshold for gold.
Some tables may list slightly different figures due to variant dirham weights.
3
Identify the nisab for crops
Crop nisab is 5 wasq. One wasq = 60 sa'; one sa' = 1040 dirhams. Total: 5 × 60 × 1040 × 3.061 = 1061.40 kg. This is the threshold for ushr (zakat on produce).
The passage notes this is from Ahsan al-Fatawa and is adopted for caution.
4
Apply the zakat rate
Zakat is 1/40 (2.5%) of wealth above nisab. The passage shows that dividing the nisab by 40 gives the minimum zakat due if one exactly reaches nisab.
For example, 612.36g silver ÷ 40 = 15.309g silver zakat.
5
Verify with tables
The passage includes tables for silver and gold. Check that the values match the calculations above.
The gold table seems to have a typo (2189g), but the correct nisab is 87.48g.

Book of Zakat: One wasq equals 60 sa' = 212.28 kg. And five wasq equals 300 sa' = 1061.40 kg, which is called ten quintals sixty-one kg and forty grams (Ahsan al-Fatawa, vol. 4, p. 416). However, in Durr Mukhtar it is written that one sa' is 1040 dirhams. The text is: 'The considered sa' is that which contains one thousand and forty dirhams of mash and lentils' (Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Bab Sadaqat al-Fitr, vol. 3, p. 374). From this it is known that one sa' weighs one thousand and forty dirhams. And one dirham weighs 3.061 grams. Therefore, one sa' weighs 1040×3.061 = 3183.44 grams. And half a sa' is 1.591 kg, i.e., half a sa' is one kg five hundred ninety grams. And for caution, I have written the calculation of Ahsan al-Fatawa. And Allah knows best. Nisab and weights at a glance (Formula): 8 rati = 1 mashah; 12 mashah = 1 tola; 11.664 grams = 1 tola; 0.218 grams = 1 qirat; 4.374 grams = 1 mithqal; 442.25 grams = 1 ratl; 3538 grams = 1 sa'; 1769 grams = half sa'; 1000 grams = 1 kg; 3.061 grams = 1 dirham; 612.36 grams = nisab of silver; 4.374 grams = 1 dinar; 87.48 grams = nisab of gold. Commentary
This passage is a modern addendum to the classical Hanafi fiqh work, providing conversion tables from traditional Islamic weights (sa', wasq, dirham, dinar, mithqal, tola, etc.) to metric units (grams and kilograms). The author begins by establishing the equivalence of one wasq to 60 sa' and calculates the metric weight based on the Hanafi position that one sa' equals 1040 dirhams (citing Durr Mukhtar). He then gives the weight of one dirham as 3.061 grams (a standard modern value) and computes the sa' as 3183.44 grams (approximately 3.18 kg). The text ends by emphasizing that metric units are universal. The commentary should note that these conversions are practical aids; the actual nisab in classical Hanafi fiqh is defined in weight units (dirham, dinar, wasq) and the modern equivalents may vary slightly depending on the weight of the dirham used. The passage is not a ruling itself but a tool for applying the ruling in modern contexts.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory; specific values for silver (200 dirhams), gold (20 dinars), and crops (5 wasq).
درهم (dirham): A unit of weight; in this passage, 1 dirham = 3.061 grams.
دينار (dinar): A unit of weight for gold; 1 dinar = 1 mithqal = 4.374 grams.
وسق (wasq): A unit of measure for crops; 1 wasq = 60 sa' = approx. 212.28 kg. Nisab for crops is 5 wasq = 1061.40 kg.

Understanding the Sa' and Wasq: Definition and Conversion
Definition and conversion of sa' and wasq to metric

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi sa' (1040 dirhams) and wasq (60 sa') are defined, and apply the conversion to calculate zakat on crops (ushr).

Core Idea
One sa' = 1040 dirhams (3.18 kg); One wasq = 60 sa' (212.28 kg); Nisab for crops = 5 wasq (1061.40 kg) — these are foundations for zakat al-fitr and ushr.

This passage delves into the definition of the sa' and wasq as used in Hanafi fiqh, citing Durr Mukhtar and Ahsan al-Fatawa. Understanding these measures is critical for sadaqat al-fitr and ushr (zakat on crops). We'll trace the chain from dirham to wasq and calculate the modern equivalent.

Guided Path
1
Define the sa'
The sa' is defined as 1040 dirhams of lentils or beans (Durr Mukhtar). Weight of dirham = 3.061g, so 1 sa' = 1040 × 3.061 = 3183.44g = 3.18 kg.
The passage also gives 3538g for 1 sa' (likely a mistake in the table), but the correct calculation from 1040 dirhams is 3183.44g.
2
Define the wasq
1 wasq = 60 sa'. So 1 wasq = 60 × 3.18 kg = 212.28 kg.
This is directly stated in the passage.
3
Compute the nisab for crops
Nisab = 5 wasq = 5 × 212.28 kg = 1061.40 kg.
This matches the passage's crop nisab.
4
Apply ushr
Ushr (zakat on rain-fed crops) is 10% of the yield. For nisab of 1061.40 kg, ushr = 106.14 kg.
The passage gives this as well.
5
Note the caution
The author notes he used Ahsan al-Fatawa's calculation for caution, implying slight variations exist due to differing definitions of the dirham or sa'.
This highlights the importance of following a reliable authority.

Zakat on Vegetables and Irrigated Crops: Hanafi Rulings and Proofs
Rulings on zakat exempt for vegetables and half-tithe for irrigated crops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat (ushr) for vegetables and determine the applicable rate (full ushr or half ushr) based on the method of irrigation, citing the primary proofs.

Core Idea
Vegetables are exempt from ushr; irrigation method determines rate: full for natural, half for manual.

This commentary from Al-Sharh al-Sameri discusses three key zakat rulings: the exemption of vegetables, the reduced rate for manually irrigated crops, and a disagreement among the Sahibayn regarding non-measurable crops like saffron. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying agricultural zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings in the passage
The passage contains three distinct rulings: (1) no ushr on vegetables according to the Sahibayn, (2) half ushr for manually irrigated crops, (3) Abu Yusuf's opinion on saffron/cotton. Notice that the passage presents each with a proof (athar or hadith).
Rulings are numbered [505], [506], [507] in the original matn.
2
For each ruling, determine the hukm level and conditions
For ruling (1): The hukm is that vegetables are exempt from ushr (i.e., not wajib). Condition: the crop is a vegetable (not a grain or fruit measured by wasq). For ruling (2): Half ushr is wajib on crops irrigated manually. Condition: irrigation is by manual means (bucket, waterwheel, etc.). For ruling (3): Abu Yusuf states ushr is wajib on saffron/cotton if value reaches nisab; this is an ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi for (3) is the majority view (no ushr).
3
Examine the proofs and their wajh al-dalalah
Ruling (1) is proven by the athar of 'Ali (ra) stating no sadaqah on vegetables. Ruling (2) is proven by the prophetic hadith differentiating between natural and manual irrigation. The wajh al-dalalah: the explicit phrasing 'half ushr' for manual irrigation directly yields the rate.
The hadith is from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf and its practical consequence
There is intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on crops not measured by wasq: Abu Yusuf says ushr if value reaches nisab; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no ushr. The mufta bihi is the majority view. Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is obligate ushr on all produce including vegetables if nisab is met.
The thamarah: a Hanafi vegetable farmer pays nothing; a Shafi'i farmer pays ushr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[505] (٤) وليس فى الخضروات عندهما عشر [٥٠٦] (٥) وما سقى بغرب او دالية او سانية ففيه نصف العشر على القولين [٥٠٧] (٦) وقال ابو يوسف فيما لا يوسق كالزعفران والقطن يجب فيه العشر اذا بلغت قيمته قيمة خمسة اوسق من ادنى ما يدخل تحت الوسق. (اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبر ٢ میں گزر چکی ہے (٢) عن علی قال ليس في الخضر صدقه البقل ، والتفاح والقثاء (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الخضر ج رابع ص ١٢٠ نمبر ٧١٨٨) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبزیوں میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ [٥٠٦] (٥) جس زمین کو بڑے ڈول، رہٹ اور اونٹنی کے ذریعہ سیراب کیا جائے اس میں بیسواں حصہ ہے دونوں قوالوں پر ۔ جو زمین قدرتی پانی مثلا بارش ، نہر اور چشموں کے ذریعہ سیراب نہ ہوئی ہو بلکہ زیادہ تر اس کو ذاتی آلات کے ذریعہ سیراب کیا ہو مثلا بڑے ڈول یا رہٹ یا اونٹنی یا مشین کے ذریعہ سیراب کیا ہو تو اس زمین کی پیداوار میں بیسواں حصہ لازم ہوگا۔ یعنی بیس کیلو میں ایک کیلو غلہ لازم ہوگا۔ چونکہ اس میں مشقت اور خرچ زیادہ ہوا ہے اس لئے شریعت نے عشر کم کر کے آدھا کر دیا (٢) عن عبد الله عن ابيه عن النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال فيما سقت السماء والعيون او كان عثر يا العشر وما سقى بالنضح نصف العشر (بخاری شریف، باب العشر فیما یسقی من ماء السماء والماء الجاری ص ٢٠١ نمبر ١٤٨٣ ابوداود شریف، باب صدقته الزرع ص ٢٣٢ نمبر ١٥٩٦ مسلم شریف، کتاب الزکوۃ ، باب ما فيه العشر او نصف العشر ص ٣١٦ نمبر (٩٨) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشین وغیرہ سے زمین کو سیراب کیا ہو تو بیسواں حصہ لازم ہوگا۔ یہ مسئلہ بالا تفاق ہے۔ نصف العشر : دسویں حصہ کا آدھا یعنی بیسواں حصہ۔ [٥٠٧] (٦) امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ان چیزوں میں جو وسق میں نہ آتی ہوں جیسے زعفران اور روئی کہ ان میں عشر واجب ہوگا جب کہ اس کی قیمت ادنی درجہ کے غلہ کے وسق کی قیمت پانچ جائے جو وسق میں داخل ہوتا ہو۔
[505] (4) According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), there is no 'ushr on vegetables. [506] (5) And what is irrigated by a large bucket, a waterwheel, or a camel-driven device, then half of the 'ushr is due, according to the two opinions. [507] (6) Abu Yusuf said: regarding things that are not measured in wasq, like saffron and cotton, 'ushr is obligatory when their value reaches the value of five wasq of the lowest grain that enters into wasq. (The proof for this passed in issue no. 2: from 'Ali: he said: There is no sadaqah on vegetables, greens, apples, and cucumbers. [Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Khudr, vol. 4, p. 120, no. 7188] This athar shows that there is no 'ushr on vegetables. [506] (5) Land that is irrigated by a large bucket, a waterwheel, or a camel—in it is one-twentieth (half of 'ushr), according to both opinions. Land that is not irrigated by natural water like rain, rivers, or springs, but rather mostly by personal devices, e.g., a large bucket, waterwheel, camel, or machine—then on its produce one-twentieth is obligatory. That is, in twenty kilos, one kilo of grain is due. Because there is more hardship and expense, the Shari'ah reduced the 'ushr to half. (2) From 'Abdullah from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him): He said: "In what is watered by the sky, springs, or is 'athari (naturally watered), there is 'ushr; and what is watered by irrigation (by manual means) has half 'ushr." [Bukhari, Bab al-'Ushr, p. 201, no. 1483; Abu Dawud, Bab Sadaqat al-Zar', p. 232, no. 1596; Muslim, Kitab al-Zakah, Bab ma fihi al-'Ushr aw nisf al-'Ushr, p. 316, no. 98] This hadith shows that if land is irrigated by machine etc., one-twentieth is due. This issue is agreed upon. Half of 'ushr: half of the tenth part, i.e., one-twentieth. [507] (6) Imam Abu Yusuf said: For things that are not measured in wasq, like saffron and cotton, 'ushr is obligatory when their value reaches the value of five wasq of the lowest grain that enters into wasq.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on three rulings from the matn of Al-Tajrid or similar work. The first ruling (505) states the position of the two companions (Sahibayn) that there is no 'ushr (tithe) on vegetables. The proof is the athar of 'Ali (ra) that there is no sadaqah on vegetables like greens, apples, and cucumbers. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school. The second ruling (506) concerns crops irrigated by manual means: if the land is irrigated by a large bucket, waterwheel, or camel-driven device (i.e., with effort and expense), then only half of the 'ushr (i.e., 1/20 of the produce) is due. This is based on the well-known hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that crops watered naturally (by rain, rivers, springs) have full 'ushr (1/10), while those watered by manual irrigation have half 'ushr. The commentary explains that the reduction is due to the increased hardship and cost. This ruling is by agreement (ittifaq). The third ruling (507) is Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion that for crops not measured by volume (wasq), like saffron and cotton, 'ushr is due when their market value equals the value of five wasq of the cheapest grain that is measured by wasq. This opinion is not the relied-upon position; the majority (including Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa) hold that 'ushr is only due on grains and fruits that are measurable by wasq and can be stored. Abu Yusuf's view considers the value, analogous to the nisab for trade goods.

Key Terms
العشر (al-'ushr): One-tenth of agricultural produce due as zakat on naturally irrigated land.
نصف العشر (nisf al-'ushr): Half of the 'ushr, i.e., one-twentieth (1/20 = 5%) of the produce, due on manually irrigated crops.
وسق (wasq): A dry volume measure equal to 60 sa' (approx. 212 kg according to Hanafi). Used as nisab for agricultural zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the ruling on zakat (ushr) for vegetables?
A) Ushr is obligatory if the value reaches the nisab.
B) There is no ushr on vegetables.
C) Half ushr is obligatory.
D) Full ushr is obligatory on all vegetables.

Key Takeaway
Vegetables are exempt from ushr in the Hanafi school, and the ushr rate depends on irrigation: full ushr for natural, half for manual, based on prophetic hadith and the athar of 'Ali.

No 'Ushr on Vegetables (Sahibayn's View)
Ruling statement: No 'ushr on vegetables according to Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'ushr for vegetables and explain the basis from Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Vegetables are exempt from 'ushr in the Hanafi school; only staple crops measured by wasq are tithed.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from Sahibayn regarding agricultural tithe. While some scholars include vegetables, the Hanafi relied-upon view exempts them. An athar from Ali (RA) supports this exemption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the central ruling: There is no 'ushr on vegetables according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The term 'عندهما' refers to the two disciples (Sahibayn).
2
Identify the authority
Note that this is the position of the two major students of Abu Hanifa. Their view is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) in the school.
Contrasted with Abu Hanifa's reported view which required 'ushr if value reaches nisab.
3
Identify the basis
The ruling is based on an athar (report) from Ali (RA) that there is no sadaqah (charity) on vegetables, apples, and cucumbers.
This is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli) from the Companion.
4

5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Sharh al-Saghir) confirm that the ruling of no 'ushr on vegetables is the operative one for fatwa.
This is a zahir al-riwayah position.

Half-Tenth for Artificially Irrigated Land
Ruling with proof for half 'ushr on artificially irrigated land.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 'ushr rate for artificially irrigated land and identify the textual proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Land irrigated by manual means incurs half the standard 'ushr (5%) because the effort reduces net yield.

This lesson addresses the zakat rate for crops from land that is irrigated artificially, such as by bucket, waterwheel, or pump. The Hanafi madhhab holds a uniform half-'ushr rate for such land, supported by a clear prophetic hadith. You will learn the ruling and its textual basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon here? It is the zakat (ushr) due on crops from land that is irrigated by artificial means such as a bucket, waterwheel, or camel-driven pump. The ruling is that the rate is half of the normal 'ushr, i.e., 5% instead of 10%.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith from the Prophet (PBUH): 'In what is irrigated by sky and springs or is 'atharī, the tithe, and what is irrigated by manual means has half the tithe.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit differentiation between natural irrigation (full 'ushr) and manual irrigation (half 'ushr) directly sets the rate. The word 'manual means' (النضح) covers all forms of artificial irrigation.
The illah (reason) is the additional effort and expense, which reduces the net yield, justifying a lower rate.
4
Understand the mufta bihi
Within the Hanafi school, there is consensus (على القولين means both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree). The mufta bihi is half 'ushr for all artificially irrigated land.
Modern pumps are included under the same ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما سقى بغرب او دالية او سانية ففيه نصف العشر على القولين. قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: فيما سقت السماء والعيون أو كان عثريا العشر، وما سقى بالنضح نصف العشر.
And what is irrigated by a bucket, waterwheel, or camel-driven pump has in it half the tithe according to both opinions. The Prophet (PBUH) said: In what is irrigated by sky and springs or is 'atharī, the tithe, and what is irrigated by manual means has half the tithe.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn stating that crops from land irrigated manually (by bucket, waterwheel, or camel) are subject to half the 'ushr, i.e., 5% instead of 10%. The term 'on both opinions' refers to the agreement of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on this point. The proof is the hadith narrated from the Prophet that distinguishes between naturally irrigated land (10%) and manually irrigated land (5%). The rational basis is that the additional effort and expense reduce the net yield, so the tax is halved.

Key Terms
غرب (gharb): A large bucket used to draw water from a well; here symbolizes any manual water-drawing device.
دالية (dāliyah): A waterwheel, typically animal-drawn, used for irrigation.
سانية (sāniyah): A camel-driven water-raising device; general term for animal-drawn irrigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full 'ushr (10%).
B) Half 'ushr (5%).
C) No 'ushr.
D) Double 'ushr (20%).

Key Takeaway
Artificially irrigated land incurs half 'ushr (5%) due to the additional effort involved, as established by the Prophet's hadith.

Dispute on 'Ushr for Non-Measured Crops: Saffron and Cotton
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the nisab for crops not measured by wasq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the nisab for 'ushr on crops not measured by wasq and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
For crops like saffron, the Hanafi school splits: Abu Yusuf uses value, Muhammad uses quantity; the latter is relied upon.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over crops not customarily measured by wasq (volume), such as saffron and cotton. Both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani agree that 'ushr is due, but they differ on how the nisab is determined. Understanding their reasoning helps clarify how Shari'ah expands principles to new commodities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed point
Recognize that the dispute is about the nisab threshold for 'ushr on crops not measured by wasq, not about the obligation itself.
Both imams agree 'ushr is wajib; the ikhtilaf is on the condition.
2
State Abu Yusuf's view and his proof
Abu Yusuf uses a value-based criterion: the crop's value must equal the value of five wasqs of the cheapest grain.
This is a qiyas on currency zakat, where value matters.
3
State Muhammad's view and his proof
Muhammad uses a quantity-based criterion: the crop must reach five of the highest customary unit (e.g., 5 loads for cotton, 5 mann for saffron).
This is a qiyas on grain nisab, but using the unit specific to each crop.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a concrete scenario: 4 mann of saffron worth 5 wasq of grain. Under Abu Yusuf, 'ushr is due; under Muhammad, it is not.
The difference depends on valuation vs. fixed quantity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi view
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers Muhammad's view for its certainty and stability; it is the operative position for fatwa.
This is the relied-upon view in the late Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وقال ابو يوسف) فيما لا يوسق كالزعفران والقطن يجب فيه العشر اذا بلغت قيمته قيمة خمسة اوسق من ادنى ما يدخل تحت الوسق. (وقال محمد) يجب العشر اذا بلغ الخارج خمسة امثال من اعلى ما يقدر به نوعه فاعتبر في القطن خمسة احمال وفى الزعفران خمسة امناء.
Abu Yusuf said: In what is not measured by wasq, like saffron and cotton, the tithe is obligatory when its value reaches the value of five wasqs of the lowest thing that enters under wasq. And Muhammad said: The tithe is obligatory when the produce reaches five examples of the highest measure by which its type is measured; so he considered for cotton five loads and for saffron five mana.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding crops that are not measured by wasq, such as saffron (expensive, lightweight) and cotton (bulky). The nisab for 'ushr on grains is five wasq (approx. 653 kg). Abu Yusuf uses a value-based criterion: if the saffron or cotton is worth the price of five wasqs of the cheapest grain (e.g., barley or millet), then 'ushr applies. This is rational because the commodity itself cannot be measured by volume. Muhammad, however, uses a physical measure: the crop must reach five of the highest unit customarily used for that crop. For cotton, the highest unit is a 'himl' (load); for saffron, a 'mann' (approx. 796g). Therefore, if one has five loads of cotton or five mann of saffron, 'ushr is due. Abu Hanifa's position is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi works often prefer Muhammad's view as more precise.

Key Terms
لا يوسق (lā yūsaq): Not measured by wasq; crops that are not customarily measured by volume (e.g., saffron, cotton).
احمال (aḥmāl): Plural of ḥiml (load); a unit of bulk measurement for cotton.
امناء (amnā’): Plural of mann; a unit of weight, approximately 795.86 g.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the nisab for 'ushr on saffron?
A) Value equal to five wasqs of cheapest grain.
B) Five mann of saffron.
C) Five kilograms of saffron.
D) No 'ushr at all on saffron.

Key Takeaway
For crops not measured by wasq, the Hanafi school relies on Muhammad's view: nisab equals five of the highest customary unit.

'Ushr on Honey from 'Ushr Land
Ruling on 'ushr for honey from 'ushr land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'ushr for honey from 'ushr land and identify the condition of land type.

Core Idea
'Ushr on honey is due regardless of amount if harvested from 'ushr land.

This lesson addresses a specific zakat ruling: honey from 'ushr land is subject to 'ushr (tithe) even if the quantity is small. The matn states this clearly, and we will explore the rationale and the intra-madhhab difference with the Sahibayn regarding the nisab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the extraction of honey from land. The ruling: 'ushr is wajib on that honey.
This is a zakat ruling, not a general tax.
2
Recognise the condition
The honey must be taken from 'ushr land (ard al-‘ushr). Honey from other types of land (e.g., kharaji, mawat) may have different rules.
The text explicitly restricts the ruling to 'ushr land.
3
Note the quantity rule
'Ushr is due whether the honey is little or much (qallan aw kathiran). No nisab applies.
This distinguishes honey from grains, which require five wasq.
4
Understand the basis
The ruling is based on qiyas on land produce: honey is a valuable product of the land, so it is analogous to crops.
Abu Hanifa held this view; the Sahibayn required a nisab (e.g., five mann).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي العسل العشر اذا اخذ من ارض العشر قل او كثر.
And in honey is the tithe when taken from 'ushr land, whether little or much.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn stating that honey harvested from 'ushrī land (land subject to 'ushr) is subject to 'ushr without any minimum nisab. The clause 'whether little or much' indicates that even a small amount triggers the obligation, unlike grains which require five wasq. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The proof is based on qiyas on land produce, as honey is a valuable product of the land. Sahibayn reportedly require a nisab of five mann or similar, but the text here does not mention their view; the author may be stating Abu Hanifa's opinion as standard.

Key Terms
العسل (al-‘asal): Honey produced by bees from flowers on 'ushr land.
أرض العشر (arḍ al-‘ushr): Land subject to 'ushr tax, typically owned by Muslims and conquered peacefully or irrigated by rain.

Nisab for Cotton and Saffron: Imam Muhammad's Measure-Based Criterion
States Imam Muhammad's view on nisab for cotton and saffron.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Muhammad's criterion for nisab of crops not measured by wasq and distinguish it from Abu Yusuf's value-based criterion.

Core Idea
For crops not measured by wasq, Imam Muhammad uses the largest local measure as the nisab unit.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nisab for zakat on agricultural produce that is not customarily measured by wasq, such as cotton and saffron. While Abu Yusuf equates their value to five wasq of the cheapest grain, Imam Muhammad proposes a measure-based criterion using the largest unit for each specific crop. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply zakat rules to diverse agricultural products.

Guided Path
1
Understand the standard nisab
Recall that for grains and fruits measured by wasq, the nisab is five wasq. This is the baseline for comparison.
One wasq ≈ 60 sa' ≈ a specific volume.
2
Identify the problem crop
Cotton and saffron are not measured by wasq due to their bulk or high value. Therefore, a different criterion is needed to determine nisab.
Saffron is produced in small quantities; cotton is bulky and packed in bales.
3
State Abu Yusuf's value-based criterion
Abu Yusuf considers the market value of the produce. If the value equals five wasq of the cheapest grain (e.g., millet), then nisab is reached. This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
This criterion is practical for high-value crops.
4
State Imam Muhammad's measure-based criterion
Imam Muhammad looks at the largest local measure used for that specific crop. For cotton, the largest measure is a bale (haml); for saffron, it is a mann. Nisab is reached when the produce amounts to five of these units.
For example, five bales of cotton or five mana of saffron constitute nisab.
5
Compare the two positions and note the tarjih
Both views are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah, but later Hanafi scholars prefer Abu Yusuf's value-based criterion because it is more practical and just, covering high-value crops that may not physically reach five large measures.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Imam Muhammad, a small quantity of high-value saffron might not reach nisab, whereas under Abu Yusuf it would.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال محمد يجب العشر اذا بلغ الخارج خمسة امثال من اعلى ما يقدر به نوعه فاعتبر في القطن خمسة احمال وفى الزعفران خمسة امناء . الشرح: ادنی درجہ کا غلہ جیسے جوار، باجرہ جنگی قیمت بہت کم ہوتی ہے اور یہ وسق کے ذریعہ نا پے جاتے ہیں۔اب زعفران اور روئی جو وسق میں نہیں ناپے جاتے کیونکہ زعفران بہت کم پیدا ہوتا ہے اور قیمتی ہوتا ہے۔ پوری کھیت میں دو چار کیلوہی ہوگا۔ پانچ وسق ، دس کو مینٹل تو ہو گا ہی نہیں ، اسی طرح روئی کی گانٹھ بناتے ہیں وسق میں وزن نہیں کرتے۔ لیکن لیکن پیدا شدہ زعفران کی قیمت پانچ وسق جوار یا باجرے کی قیمت کے برابر ہو جائے تو اب زعفران پر عشر لازم ہوگا۔ اسی طرح پیدا شدہ روئی کی قیمت پانچ وسق جوار یا باجرے کی قیمت کے برابر ہو جائے تو اب روئی میں عشر لازم ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے معنی اور قیمت کا اعتبار کیا ہے کہ ادنی درجہ کے غلہ کی قیمت کے برابر ہو جائے تو گویا کہ معنوی اعتبار سے پانچ وسق ہو گیا۔ اور اتنا ہی کافی سمجھا گیا۔ امام محمد نے فرمایا جب نکلنے والا غلہ پانچ مثل پہنچ جائے اعلی پیمانہ سے جس کے ذریعہ سے اس قسم کا غلہ ناپا جاتا ہے تو اعتبار کیا جائے گاروئی میں پانچ گانٹھ کا اور زعفران میں پانچ من کا۔ امام محمد کی رائے یہ ہے کہ وہ غلہ جو وسق میں نہیں ناپا جاتا ہو تو یہ دیکھا جائے کہ اس کے ناپنے کا بڑے سے بڑا پیمانہ کیا ہے۔ اس بڑے سے بڑے پیمانے سے پانچ پیمانہ وہ غلہ ہو جائے تو گویا کہ پانچ وسق کی طرح ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اب اس میں عشر لازم ہوگا۔ مثلا زعفران کے ناپنے کا بڑے سے بڑا پیمانہ من ہے جو 795.86 گرام کا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے پانچ کیلو زعفران ہو جائے تو گویا کہ پانچ وسق گیہوں کی طرح ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اب اس میں عشر واجب ہے۔ یا روئی کو گانٹھ سے ناپتے ہیں اس کا بڑا پیمانہ وہی ہے اس لئے پانچ گانٹھ روٹی ہو جائے تو اس میں عشر واجب ہوگا۔ ول امام محمد نے ایسے غلے کے بڑے پیمانے کا اعتبار کیا۔ احمال : حمل کی جمع ہے بوجھ، گانٹھ۔ امناء : جمع ہے من کی ایک وزن ہے جو 795.86 گرام کا ہوتا ہے۔
And Muhammad said: Tithe is obligatory when the produce reaches five times the highest measure by which its type is measured. So in cotton, five loads are considered; in saffron, five mana. [Commentary: Low-grade grain like millet, sorghum—its market value is very low and it is measured by wasq. Now saffron and cotton are not measured by wasq because saffron is produced in very small quantities and is valuable. In a whole field, only two or four kilos. Five wasq, ten quintals would not happen. Similarly, cotton bales are made, not weighed by wasq. But if the value of the produced saffron equals the value of five wasq of millet or sorghum, then tithe becomes obligatory on saffron. Similarly, if the value of produced cotton equals the value of five wasq of millet or sorghum, then tithe becomes obligatory on cotton. Abu Yusuf considered meaning and value: if it equals the value of the lowest grade grain, then in a meaningful sense it becomes five wasq, and that is sufficient. Imam Muhammad said: When the produce reaches five times the highest measure by which that type is measured, then it is considered. In cotton, five bales; in saffron, five mana. Imam Muhammad's opinion is: for crops not measured by wasq, we look at the largest measure used for that crop. If the crop reaches five of those largest measures, then it is akin to five wasq. Therefore, tithe becomes obligatory. For example, the largest measure for saffron is a mann which is 795.86 grams. So if five kilos of saffron are produced, it is akin to five wasq of wheat. Therefore, tithe is wajib. Or cotton is measured by bales, its largest measure is that, so if five bales of cotton are produced, tithe becomes wajib. Imam Muhammad thus considered the largest measure for such crops.]
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Muhammad's ruling regarding the nisab for crops that are not customarily measured by wasq, such as cotton and saffron. The text first explains the background: low-grade grains like millet and sorghum are measured by wasq and have a nisab of five wasq. However, saffron and cotton are not measured by wasq due to their high value or bulk. Abu Yusuf's approach is to equate their value to five wasq of the lowest grade grain. Imam Muhammad offers a different criterion: he looks at the largest local measure used for that specific crop. For cotton, the largest measure is a bale (haml), so five bales constitute nisab. For saffron, the largest measure is a mann (mina), so five mana constitute nisab. The commentary further clarifies that Imam Muhammad's view is based on the physical volume rather than value. The key terms are explained: 'ahmal' (plural of haml) meaning loads or bales, and 'amna'' (plural of mann) a weight measure approximately 795.86 grams.

Key Terms
وسق (wasq): A standard measure of volume for grain, approximately 60 sa'.
حمل (haml): A load or bale, used as a measure for cotton.
من (mann): A measure of weight, approximately 795.86 grams, used for saffron.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Five wasq
B) Five mana
C) Five loads
D) Value equal to five wasq of millet

Key Takeaway
For crops not measured by wasq, Imam Muhammad uses the largest local measure (five units) as nisab, while the relied-upon Hanafi position prefers a value-based criterion.

Nisab for Honey: Dispute Among Hanafi Imams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on honey nisab with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the nisab of honey and evaluate the evidence each imam uses.

Core Idea
The nisab of honey is disputed: Abu Hanifa requires no minimum, Abu Yusuf ten water-skins, Muhammad five faraq.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the nisab for zakat on honey. Each of the three major imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—derives a different threshold from hadith evidence. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting textual evidence within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State what each imam says about the minimum amount of honey that triggers zakat.
Abu Hanifa: any amount. Abu Yusuf: 10 water-skins (azqaq). Muhammad: 5 faraq (1 farq = 36 Iraqi ratls).
2
Locate each imam's dalil
Identify the specific hadith or reasoning each imam uses.
Abu Hanifa uses the absolute hadith of Hilal (no nisab specified). Abu Yusuf uses the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'For every ten water-skins, one water-skin.' Muhammad uses analogy with other zakatable produce and defines nisab as 5 faraq.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof yields the nisab number.
Abu Hanifa: the command 'give tithe' is unrestricted. Abu Yusuf: the phrase 'in every ten water-skins' implies a minimum. Muhammad: 'zakat' implies a nisab, and he sets it by analogy with grains (5 wasq).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which position is relied upon for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
Later scholars (e.g., in al-Hidayah) prefer Abu Hanifa's view due to the general evidence.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference in rulings.
A beekeeper with a small honey harvest may or may not owe zakat depending on which view is applied.

And concerning honey: tithe is due when it is taken from 'ushri land, whether little or much. The commentary: ... [repeated from previous lesson actually the start is from page 334 but we take the honey-specific part]. [Page 335] (9) And Abu Yusuf said: Nothing is due until it reaches ten water-skins. (10) And Muhammad said: Five faraq, and a farq is thirty-six ratls by Iraqi ratl. (11) And there is nothing in what is taken from the mountains, whether little or much. A narration: Hilal, one of the Banu Matta'an, came to the Messenger of Allah with the tithe of his bees, and he asked him to protect a valley called Salaba. So the Messenger of Allah protected that valley for him. When Umar ibn al-Khattab became caliph, Sufyan ibn Wahb wrote to Umar ibn al-Khattab asking about that. Umar wrote: Pay to him what he used to pay to the Messenger of Allah from the tithe of his bees, and protect for him his valley; otherwise it is merely the monsoon flies that whoever wishes may eat. (Abu Dawud, ...). This hadith mentions giving zakat on honey and is absolute; there is no condition of ten water-skins. Therefore, whatever honey is obtained, one-tenth is obligatory. The principle for honey is the same as for crops: tithe on all, little or much. (9) Imam Abu Yusuf said: Until it reaches ten water-skins, i.e., ten water-skins or more, then tithe is due; less than that, no tithe. Their evidence is the hadith from Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Concerning honey, for every ten water-skins, one water-skin.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that when there are ten water-skins, one is due. (10) Imam Muhammad said: Until the honey reaches five faraq. One farq is thirty-six ratls by Iraqi ratl. Imam Muhammad says: if at least five faraq of honey are produced, tithe is due; less than that, no tithe. One farq is thirty-six ratls. If one ratl is 442.25 grams, one farq is 15.921 kg, and five faraq are 79.605 kg. If one ratl is 663.41 grams, one farq is 23.882 kg, and five faraq are 119.413 kg.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents the three Hanafi opinions on the nisab for honey. Abu Hanifa holds that any amount of honey from 'ushri land is subject to tithe, citing a general hadith that does not specify a minimum. Abu Yusuf requires ten water-skins (ziq), based on a specific hadith from Ibn Umar: 'For every ten water-skins, one water-skin is due.' Imam Muhammad requires five faraq, where one farq equals thirty-six Iraqi ratls. The commentary explains the weight conversions. The hadith of Hilal is used to support Abu Hanifa's view because it mentions tithe on honey without specifying a nisab. The passage thus illustrates an intra-Hanafi dispute where each imam uses different evidence.

Key Terms
زق (ziq): A water-skin used as a measure for honey; plural azqaq.
فرق (farq): A measure of capacity equal to 36 Iraqi ratls.
عشر (ushr): Tithe, one-tenth of produce, obligatory on certain agricultural products from 'ushri land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab contains a legitimate ikhtilaf on honey nisab, but the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's: any amount triggers tithe.

Abu Yusuf's Minimum Threshold for Zakat on Honey
Intra-Hanafi dispute on honey zakat minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's position on the minimum amount for zakat on honey, identify the hadith evidence, and compare it with the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Zakat on honey is due only when the quantity reaches ten water skins, according to Abu Yusuf, based on a hadith.

This lesson focuses on the specific ruling of Imam Abu Yusuf within the Hanafi school regarding the minimum amount (nisab) for zakat on honey. While Imam Abu Hanifa holds that zakat is due on any amount, Abu Yusuf requires ten water skins, citing a hadith from Ibn Umar. We will examine the textual evidence and understand the practical implications of this disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Imam
State that Abu Yusuf rules that zakat (one-tenth) is wajib only when the honey reaches ten water skins (azqaq).
This is in contrast to Abu Hanifa who requires no minimum.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the hadith cited by Abu Yusuf: from Ibn Umar, the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Indeed, regarding honey, for every ten water skins, one water skin.'
The hadith is recorded in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Analyse the Wajh al-Dalalah
The phrase 'in kulli 'asharati azqaqin zuqq' indicates a proportion: one out of ten. This implies that zakat is due only when the total reaches ten.
Abu Yusuf interprets this as a condition: no zakat below ten.
4
Compare with Other Hanafi Views
Note that Abu Hanifa holds zakat on any amount, and Muhammad requires five faraq (about 60-80 kg).
Each imam relies on different evidence or interpretations.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
In fatwa, the mufta bihi may vary by region; some follow Abu Yusuf (ten water skins), others Abu Hanifa (any amount).
The difference affects when a beekeeper must pay zakat.
