وقال ابو يوسف لا شيء فيه حتى تبلغ عشرة ازقاق [۵۱۰] (۹) امام ابو يوسف نے فرمایا یہاں تک کہ دس مشک پہنچ جائے۔ یعنی دس مشک یا اس سے زیادہ شہد وصول ہوگا تو اس میں عشر لازم ہوگا اور اس سے کم ہوا تو اس میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الا الله في العسل في كل عشرة ازقاق زق (ب) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء في زکوۃ العسل ص ۱۳۷ نمبر ۶۲۹ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب زکوۃ العسل ص ۲۳۳ نمبر (۱۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دس مشک ہو تب ایک مشک لازم ہوگا۔ ازقاق : زق کی جمع ہے مشک۔
And Abu Yusuf said: Nothing is obligatory on it until it reaches ten water skins. (9) Imam Abu Yusuf said: Until ten water skins are reached. That is, when ten or more water skins of honey are obtained, one-tenth is obligatory, and if less, no one-tenth is due. His evidence is this hadith: from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, regarding honey, for every ten water skins, one water skin.' (Tirmidhi, Bab Zakat al-Asal, p. 137 no. 629 / Abu Dawud, Bab Zakat al-Asal, p. 233 no. 120). From this hadith it is known that when there are ten water skins, one water skin is due. Azqaq is the plural of ziq, meaning water skin.

Commentary
This passage presents the position of Imam Abu Yusuf within the Hanafi school on the minimum amount (nisab) for zakat on honey. He holds that zakat (one-tenth) is only obligatory when the honey reaches ten water skins (azqaq). His evidence is a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ specified one water skin for every ten. The commentator explains that Abu Yusuf's view is based on this explicit textual proof. Note that within the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad have different thresholds, as will be seen in the following lessons.

Key Terms
ازقاق (azqaq): Plural of زق (ziq), meaning water skins used to store honey.
عشر (ushr): One-tenth, the rate of zakat on honey and certain agricultural produce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Ten water skins
C) Any amount

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Yusuf's ruling that zakat on honey is due only after ten water skins is based on a specific hadith, but it is one of three valid Hanafi positions on the nisab.

Imam Muhammad: Nisab of Honey Zakat at Five Faraq
Imam Muhammad's nisab for honey zakat with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Muhammad's nisab for honey zakat and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
For Imam Muhammad, honey zakat begins at five faraq, analogized to grains at five wasaq.

This passage presents the position of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on the minimum threshold (nisab) for honey zakat. While Abu Hanifa held that any amount of honey triggers zakat, Imam Muhammad set a nisab of five faraq by analogy with grains. Understanding this intra-madhhab ikhtilaf is crucial for applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Imam Muhammad states that honey zakat is due only when the quantity reaches five faraq. If less than five faraq, no zakat is owed.
A faraq is a large vessel of 36 Iraqi ratls.
2
Recognize the basis: qiyas
Imam Muhammad uses qiyas (analogy) to grains: grains have a nisab of five wasaq, so honey should have a nisab of its largest standard measure, the faraq, at five.
The underlying illa (effective cause) is that both are staple items measured by a large vessel.
3
Understand the dispute within the Hanafi school
Abu Hanifa held that honey zakat is due on any amount (no nisab), based on a general command and practice. Imam Muhammad's position is one of three opinions in the school.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school is generally Imam Muhammad's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال محمد خمسة افراق والفرق ستة وثلثون رطلا بالعراقي [۵۱۱] (۱۰) امام محمد نے فرمایا یہاں تک کہ شہر پانچ فرق کو پہنچے اور ایک فرق چھتیس رطل کا ہو گا عراقی رطل کے ساتھ۔ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ شہد کم سے کم پانچ فرق نکلے تو اس میں عشر لازم ہے اور اگر اس سے کم وصول ہو تو عشر لازم نہیں۔ اور ایک فرق چھتیس (63) رطل کا ہوتا ہے۔ اب اگر ایک رطل 442.25 گرام کا لیں تو ایک فرق 15.921 کیلو کا ہوگا۔ اور پانچ فرق 79.605 کیلو کے ہوں گے۔ اور اگر ایک رطل 663.41 گرام کا لیں تو ایک فرق 23.882 کیلو کا ہوگا۔ اور پانچ فرق 119.413 کیلو کے ہوں گے۔ حاشیه : (الف) منی متعان کا ایک آدمی ہلال حضور کے پاس دئے شہد کا عشر لے کر اور یہ سوال کیا کہ ایک وادی جس کا نام سلمہ ہے اس کو ان کے لئے محفوظ کر دیا جائے۔ تو حضور نے اس وادی کو ہلال کے لئے محفوظ کر دیا۔ پس جب عمر بن خطاب امیر المؤمنین بنے تو سفیان بن وہب نے ان کو اس بارے میں پوچھنے کے لئے خط لکھا تو حضرت عمر نے جواب دیا کہ شہد کا جتنا عشر حضور کو ادا کیا کرتے تھے اتنا ہی ادا کریں۔ اور حضرت ہلال کے لئے سلمہ وادی محفوظ کر دیں۔ ورنہ تو وہ بارش کا گھاس ہے جو چاہے اس کو کھائے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا شہد کے بارے میں کہ ہر دس ملک میں ایک مشک ہے۔
And Muhammad said: Five faraq, and one faraq is thirty-six ratls by the Iraqi ratl. (10) Imam Muhammad said: Until the honey reaches five faraq. And one faraq is thirty-six ratls by the Iraqi ratl. Imam Muhammad says: If at least five faraq of honey are obtained, one-tenth is due; if less, no one-tenth is due. And one faraq is thirty-six ratls. So if one ratl is taken as 442.25 grams, one faraq equals 15.921 kg, and five faraq equal 79.605 kg. And if one ratl is taken as 663.41 grams, one faraq equals 23.882 kg, and five faraq equal 119.413 kg. Footnote (a): Hilal ibn Mu'yan came to the Prophet with the tenth of honey and asked that a valley called Salama be reserved for him. The Prophet reserved it for him. When Umar became caliph, Sufyan ibn Wahb wrote to him asking about it, and Umar replied: 'Pay to him what he used to pay to the Prophet of the tenth of his honey, and reserve Salama valley for him. Otherwise, it is just rain-fed grass that anyone can eat.' (b) The Prophet said regarding honey: 'For every ten containers, one container.'
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents the position of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on the nisab for zakat on honey. He sets it at five faraq, where a faraq is a large measuring vessel. His reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas) with other measurable items: since honey is measured by volume, its largest vessel (faraq) is used, and when five of these are reached, zakat becomes due, similar to grains where five wasaq is the nisab. The commentator provides modern weight equivalents for clarity. The footnote includes historical background about Hilal ibn Mu'yan, showing that the Prophet accepted honey zakat without specifying a minimum, which supports the absolute view of Abu Hanifa, but Muhammad uses qiyas to set a nisab.

Key Terms
فرق (faraq): A large measuring vessel for honey, equivalent to 36 ratls Iraqi.
رطل (ratl): A unit of weight; Iraqi ratl used here, approximately 442-663 grams depending on the standard.

No Zakat on Kharaj Land Produce
Ruling that kharaj land produce exempt from ushr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that produce from kharaj land is exempt from ushr and explain the rationale of preventing double taxation.

Core Idea
Kharaj and ushr never converge on the same land – double taxation is impermissible.

Agricultural land in Islamic law is categorized into ushr land and kharaj land. While ushr land requires zakat on its produce, kharaj land – conquered lands retained by original owners – requires a fixed tax called kharaj. This lesson clarifies that the two taxes are mutually exclusive; imposing both would constitute double taxation, which is prohibited by shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and determine what the ruling is regarding produce from kharaj land. Is zakat (ushr) required? The answer is clearly no.
The matn phrase 'من ارض الخراج عشر' is negated by the commentary.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentary gives the reasoning: imposing both kharaj and ushr would double the burden on the landowner, and shari'ah does not allow double taxation on the same land.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on the principle of preventing hardship.
3
Distinguish kharaj from ushr
Recognize that kharaj is a fixed land tax on conquered lands, while ushr is a proportional zakat on produce from non-kharaj land. They apply to different categories of land.
Key terms: kharaj and ushr.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position is that ushr is not due on kharaj land. Some other schools may differ and impose ushr on all land. Understand the practical consequence of this disagreement.
Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من ارض الخراج عشر [۵۱۲] (۱۱) اور خراجی زمین کی پیداوار میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ خراجی زمین میں خراج لازم ہوتا ہے۔ اب اس پر عشر لازم کریں تو مونت دوگنی ہو جائے گی اور شریعت ایک زمین پر دو مرتبہ خراج یا عشر وصول نہیں کرتی۔ اس لئے زمین کی پیداوار میں عشر لازم نہیں ہے۔ صرف خراج لازم ہوگا۔
From kharaj land, nothing. (11) And on the produce of kharaj land, there is no one-tenth. Kharaj is obligatory on kharaj land. Now if one-tenth is also imposed on it, the burden will become double, and the Sharia does not collect both kharaj and one-tenth on the same land twice. Therefore, no one-tenth is obligatory on the produce of such land; only kharaj is obligatory.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage clarifies that agricultural produce from kharaj land (land conquered by force and kept under Muslim control with a fixed tax) is not subject to zakat (one-tenth). Instead, only kharaj is paid. The reasoning is that imposing both would lead to double taxation, which is prohibited in Islamic law. This ruling prevents undue hardship on landowners. The matn phrase 'من ارض الخراج عشر' might be a statement to be negated, as the commentary explains the correct ruling.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): A fixed land tax imposed on conquered lands retained by the original owners.
عشر (ushr): One-tenth, the zakat on agricultural produce from non-kharaj land.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj land produce is exempt from ushr; only kharaj is due, because shari'ah does not permit double taxation on the same land.

Rulings on 'Ushr for Honey and Kharaj Land
Explains when 'ushr is due and exempt on agricultural produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which 'ushr is due on honey according to Imam Muhammad and explain why kharaj land is exempt from 'ushr.

Core Idea
Honey requires five farq for 'ushr; kharaj land is exempt because Shari'ah does not double-tax.

This passage addresses two specific zakat rulings: the measure for honey and the exemption for kharaj land. Understanding these rulings requires knowing the basis for determining nisab for items not measured by wasq, and the principle of avoiding double taxation. Imam Muhammad's approach extends the general zakat framework to honey using the largest customary measure, while the kharaj exemption is based on clear rational analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and note that it presents two separate rulings: one on honey (when 'ushr becomes wajib) and one on kharaj land (exemption from 'ushr).
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's principle for honey
Imam Muhammad uses a general principle: for items not measured by wasq, look at their largest customary measuring vessel. For honey, that is the farq, so five farq trigger 'ushr.
This is a form of qiyas (analogy) based on the standard nisab of five wasq for grains.
3
Apply the principle to honey
Once you know the farq is the largest measure, the condition for 'ushr on honey is reaching five farq. If the honey is less than five farq, no 'ushr is due.
Other scholars may use different measures, but this is the Hanafi position according to Imam Muhammad.
4
Analyze the kharaj land exemption
Kharaj land is already subject to kharaj tax. The Shari'ah does not impose both kharaj and 'ushr on the same land to avoid double taxation. Therefore, its produce is exempt from 'ushr.
This ruling is based on rational analogy (dalil 'aqli) and is agreed upon in the Hanafi school.
5
Contrast the two cases
Compare: on 'ushr land, produce is subject to 'ushr; on kharaj land, only kharaj is levied. Honey from any land is subject to 'ushr when it reaches nisab, unless the land is kharaji (but honey is not land produce in the same sense).
Note that honey is not a land tax but a produce tax, so it is treated separately.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاع کے وزن میں اختلاف ہے۔ آٹھ رطل کا صاع ہوتا ہے جو حنفیہ کے نزدیک مروج ہے۔ اور پانچ رطل اور ایک تہائی رمل کا صاع ہوتا ہے جو دوسرے ائمہ کے نزدیک مروج ہے۔ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ شہد کو ناپنے کا زیادہ سے زیادہ بڑا پیمانہ فرق ہے۔ اس لئے پانچ فرق ہو جائے تو عشر لازم ہوگا۔ امام محمد اپنے پرانے اصول پر گئے ہیں کہ جس چیز کو وسق سے نہیں ناپتے ہیں اس میں یہ دیکھیں کہ ان کو ناپنے کا بڑا پیمانہ کیا ہے؟ اگر اس بڑے پیمانے سے پانچ پیمانے ہو جائیں تو اس پر عشر لازم ہوگا۔ اور شہد کو ناپنے کا بڑا پیمانہ فرق ہے، اس لئے پانچ فرق ہو گا تو عشر لازم ہو گا۔ [۵۱۲] (۱۱) اور خراجی زمین کی پیداوار میں عشر نہیں ہے۔ خراجی زمین میں خراج لازم ہوتا ہے۔ اب اس پر عشر لازم کریں تو مونت دوگنی ہو جائے گی اور شریعت ایک زمین پر دو مرتبہ خراج یا عشر وصول نہیں کرتی۔ اس لئے زمین کی پیداوار میں عشر لازم نہیں ہے۔ صرف خراج لازم ہوگا۔
There is disagreement about the weight of the sa'. The sa' is 8 ratls, which is prevalent among the Hanafis. And the sa' is 5 and one-third ratls, which is prevalent among other imams. Imam Muhammad says that the largest measuring vessel for honey is the farq. Therefore, if it reaches five farq, 'ushr becomes obligatory. Imam Muhammad follows his earlier principle that for things not measured by wasq, one looks at their largest measuring vessel; if it reaches five of those measures, 'ushr becomes obligatory. And the largest measure for honey is the farq, so if it reaches five farq, 'ushr becomes obligatory. [512] (11) And there is no 'ushr on the produce of kharaj land. Kharaj is obligatory on kharaj land. If 'ushr were also levied, the burden would be doubled, and the Shari'ah does not collect both kharaj and 'ushr twice on one land. Therefore, 'ushr is not obligatory on its produce; only kharaj is obligatory.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings related to 'ushr (the tithe on agricultural produce). First, it discusses the measure for honey according to Imam Muhammad. There is a known difference among schools regarding the weight of the sa', but here the focus is on the principle for items not measured by wasq (a standard measure). Imam Muhammad argues that for such items, one uses the largest customary measure; for honey, that is the farq, so five farq trigger 'ushr. Second, the passage states that land subject to kharaj (a land tax) is not subject to 'ushr. The reasoning is that the Shari'ah does not impose two taxes on the same land, as that would cause undue hardship. This is a clear ruling based on rational analogy (dalil 'aqli).

Key Terms
صاع (ṣā‘): A unit of volume for measuring agricultural produce; its weight differs: 8 ratls (Hanafi) or 5⅓ ratls (others).
فرق (farq): A large measuring vessel used for honey; one farq equals a specific volume (not defined here).
خراجی زمین (kharājī zamīn): Land subject to kharaj tax, typically conquered lands where the original owners retain the land but pay tax.

Abrogation of Mu'allafatu Qulubihim from Zakat
Lists eight zakat recipients and discusses abrogation of one category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that mu'allafatu qulubihim is abrogated as a zakat recipient and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'is.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school rules mu'allafatu qulubihim abrogated; only seven categories remain.

The Quran (9:60) enumerates eight categories of zakat recipients. The Hanafi school, however, holds that one category—mu'allafatu qulubihim—is no longer valid because Islam became strong and no longer needs to win hearts. This lesson unpacks the proof from the practice of Abu Bakr (ra) and the resulting difference with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight categories from the verse
Read the Quranic verse (9:60) and list the eight categories exactly as mentioned.
The verse is explicitly quoted in the source text.
2
Note the Hanafi claim of abrogation
The text states that mu'allafatu qulubihim 'has fallen away' and explains the reason: Allah honored Islam and made it independent.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof cited is an athar from 'Amir that the category existed in the Prophet's time but ceased under Abu Bakr (ra). This is a sunnah-based abrogation.
The dalil is not from the Quran itself but from practice.
4
State the opposing school position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the verse has not been abrogated and mu'allafatu qulubihim remains a valid category.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis cannot give zakat to non-Muslims to incline them; Shafi'is can do so under certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الله تعالى انما الصدقات للفقراء والمساكين الآية فهذه ثمانية اصناف فقد سقط منها المؤلفة قلوبهم لان الله تعالى اعز الاسلام واغنى عنهم والفقير من له ادنى شيء والمسكين من لا شيء له باب من يجوز دفع الصدقۃ اليه ومن لا يجوز ضروری نوٹ کن لوگوں کو زکوۃ دینا جائز ہے جس سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہوگی اس کی پوری تفصیل ہے۔ ۱۳ (۱) اللہ تعالی نے فرمایا انما الصدقات للفقراء والمساكين والعاملين عليها والمؤلفة قلوبهم و في الرقاب والغارمين و في سبيل الله وابن السبيل فريضة من الله والله عليم حکیم (الف ) ( آیت ۶۰ سورۃ التوبۃ ۹ ) اس آیت میں آٹھ قسم کے آدمیوں کو مستحق زکوۃ قرار دیا ہے۔ [۵۱۴] (۲) ان میں سے مؤلفت قلوب ساقط ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالی نے اسلام کو عزت دی اور مؤلفت قلوب سے اسلام کو بے نیاز کر دیا تشر مؤلفت قلوب اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ کافر کوزکوۃ کا روپیہ دے کر اس کو دین اسلام کی طرف مائل کیا جائے۔ شروع اسلام میں یہ جائز تھا لیکن بعد میں یہ قسم منسوخ ہوگئی۔ اس لئے کہ اب اسلام کو اللہ نے عزت دیدی۔ اب مؤلفت قلوب کو زکوۃ دینا حنفیہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔ یہ اثر ہے عن عامر قال انما كانت المؤلفة قلوبهم على عهد رسول الله الا الله فلما ولی ابو بکر انقطعت (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۱۴۵ء في المؤلفة قلوبهم يوجدون الیوم او ذهبواج ثمانی ص ۴۳۵ نمبر ۱۰۷۵۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ابو بکر کے زمانے میں مؤلفت قلوب کا حق ساقط ہو گیا۔ [۵۱۵] (۳) فقیر اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جس کے پاس کوئی چیز نہ ہو۔ کسی کے پاس کچھ مال ہو لیکن نصاب کے برابر نہ ہو تو اس کو فقیر کہتے ہیں۔ اس کے خلاف بھی فقیر کی تفسیر ہے کہ جس کے پاس کچھ بھی نہ ہواس کو فقیر کہتے ہیں۔ [۵۱۶) (۴) اور مسکین اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کے پاس کچھ بھی نہ ہو۔ جس کے پاس کچھ مال نہ ہو اس کو مسکین کہتے ہیں۔ [۵۱۷) (۵) اور عامل کو امام دے گا اگر عمل کیا ہو اس کے عمل کے مطابق۔ حاشیہ : (الف) زکوۃ صرف (۱) فقراء (۲) مساکین (۳) زکوۃ پر کام کرنے والے (۴) مؤلفت قلوب (۵) مکاتب غلام کی گردن چھڑانے (۶) مقروض ( ۷ ) جو اللہ کے راستے میں جہاد میں ہو (۸) اور مسافر کے لئے ہے۔ یہ فرض ہے اللہ کی جانب سے اور اللہ جانے والا حکمت والا ہے (ب ) حضرت عامر نے فرمایا مولفہ قلوب حضور کے زمانے میں تھا۔ پس جب حضرت ابو بکر والی بنے تو مؤلفہ قلوب ساقط ہو گئے۔
Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed the charitable contributions are only for the poor and the needy...' So these are eight categories. The category of 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' has fallen away because Allah has honored Islam and made it independent of them. The faqir is one who has the least thing. The miskin is one who has nothing. Chapter: Who is permissible to give sadaqah to and who is not. Essential note: A full explanation of to whom zakah may be given so that zakah is discharged. 13 (1) Allah said: 'Indeed the charitable contributions are only for the poor, the needy, those employed to collect it, those whose hearts are to be reconciled, for freeing necks, the indebted, in the way of Allah, and the traveler – an obligation from Allah, and Allah is Knowing, Wise.' [Surah al-Tawbah 9:60] In this verse, eight types of people are designated as deserving of zakah. [514] (2) Among them, the mu'allafatu qulubihim has been dropped because Allah has honored Islam and made it independent of them. Mu'allafatu qulubihim means giving zakah money to a disbeliever to incline him towards Islam. This was permissible in early Islam, but later this category was abrogated because Allah has honored Islam. Now giving zakah to mu'allaf is not permissible according to the Hanafis. There is an athar from 'Amir who said: 'Mu'allafatu qulubihim existed in the time of the Messenger of Allah, then when Abu Bakr became caliph, it ceased.' [Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah] From this athar, it is known that in the time of Abu Bakr, the right of mu'allafatu qulubihim was dropped. [515] (3) The faqir is one who has nothing. If someone has some wealth but less than nisab, he is called faqir. There is also an interpretation that the faqir is one who has nothing at all. [516] (4) And the miskin is one who has nothing at all. One who has no wealth is called miskin. [517] (5) And the 'amil (collector) will be given by the Imam according to his work. Footnote (a): Zakah is only for (1) poor (2) needy (3) those working on zakah (4) mu'allafatu qulubihim (5) freeing the neck of a mukatib slave (6) indebted (7) those in the way of Allah in jihad (8) and the traveler. This is an obligation from Allah, and Allah is Knowing, Wise. (b) Hadrat 'Amir said: 'Mu'allafatu qulubihim existed in the time of the Prophet. Then when Hadrat Abu Bakr became caliph, the mu'allafatu qulubihim ceased.'
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on who is eligible to receive zakah. The author begins by quoting the Quranic verse (9:60) which lists eight categories of recipients: the poor, the needy, the collectors, those whose hearts are to be reconciled (mu'allafatu qulubihim), for freeing slaves, the indebted, in the way of Allah, and the traveler. Then the commentary explains that the category of mu'allafatu qulubihim is considered abrogated because after Islam became strong, there was no need to win over disbelievers with zakah. This is the Hanafi position, supported by an athar from 'Amir stating that Abu Bakr discontinued this practice. The passage then discusses the definitions of faqir and miskin, but presents two conflicting interpretations: one from the Arabic matn (faqir has the least, miskin has nothing) and the Urdu commentary that sometimes reverses them. The relied-upon Hanafi view is that faqir is one who has nothing (or less than nisab) and miskin is one who has something but not enough, though there is ikhtilaf among scholars. Finally, the 'amil (zakah collector) receives his due from the Imam according to his work.

Key Terms
مؤلفة قلوبهم (mu'allafatu qulūbihim): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled; originally non-Muslims given zakah to incline them to Islam.
صدقات (ṣadaqāt): In this context, obligatory zakah (the verse uses 'ṣadaqāt' to mean the obligatory charity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the category of mu'allafatu qulubihim dropped from zakat recipients?
A) Because the Quranic verse was abrogated
B) Because Allah honored Islam and made it independent of them
C) Because there are no longer any disbelievers
D) Because the Prophet forbade it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that mu'allafatu qulubihim is abrogated as a zakat recipient due to the strength of Islam and the practice of Abu Bakr.

Defining Faqir and Miskin: Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Lists eight zakat recipients and discusses abrogation of one category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conflicting definitions of faqir and miskin within the Hanafi school and apply the more common fatwa position.

Core Idea
Which definition you choose for faqir and miskin changes who gets your zakat.

Zakat requires giving to the correct recipients. The categories 'faqir' (poor) and 'miskin' (needy) are well-known, but their precise definitions vary. This lesson examines the two main interpretations within the Hanafi school: one from the matn (Arabic) and another from later commentary.

Guided Path
1
Read the two definitions given in the text
The Arabic matn says: 'al-faqiru man lahu adna shay'in, wa al-misku man la shay'a lahu' (the poor is one who has the least thing, the needy is one who has nothing).
This is the first definition.
2
Note the contradictory commentary
The Urdu commentary states: 'faqir is one who has nothing' and 'miskin is one who has nothing' but also offers an opposite view: some say faqir has nothing, miskin has something but less than nisab.
There is clear ikhtilaf.
3
Identify the more common Hanafi fatwa position
In Hanafi fatwa manuals (e.g., Radd al-Muhtar), the reputed view is that faqir has nothing, and miskin has some property but less than nisab. However, the definition is also reversed in some sources.
You need to know the mufta bihi in your region or text.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a person with less than nisab, decide if he is faqir or miskin based on the two definitions.

Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed the charitable contributions are only for the poor and the needy...' So these are eight categories. The category of 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' has fallen away because Allah has honored Islam and made it independent of them. The faqir is one who has the least thing. The miskin is one who has nothing. Chapter: Who is permissible to give sadaqah to and who is not. Essential note: A full explanation of to whom zakah may be given so that zakah is discharged. 13 (1) Allah said: 'Indeed the charitable contributions are only for the poor, the needy, those employed to collect it, those whose hearts are to be reconciled, for freeing necks, the indebted, in the way of Allah, and the traveler – an obligation from Allah, and Allah is Knowing, Wise.' [Surah al-Tawbah 9:60] In this verse, eight types of people are designated as deserving of zakah. [514] (2) Among them, the mu'allafatu qulubihim has been dropped because Allah has honored Islam and made it independent of them. Mu'allafatu qulubihim means giving zakah money to a disbeliever to incline him towards Islam. This was permissible in early Islam, but later this category was abrogated because Allah has honored Islam. Now giving zakah to mu'allaf is not permissible according to the Hanafis. There is an athar from 'Amir who said: 'Mu'allafatu qulubihim existed in the time of the Messenger of Allah, then when Abu Bakr became caliph, it ceased.' [Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah] From this athar, it is known that in the time of Abu Bakr, the right of mu'allafatu qulubihim was dropped. [515] (3) The faqir is one who has nothing. If someone has some wealth but less than nisab, he is called faqir. There is also an interpretation that the faqir is one who has nothing at all. [516] (4) And the miskin is one who has nothing at all. One who has no wealth is called miskin. [517] (5) And the 'amil (collector) will be given by the Imam according to his work. Footnote (a): Zakah is only for (1) poor (2) needy (3) those working on zakah (4) mu'allafatu qulubihim (5) freeing the neck of a mukatib slave (6) indebted (7) those in the way of Allah in jihad (8) and the traveler. This is an obligation from Allah, and Allah is Knowing, Wise. (b) Hadrat 'Amir said: 'Mu'allafatu qulubihim existed in the time of the Prophet. Then when Hadrat Abu Bakr became caliph, the mu'allafatu qulubihim ceased.'
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on who is eligible to receive zakah. The author begins by quoting the Quranic verse (9:60) which lists eight categories of recipients: the poor, the needy, the collectors, those whose hearts are to be reconciled (mu'allafatu qulubihim), for freeing slaves, the indebted, in the way of Allah, and the traveler. Then the commentary explains that the category of mu'allafatu qulubihim is considered abrogated because after Islam became strong, there was no need to win over disbelievers with zakah. This is the Hanafi position, supported by an athar from 'Amir stating that Abu Bakr discontinued this practice. The passage then discusses the definitions of faqir and miskin, but presents two conflicting interpretations: one from the Arabic matn (faqir has the least, miskin has nothing) and the Urdu commentary that sometimes reverses them. The relied-upon Hanafi view is that faqir is one who has nothing (or less than nisab) and miskin is one who has something but not enough, though there is ikhtilaf among scholars. Finally, the 'amil (zakah collector) receives his due from the Imam according to his work.

Key Terms
فقير (faqīr): A poor person; text says one who has the least thing (Arabic) or nothing (Urdu commentary).
مسكين (miskīn): A needy person; text says one who has nothing (Arabic) or one who has nothing (Urdu).
عامل (ʿāmil): The person employed to collect zakat; the Imam gives him his due according to his work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One who has nothing at all
B) One who has less than nisab
C) One who has the least thing
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The definitions of faqir and miskin in the Hanafi school are not monolithic; the mufta bihi often gives priority to the more destitute.

The Eight Categories of Zakat Recipients
Definitions of gharim, ibn al-sabil, and fi sabilillah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight categories of zakat recipients, define each category, and apply the conditions for eligibility.

Core Idea
Zakat must be given to a needy Muslim from one of the eight specified categories.

The Quran in Surah at-Tawbah (9:60) specifies eight categories of people who are eligible to receive zakat. Understanding these categories is essential for fulfilling the obligation of zakat correctly. In this lesson, we will explore each category, its definition, and the conditions that make a person eligible.

Guided Path
1
Memorise the eight categories
The Quran names eight categories: fuqara (poor), masakin (needy), 'amilun (collectors), mu'allafatu qulubuhum (those whose hearts are to be reconciled), fi riqab (slaves/freeing captives), gharimun (debtors), fi sabilillah (wayfarers in the path of Allah), ibn al-sabil (stranded travelers). Commit these to memory.
Some variations exist in English translations; focus on the Arabic terms.
2
Define each category with conditions
For each category, understand the specific conditions that make a person eligible. For example, gharim is a debtor who has no wealth beyond basic needs and nisab. Ibn al-sabil is a traveler whose wealth is at home and is in need. Fi sabilillah refers to those stranded from jihad or other good works.
The commentary elaborates on gharim and ibn al-sabil.
3
Distinguish between similar categories
Some categories may appear similar, e.g., fuqara and masakin (both poor), but fuqara are generally considered more needy. Gharim and ibn al-sabil are different: gharim has debt at home, ibn al-sabil is away from home. Understand the distinctions.
These nuances affect who you choose to give to.
4
Apply to real-life scenarios
Given a description of a person, determine which zakat category they belong to. For example, a person with a large debt but no extra wealth is gharim. A traveler stranded without money is ibn al-sabil.
Practice makes this intuitive.

غازیوں اور مجاہدوں کے پیچھے جو لوگ رہ گئے ہوں ان کو منقطع الغزاة کہتے ہیں۔ اور ان کو بھی زکوۃ کا مال دیگر امداد کرنا جائز ہے۔ [۵۲۱] (۹) ابن السبیل، جس کا مال اس کے وطن میں ہو اور وہ دوسری جگہ میں ہو اور وہاں اس کے لئے کچھ نہ ہو۔ ابن السبیل : راستے کا بیٹا یعنی مسافر، جس کے گھر میں مال نصاب ہو لیکن اس کے پاس ابھی کچھ نہ ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ کا مال دیا جاسکتا ہے۔ تا کہ وہ گھر تک پہنچ جائے۔
[۵۲۲] (۱۰) مالک کے لئے جائز ہے کہ زکوۃ کے ہر صنف والوں کو دے۔ اور اس کے لئے یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ ایک قسم پر اکتفا کرے۔
آیت میں آٹھ قسموں کو زکوۃ دینے کا تذکرہ کیا ہے۔ لیکن اگر ایک قسم کو تمام زکوۃ دیدے تب بھی زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ اس اثر میں ہے عن حذيفة قال اذا اعطاها في صنف واحد من الاصناف الثمانية التي سمى الله تعالى اجزأه (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیسته ۸۵، ما قالوا فی الرجل اذا وضع الصدقة فی صنف واحد ج ثانی ص ۴۰۵ نمبر ۱۰۴۴۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک قسم کو بھی زکوۃ دی دیگا تو کافی ہو جائیگا۔ فاند امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ آیت میں جمع کا صیغہ ہے اس لئے کم از کم تین آدمی ہونے چاہئے۔ اور ہر قسموں کو انما کے ذریعہ گھیرا ہے اس لئے تمام قسموں کو زکوۃ دے، اور ہر قسم کے تین تین آدمیوں کو دے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ قرآن نے ان قسموں کو بیان کیا کہ یہ سب مصرف ہیں۔
چاہے کبھی کو دیں چاہے کسی ایک کو بقدر ضرورت دیں۔ البتہ ضرورت سے زائد کسی ایک کو اتنادیں کہ وہ مالدار بن جائیں یہ مکروہ ہے۔ [۵۲۳] (۱۱) نہیں جائز ہے کہ زکوۃ ذمی کو دے، اور نہ اس سے مسجد بنائے ، اور نہ اس سے میت کو کفن دے، اور نہ اس سے غلام خریدے جس کو آزاد کیا جائے۔ (۱) زکوۃ کا کسی غریب مسلمان کو مالک بنانا ضروری ہے۔ کسی کافر کوزکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح کسی غریب کو یا
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حذیفہ سے منقول ہیں کہ اگر آٹھ قسموں میں سے ایک قسم کو دے دیا جس کا اللہ نے نام لیا ہے تو اس کو کافی ہو جائے گا۔
The commentary explains that the zakat collector is paid according to his work from zakat funds, and that paying zakat to the Ahl al-Bayt and their freed slaves is disliked but permissible based on hadith evidence. It then defines the categories of zakat recipients: gharim (debtor), fi sabilillah (those cut off from military expeditions), and ibn al-sabil (wayfarer). It states that the owner may give zakat to all categories or restrict to one category, and it is not permissible to give zakat to a dhimmi or to use it to build a mosque. The text includes a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i who required distribution among all eight categories with at least three persons each, but the Hanafi position holds that giving to one category suffices.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the eight categories of zakat recipients (asnaf al-zakah). It begins by discussing the payment of the zakat collector ('amil) and the category of 'riqab' (freeing slaves), specifically helping the mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom). It then provides hadith evidence that the Ahl al-Bayt and their freed slaves should not receive zakat as a wage, though taking it is still permissible. The commentary then defines the remaining categories: gharim (debtor who cannot pay his debt after meeting basic needs), fi sabilillah (those stranded from participating in jihad), and ibn al-sabil (a traveler whose wealth is at home and is in need). After listing the eight categories, the text addresses the permissibility of giving all zakat to one category versus distributing among all. It cites an athar from Hudhayfa that giving to one category suffices, and then contrasts the Shafi'i view, which requires at least three recipients from each of the eight categories. The Hanafi position is that since the Quran merely states the categories as eligible recipients, the owner may choose to give to one or all, as long as the recipient is in need. However, it is makruh to give so much that the recipient becomes wealthy. Finally, the text rules that zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) and cannot be used to build mosques, shroud the dead, or purchase slaves for emancipation, because zakat must be given as ownership to a needy Muslim.

Key Terms
غارم (ghārim): A debtor who cannot pay his debt and has no wealth beyond his basic needs and nisab.
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabīl): A traveler who is in need even though he has wealth back home; he is given zakat to enable his return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following describes a person eligible to receive zakat as ibn al-sabil?
A) A person who is poor and has no wealth at home.
B) A person traveling who has no money with him, even though he has wealth at home.
C) A person who is in debt and has no money.
D) A person who is collecting zakat on behalf of the state.

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given to a needy Muslim from one of the eight specified categories, and each category has its own conditions.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
12 min
Giving Zakat to One Category is Sufficient
Dispute over whether zakat must be distributed among all eight categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that giving all zakat to one eligible category is valid, and critically evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
You may give your entire zakat to one eligible person or category; distribution among all eight is not required.

The Quran lists eight categories of zakat recipients, but does it require that we give to all of them? The Hanafi school says no: the verse identifies eligible types, not a mandatory distribution. This lesson examines the evidence for each view and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The owner may give all his zakat to one category (e.g., all to the poor) or to any number of categories. The proofs: the athar of Hudhayfa and the fact that the Quran merely mentions categories as eligible.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that 'innama' in the verse indicates limitation, so zakat must be given to all eight categories, with at least three recipients per category.
This is based on the usul principle that 'innama' restricts the ruling to those mentioned.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the verse indicates the categories of eligible recipients but does not impose distribution. The athar of Hudhayfa (companion) supports giving to one category.
The athar from Hudhayfa is considered strong evidence by Hanafis.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Hanafi: You may give your entire zakat to one poor person if that person is eligible. Shafi'i: You must give to at least three persons from each of the eight categories, total 24 recipients.
This has major implications for ease of fulfilling zakat.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the eight categories of zakat recipients (asnaf al-zakah). It begins by discussing the payment of the zakat collector ('amil) and the category of 'riqab' (freeing slaves), specifically helping the mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom). It then provides hadith evidence that the Ahl al-Bayt and their freed slaves should not receive zakat as a wage, though taking it is still permissible. The commentary then defines the remaining categories: gharim (debtor who cannot pay his debt after meeting basic needs), fi sabilillah (those stranded from participating in jihad), and ibn al-sabil (a traveler whose wealth is at home and is in need). After listing the eight categories, the text addresses the permissibility of giving all zakat to one category versus distributing among all. It cites an athar from Hudhayfa that giving to one category suffices, and then contrasts the Shafi'i view, which requires at least three recipients from each of the eight categories. The Hanafi position is that since the Quran merely states the categories as eligible recipients, the owner may choose to give to one or all, as long as the recipient is in need. However, it is makruh to give so much that the recipient becomes wealthy. Finally, the text rules that zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) and cannot be used to build mosques, shroud the dead, or purchase slaves for emancipation, because zakat must be given as ownership to a needy Muslim.

Key Terms
إنما (innamā): A particle of restriction (hasr) meaning 'only' or 'but'. In the verse, it limits zakat to the eight categories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it sufficient to give all zakat to a single poor person?
A) No, you must give to at least three poor people.
B) Yes, because the poor are one of the eight categories, and giving to one person of that category is valid.
C) No, you must give to all eight categories.
D) Yes, but only if you give to a traveler.

Key Takeaway
Giving all zakat to one eligible category is valid in the Hanafi school, based on the athar of Hudhayfa.

beginner
8 min
Prohibited Recipients and Uses of Zakat
List of prohibited recipients and uses of zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify to whom and for what purposes zakat cannot be given, and apply the rulings in practical cases.

Core Idea
Zakat must be given as ownership (tamlik) to a needy Muslim; it cannot be given to non-Muslims or used for public works.

The zakat payment is not just a charitable donation; it has specific rules about who can receive it and how it can be used. The text explicitly prohibits giving zakat to dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens) and using zakat funds to build mosques, shroud the dead, or purchase slaves for emancipation. Let's explore the rationale and applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited recipients
The text says it is not permissible (la yajuz) to give zakat to a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Muslim protection). This is because zakat is a purification for Muslims and must be given to a Muslim.
Some later Hanafis allow giving to dhimmis in need if there is a maslaha, but the classical position is prohibition.
2
Identify the prohibited uses
Zakat cannot be used to build a mosque, to give a funeral shroud (kafan), or to purchase a slave for emancipation. The reason is that zakat requires tamlik (giving ownership) of the money to a poor Muslim. Using it for construction or services does not involve ownership transfer.
This is a fundamental principle: zakat must be given as ownership, not as a benefit or use.
3
Understand the rationale
Zakat is defined as giving ownership of a specific portion to a needy Muslim. Non-Muslims do not qualify for purification, and building mosques is a public benefit, not a personal ownership. Thus, the obligation is not fulfilled if zakat is used these ways.
The act of giving must be tamlik (transfer of ownership) to a specific eligible individual.
4
Apply to practical scenarios
For example, if a person uses his zakat money to build a mosque, his zakat is not paid; he must still give zakat separately. Similarly, if he buys a shroud for a deceased poor person, it does not count.
Exceptions exist for certain services like paying a zakat collector, but that is a specific category (al-'amilun).

چاہے کبھی کو دیں چاہے کسی ایک کو بقدر ضرورت دیں۔ البتہ ضرورت سے زائد کسی ایک کو اتنادیں کہ وہ مالدار بن جائیں یہ مکروہ ہے۔ [۵۲۳] (۱۱) نہیں جائز ہے کہ زکوۃ ذمی کو دے، اور نہ اس سے مسجد بنائے ، اور نہ اس سے میت کو کفن دے، اور نہ اس سے غلام خریدے جس کو آزاد کیا جائے۔ (۱) زکوۃ کا کسی غریب مسلمان کو مالک بنانا ضروری ہے۔ کسی کافر کوزکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح کسی غریب کو یا
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حذیفہ سے منقول ہیں کہ اگر آٹھ قسموں میں سے ایک قسم کو دے دیا جس کا اللہ نے نام لیا ہے تو اس کو کافی ہو جائے گا۔
The commentary explains that the zakat collector is paid according to his work from zakat funds, and that paying zakat to the Ahl al-Bayt and their freed slaves is disliked but permissible based on hadith evidence. It then defines the categories of zakat recipients: gharim (debtor), fi sabilillah (those cut off from military expeditions), and ibn al-sabil (wayfarer). It states that the owner may give zakat to all categories or restrict to one category, and it is not permissible to give zakat to a dhimmi or to use it to build a mosque. The text includes a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i who required distribution among all eight categories with at least three persons each, but the Hanafi position holds that giving to one category suffices.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the eight categories of zakat recipients (asnaf al-zakah). It begins by discussing the payment of the zakat collector ('amil) and the category of 'riqab' (freeing slaves), specifically helping the mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom). It then provides hadith evidence that the Ahl al-Bayt and their freed slaves should not receive zakat as a wage, though taking it is still permissible. The commentary then defines the remaining categories: gharim (debtor who cannot pay his debt after meeting basic needs), fi sabilillah (those stranded from participating in jihad), and ibn al-sabil (a traveler whose wealth is at home and is in need). After listing the eight categories, the text addresses the permissibility of giving all zakat to one category versus distributing among all. It cites an athar from Hudhayfa that giving to one category suffices, and then contrasts the Shafi'i view, which requires at least three recipients from each of the eight categories. The Hanafi position is that since the Quran merely states the categories as eligible recipients, the owner may choose to give to one or all, as long as the recipient is in need. However, it is makruh to give so much that the recipient becomes wealthy. Finally, the text rules that zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) and cannot be used to build mosques, shroud the dead, or purchase slaves for emancipation, because zakat must be given as ownership to a needy Muslim.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim citizen living under Muslim rule with a covenant of protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, is it permissible to give zakat to a dhimmi?
A) Yes, it is permissible.
B) No, it is not permissible.
C) It is permissible only if the dhimmi is poor.
D) It is permissible only for dhimmi family members.

Key Takeaway
Zakat cannot be given to non-Muslims or used for public facilities; it must be given as ownership to a needy Muslim.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Zakat to a Single Category: Hanafi Permissibility
Ruling on zakat distribution with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving all zakat to one category and explain the difference with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Giving all zakat to one eligible category is valid; the Quran's list indicates eligibility, not mandatory distribution.

The eight categories of zakat recipients are well-known from Quran 9:60. A common question is whether a payer must distribute among all eight or may give to just one. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi view, which allows restriction to a single category, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i requirement of distribution to all eight.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify that the matn allows the payer to either give to each category or restrict to one. The commentator affirms this with the athar of Hudhayfa.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) and the obligation is fulfilled even with one category.
2
Identify the Shafi'i Objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the Quranic verse uses plural forms and the restrictive particle 'innama', requiring distribution to all eight categories, with at least three recipients per category (since the plural minimum is three).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
3
Follow the Proof of Each School
Hanafi proof: athar of Hudhayfa (companion saying that giving to one category suffices). Shafi'i proof: the verse's wording ('innama' and plural).
The Hanafi dalil is a qawl sahabi, which is a source of law in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
Hanafis respond that 'innama' restricts eligibility to these categories but does not mandate distribution; the plural defines types, not obligatory allocation. The athar explicitly supports sufficiency with one category.
The response is based on the distinction between conditions of eligibility and conditions of distribution.
5
Determine the Practical Difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi may give all zakat to one category (e.g., all to fuqara), while a Shafi'i must divide among eight categories, with at least three from each.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position, as supported by the athar and later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمالك ان يدفع الى كل واحد منهم وله ان يقتصر على صنف واحد [۵۲۳] (۱۰) مالک کے لئے جائز ہے کہ زکوۃ کے ہر صنف والوں کو دے۔ اور اس کے لئے یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ ایک قسم پر اکتفا کرے۔
آیت میں آٹھ قسموں کو زکوۃ دینے کا تذکرہ کیا ہے۔ لیکن اگر ایک قسم کو تمام زکوۃ دیدے تب بھی زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ اس اثر میں ہے عن حذيفة قال اذا اعطاها في صنف واحد من الاصناف الثمانية التي سمى الله تعالى اجزأه (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیسته ۸۵، ما قالوا فی الرجل اذا وضع الصدقة فی صنف واحد ج ثانی ص ۴۰۵ نمبر ۱۰۴۴۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک قسم کو بھی زکوۃ دی دیگا تو کافی ہو جائیگا۔ فاند امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ آیت میں جمع کا صیغہ ہے اس لئے کم از کم تین آدمی ہونے چاہئے۔ اور ہر قسموں کو انما کے ذریعہ گھیرا ہے اس لئے تمام قسموں کو زکوۃ دے، اور ہر قسم کے تین تین آدمیوں کو دے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ قرآن نے ان قسموں کو بیان کیا کہ یہ سب مصرف ہیں۔
چاہے کبھی کو دیں چاہے کسی ایک کو بقدر ضرورت دیں۔ البتہ ضرورت سے زائد کسی ایک کو اتنادیں کہ وہ مالدار بن جائیں یہ مکروہ ہے۔
It is permissible for the owner to give to each one of them, and it is permissible for him to restrict [it] to one category. (10) It is permissible for the owner to give to every category of zakat, and it is also permissible for him to content himself with one type. The verse mentioned eight categories for giving zakat. But if he gives all the zakat to one type, the payment of zakat will still be valid. In this effect, it is narrated from Hudhayfa: he said, 'If he gives it to one category from the eight categories that Allah the Exalted named, it suffices him.' (Source: Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 85) This effect shows that giving zakat to one category is sufficient. As for Imam al-Shafi'i, he said that the verse uses a plural form, so at least three people must be [from each category?], and the word 'innama' restricts it to those categories, so he must give to all categories, and to three people from each category. We say: The Quran mentioned these categories to indicate that they are all recipients. Whether one gives [to any] at times, or gives to a single person to the extent of his need. However, giving to one person in excess of his need to the point that he becomes wealthy is disliked (makruh).
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on distributing zakat among the eight eligible categories. The matn states that the payer may either give to each category or restrict to one. The commentator expands on this, citing an athar from Hudhayfa that giving all zakat to one category suffices. He then contrasts the Shafi'i position: Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the Quranic verse (9:60) uses a plural and the restrictive particle 'innama', implying distribution to all eight categories, with at least three recipients per category (since the plural minimum is three). The Hanafi response is that the verse merely lists eligibility; 'innama' restricts zakat to these types of recipients, not to a specific distribution. The commentator adds that while giving to one category is valid, giving excessively to one person to make him wealthy is makruh. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.

Key Terms
صنف (sinf): A category among the eight recipients of zakat as mentioned in Quran 9:60.
مصرف (masrif): An eligible recipient category or individual for zakat distribution.
إجزاء (ijza'): Sufficiency; the act of paying zakat to one category suffices and fulfills the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person gives all his zakat to a single category of the eight eligible categories?
A) It is invalid and must be redistributed.
B) It is permissible and suffices, but giving to one person excessively to make him wealthy is disliked.
C) It is obligatory to give to all eight categories.
D) It is only valid if given to three individuals from that category.

Key Takeaway
Giving all zakat to a single eligible category is valid in the Hanafi school; the Quranic list defines eligibility, not mandatory distribution.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Prohibited Uses of Zakat and Permissibility of Optional Charity to Non-Muslims
Rulings with proofs on prohibited zakat uses and permission of optional charity to dhimmis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify prohibited recipients and uses of zakat funds according to the Hanafi school and explain the underlying principle of tamlik (ownership transfer).

Core Idea
Zakat must be given into the ownership of a poor Muslim; all other uses are invalid.

Zakat is a prescribed charity with specific rules about who may receive it and how it may be used. The Hanafi school holds that the core requirement is tamlik – making a poor Muslim the owner of the zakat payment. This lesson examines the prohibited uses listed in the text and the evidence that supports them, then distinguishes between zakat and optional charity.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibited uses
Identify each of the five prohibited uses mentioned in the passage: giving to a dhimmi, building a mosque, shrouding a deceased, purchasing a slave for emancipation, and giving to a wealthy person.
These are all considered invalid because they do not result in tamlik.
2
Identify the underlying principle
The commentator explains that the common flaw in all these cases is the absence of making a poor Muslim owner. For each case, explain why tamlik fails.
e.g., a mosque has no owner, a deceased cannot own, etc.
3
Analyze the primary dalil
Examine the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Allah has prescribed upon them a charity taken from their wealthy and returned to their poor.' Identify the key phrase and how it proves the ruling.
The hadith restricts zakat to the poor of the Muslims.
4
Examine supporting athar
Review the athar from al-Thawri which explicitly lists impermissible uses, confirming the principle.
This athar is cited as corroboration.
5
Distinguish zakat from optional charity
Contrast the strict rules for zakat with the permissibility of giving optional charity (sadaqah tatawwu') to non-Muslims, especially for family ties. Use the hadith of Asma.
This distinction shows that the prohibition is specific to zakat.

It is not permissible to give zakat to a dhimmi, nor to build a mosque with it, nor to shroud a deceased person with it, nor to purchase a slave for emancipation with it, nor is it given to a wealthy person. ... (2) From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said to Mu'adh ibn Jabal: 'Indeed, Allah has prescribed upon them a charity taken from their wealthy and returned to their poor.' (Bukhari) This hadith indicates that zakat is taken from wealthy Muslims and distributed to poor Muslims. Therefore, giving zakat to a non-Muslim is not permissible. (3) This effect supports all the above issues: From al-Thawri: 'A man should not give his zakat to someone whom he is obliged to support among his relatives, nor should he give it for a shroud of a deceased, nor for a debt of a deceased, nor for building a mosque, nor for purchasing a mushaf, nor for performing hajj with it, nor to his mukatib, nor to purchase a slave for emancipation, nor to Jews and Christians, nor should he hire someone with it to carry it from one place to another.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This hadith supports all the above rulings. (4) The verse with 'innama' restricts [zakat] to eight categories, meaning that zakat is only fulfilled by giving to these eight categories. It is necessary to make a poor Muslim owner [of the zakat]. It is permissible to give optional charity to a dhimmi. From Asma: 'My mother came to me seeking something during the time of Quraysh while she was displeased and a polytheist. I said, O Messenger of Allah, my mother has come to me while she is displeased and a polytheist. Shall I maintain ties with her? He said: Yes, maintain ties with your mother.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that it is permissible to give optional charity to a polytheist for maintaining family ties. [524] (12) Zakat should not be given to a wealthy person.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage lists several prohibited uses of zakat funds and provides evidence. The commentator first states the ruling: zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi, used for building a mosque, for a shroud, for purchasing a slave for emancipation, or to a wealthy person. The underlying principle is that zakat must be transferred into the ownership of a poor Muslim. In each forbidden case, no such transfer occurs. For example, with a mosque, there is no individual owner; with a shroud, the deceased cannot own; with a slave, the owner (the master) receives value, but he is likely wealthy. Three proofs are offered: (1) The hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal stating zakat is taken from the rich and given to the poor of the Muslim community; (2) The athar of al-Thawri listing prohibited uses; (3) The Quranic verse restricting zakat to eight categories. The passage then clarifies that while zakat cannot be given to non-Muslims, optional charity (sadaqah tatawwu') can be given to them, especially for maintaining family ties, as shown by the hadith of Asma bint Abi Bakr with her polytheist mother. Finally, the ruling that zakat should not be given to a wealthy person is emphasized.

Key Terms
ذمى (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection who is not eligible to receive zakat.
صدقة تطوع (sadaqah tatawwu'): Voluntary charity beyond zakat, permissible to give to non-Muslims especially for family ties.
غنى (ghani): A wealthy person who possesses nisab or has sufficient income; zakat should not be given to such a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an impermissible use of zakat according to the passage?
A) Giving zakat to a poor Muslim relative.
B) Using zakat to build a mosque.
C) Giving optional charity to a non-Muslim mother.
D) Giving zakat to a poor Muslim traveler (ibn al-sabil).

Key Takeaway
Zakat is only fulfilled when it is given into the ownership of a poor Muslim; any use that bypasses tamlik is invalid.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Zakat Requires Tamleek: Invalid Uses of Zakat
Ruling with proof on invalid recipients and uses of zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of tamleek (making the recipient owner) for zakat validity and identify which uses of zakat funds are invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Zakat is invalid unless the recipient is made owner; spending on mosques or the dead does not fulfill tamleek.

This lesson establishes a core condition for zakat in the Hanafi school: the payment must involve tamleek, i.e., transferring ownership to a poor Muslim. The passage lists several common practices—like building mosques or shrouding the dead—that do not fulfill this condition and therefore do not discharge the zakat obligation. We will examine the textual proofs and understand the legal reasoning behind this restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
The passage states that zakat is only valid when the recipient is made owner (mālik banānā). This is the key condition (tamleek). Without it, the zakat obligation remains unfulfilled.
Tamleek distinguishes zakat from mere charitable spending.
2
List the Invalid Uses of Zakat
The passage explicitly forbids using zakat for: building mosques, shrouding the dead, buying slaves to free, giving to the rich, paying debts of the deceased, performing Hajj, giving to Jews and Christians, and hiring a carrier. For each, the missing element is tamleek of a poor Muslim.
Some of these may seem charitable but are legally insufficient.
3
Locate the Primary Proof
The primary proof is the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal (Bukhari) where the Prophet says: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed upon them a charity taken from their rich and given to their poor.' This indicates a direct transfer from rich to poor.
The phrase 'faturaddu 'ala fuqaraihim' specifies the recipients as the poor (fuqara).
4
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith uses 'min aghniyaihim' (from their rich) and 'faturaddu 'ala fuqaraihim' (returned to their poor). The word 'faturaddu' implies returning as ownership, and limiting to 'their poor' (the Muslim poor) excludes non-Muslims and other uses.
Hanafi usul: a general command (amr) indicates obligation; here the specification (khass) of poor indicates exclusivity.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dimension
The passage hints that other schools may allow some of these uses. For example, some permit giving zakat for mosque construction or to non-Muslims. The Hanafi school maintains a strict requirement of tamleek to a Muslim poor person.
The ikhtilaf stems from differing interpretations of the hadith and the Quranic verse (9:60).

۵۲۴] (۱۲) زکوۃ کسی مالدار کو نہ دی جائے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) اللہ نے ان پر زکوۃ فرض کی ہے جو ان کے مالداروں سے لی جائے گی اور ان کے فقراء پر تقسیم کی جائے گی (ب) حضرت ثوری سے منقول ہے کہ کوئی آدمی اپنے ذوی الارحام کے نفقہ کا ذمہ دار ہو اس پر اپنی زکوۃ خرچ نہ کرے۔ اور نہ دے میت کے کفن میں۔ اور نہ میت کے قرض میں۔ اور نہ مسجد کے بنانے میں۔ اور نہ قرآن کے خریدنے میں۔ اور نہ اس سے حج کیا جائے اور اس کو اپنے مکاتب کو دیں۔ اور نہ اس سے کوئی غلام خریدے جس کو آزاد کرے۔ اور نہ یہود اور نصاری کو دے۔ اور نہ زکوۃ ہی سے اجرت پر کسی کو لیا جائے جو اس کو ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ لے جائے ( ج ) حضرت اسماء فرماتی ہیں کہ میرے پاس میری ماں آئی اس حال میں کہ عہد قریش کو چاہتی تھی اور غضبناک تھی کہ مشرکہ تھی۔ میں نے کہا اے اللہ کے رسول ! میری ماں میرے پاس آئی ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ غضبناک ہے، مشرکہ ہے۔ کیا میں ان کے ساتھ صلہ رحمی کروں؟ آپ نے فرمایا ہاں ! اپنی ماں کے ساتھ صلہ رحمی کرو۔
A dead person is not shrouded with it, nor is a slave bought to be freed, nor is it given to a rich person. If the recipient of zakat is not made owner, then the zakat is not paid. In the mentioned cases, a poor person is not made owner, so zakat is not paid. For example, in building a mosque, a poor person is not made owner. Similarly, in giving a shroud to the deceased, the deceased cannot be made owner because after death how can he be made owner? Similarly, in buying a slave to free, the slave is not made owner; rather his master is made owner, and the master is rich, so zakat is not paid. (2) From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to Mu'adh ibn Jabal: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed upon them a charity taken from their rich and given to their poor.' (Bukhari, no. 1496) This hadith indicates that zakat is taken from Muslim rich and distributed to Muslim poor, so giving zakat to non-Muslims is not permissible. (3) This athar supports the above issues. From al-Thawri: A man should not give his zakat to one whose maintenance he is responsible for from his relatives, nor give it for a shroud of a dead, nor for a debt of a dead, nor for building a mosque, nor for buying a Quran, nor should he perform Hajj with it, nor give it to his mukatab, nor buy a slave to free with it, nor give it to Jews and Christians, nor hire someone to carry it from one place to another. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab: li-man al-zakah, vol. 4, p. 13, no. 170; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 2, p. 202, no. 10410) This hadith supports all the above issues. (4) In the verse, 'innama' restricts it to eight categories, meaning zakat is only discharged by giving it to these eight categories, and it is necessary to make a poor Muslim owner. Giving nafl sadaqah to a dhimmi is permissible. From Asma: She said: 'My mother came to me during the Quraysh treaty, and she was angry and a polytheist. I said, O Messenger of Allah, my mother has come to me angry and polytheist, should I maintain ties with her? He said: Yes, maintain ties with your mother.' (Abu Dawood, no. 1668) This hadith indicates that maintaining ties with a polytheist and giving nafl sadaqah is permissible.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that zakat must be given to a poor Muslim and the recipient must be made owner. Zakat cannot be used for building mosques, shrouding the dead, buying slaves to free, or given to the rich. The proof is from the hadith of Mu'adh that zakat is taken from the rich and given to the poor. Another proof is the athar from al-Thawri listing invalid uses. The passage also clarifies that giving zakat to non-Muslims is not allowed, but giving nafl sadaqah to them is permissible, supported by the hadith of Asma about her polytheist mother.

Key Terms
زکوۃ (zakāh): The obligatory charity that is one of the five pillars, given to eight categories specified in the Quran.
مالک بنانا (mālik banānā): The condition of transferring ownership of the zakat payment to the recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Zakat is only valid when given directly to a poor Muslim with the intention of making them owner; any use that does not transfer ownership is insufficient.

Zakat Cannot Be Given to Ascending or Descending Relatives
Ruling with proof on prohibited zakat recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to lineal ascendants, descendants, and spouse, explain the legal reasoning (return of benefit), and identify the primary hadith and athar evidence.

Core Idea
Giving zakat to your own dependents is invalid—the benefit returns to you.

This passage from our text presents a fundamental rule of zakat disbursement: you cannot give your zakat to your parents, grandparents, children, grandchildren, or spouse. Why? Because these individuals are your dependents (iyāl), and giving to them effectively means the money remains within your household. The zakat obligation requires transferring ownership (tamleek) to a recipient who is not a dependent. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence from hadith and athar, and the underlying principle that prevents discharge of zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage clearly states: 'The zakāh-payer should not give his zakāh to his father, grandfather... child, grandchild... mother, grandmother... nor to his wife.' This is a prohibition (la yadfa‘). Identify that the act is giving zakat to these specific relatives and the ruling is that it does not discharge the zakat obligation.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the relative is poor or rich.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The author cites a hadith from Abu Sa‘īd (ra) that charity is not permissible for the rich except for specific categories. Understand how this hadith is used to support the rule: giving to those who are not genuinely needy (or whose need is not independent) is not valid.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear.
3
Understand the underlying reasoning (‛illa)
The commentator explains that the close relationship makes these individuals dependents; their maintenance is obligatory on the giver. Therefore, giving zakat to them is like keeping the money for oneself—the required transfer of ownership (tamleek) is not genuinely achieved.
This is the key principle: if the benefit ultimately returns to the giver, the zakat is invalid.
4
Note the exception from the athar
The athar from Ibn ‘Abbās (ra) says there is no harm in giving zakāt to relatives provided they are not dependents (‛iyāl). This implies that if the relative is not a dependent (e.g., a poor cousin), giving zakat is allowed. The passage clarifies that ascendants, descendants, and spouse are always dependents.
This distinguishes between relatives who are dependents and those who are not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يدفع المزكى زكوته الى ابيه وجده وان علا ولا الى ولده وولد ولده وان سفل ولا الى امه وجداته وان علت ولا الى امرأته حدیث میں ہے عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله لا تحل الصدقة لغني الا في سبيل الله او ابن السبيل او جار فقير يتصدق عليه فيهدی لک او يدعوك (الف ) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب من یجوز له اخذ الصدقته وهوغنی ص ۲۳۸ نمبر ۱۶۳۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مالدار کے لئے عام حالات میں زکوۃ لینا جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ مجاہد ہو یا مسافر ہو۔ [ ۵۲۵] (۱۳) زکوہ دینے والا زکوۃ نہ دے اپنے باپ کو ، اپنے دادا کو اگر چہ اوپر تک ہو، اپنی اولاد کو نہ اولاد کی اولاد کو اگر چہ نیچے تک ہو، نہ اپنی ماں کو نہ اپنی دادی کو اگر چہ اوپر تک ہو، اور نہ اپنی بیوی کو ۔ (1) ان لوگوں کے ساتھ اتنا گہرا رابطہ ہوتا ہے کہ ان کا نان و نفقہ بھی اپنے ہی ذمہ ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان لوگوں کو دینا گویا کہ زکوۃ کا مال اپنے ہی پاس رکھ لینا ہے۔ اس لئے زکوۃ کا مال ان لوگوں کو دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے کہ جن لوگوں کی کفالت کرتا ہوا اور اصول و فروع میں سے ہوں ان کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی عن ابن عباس قال لا بأس ان تجعل زكوتك في ذوی قرابتک مالم يكونوا في عيالك (ب) (مصنف ابی ابی شیبة ۹۶ ما قالوافی الرجل يدفع زکوتہ الی قرابته ج ثانی ص۴۱۲، نمبر ۱۰۵۳۱ر مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب لمن الزكوة ج رابع ص ۱۲ نمبر ۷۱۶۴ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو قریب کے رشتہ دار ہوں اور اس کی قدرتی طور پر کفالت بھی کرتا ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی نوٹ باپ، دادا، ماں، دادی اصول ہیں اور بیٹا، پوتا فروع ہیں۔
The zakāh-payer should not give his zakāh to his father, his grandfather however high, nor to his child, nor his grandchild however low, nor to his mother, nor his grandmother however high, nor to his wife. There is a hadith from Abu Sa‘īd: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Charity is not permissible for a rich person except in the cause of Allah, or a traveler, or a poor neighbor who is given charity and then gives a gift to you or invites you.” (Abu Dāwūd, no. 1637) From this hadith it is understood that in general circumstances it is not permissible for a rich person to receive zakāh, unless he is a mujāhid or a traveler. [525] (13) The zakāh-payer should not give zakāh to his father, his grandfather however high, nor to his child, nor his grandchild however low, nor to his mother, nor his grandmother however high, nor to his wife. (1) The connection with these people is so close that their maintenance is his responsibility. So giving to them is like keeping the zakāh money with himself, therefore giving zakāh to them does not discharge the zakāh. (2) There is an athar: “There is no harm in you placing your zakāh among your relatives as long as they are not your dependents.” (Musannaf Ibn Abī Shaybah, no. 10531; Musannaf ‘Abd al-Razzāq, no. 7164) From this athar it is understood that close relatives whom one naturally provides for cannot be given zakāh. Note: Father, grandfather, mother, grandmother are uṣūl (ascendants); son, grandson are furū‘ (descendants).
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that a person cannot give zakāh to his own parents, grandparents, children, grandchildren, or spouse. The reason given is that these people are dependents of the giver; their maintenance is obligatory upon him. Giving zakāh to them would effectively return the money to himself, defeating the purpose of zakāh. The proof includes a hadith from Abu Sa‘īd that charity is not allowed for the rich, implying that if the relative is rich, it is invalid; but even if poor, the close relationship prevents tamleek. An athar from Ibn ‘Abbās confirms that zakāh can be given to relatives only if they are not dependents. The passage distinguishes between uṣūl (ascendants) and furū‘ (descendants).

Key Terms
اصول (uṣūl): Lineal ascendants: father, mother, grandfathers, grandmothers.
فروع (furū‘): Lineal descendants: children, grandchildren.
عیال (iyāl): Dependents whose maintenance is obligatory upon the giver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the child is not poor

C) Because children cannot own property
D) Because the child is a minor

Key Takeaway
Giving zakat to one's own ascendants, descendants, or spouse is invalid because the condition of transferring ownership away from the giver is not fulfilled.

Wife Giving Zakah to Husband: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wife giving zakat to husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conflicting positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a woman giving zakah to her husband, and explain the reasoning and practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
A wife cannot give zakah to her husband because it returns to her; the Sahibayn disagree.

Zakah must be given to eligible recipients, and tamleek (transfer of ownership) must be complete. A classic intra-Hanafi dispute arises when a wife wishes to give her obligatory zakah to her husband. Imam Abu Hanifa rules it invalid, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), permit it. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and highlights the practical consequence for a Hanafi mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Positions
The core question is whether a wife may give her obligatory zakah to her husband. Memorise: Abu Hanifa says no; the Sahibayn say yes.
2
Analyse Abu Hanifa's Proof (Dependency Argument)
Abu Hanifa argues that the wife is a dependent (kafilat) of the husband – he maintains her. Therefore if she gives him zakah, the benefit eventually returns to her, so tamleek is not realised and the zakah obligation remains undischarged.
This is based on the principle that zakah cannot go to a dependent whose maintenance is obligatory on the giver.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's Proof (Non-Dependency & Hadith)
The Sahibayn counter that the husband is not a dependent of the wife – she is not obliged to maintain him. They also cite a hadith where a woman gave her necklace as charity, implying she could have given to her husband.
The hadith is incomplete in the text but is used as supporting evidence.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
According to Abu Hanifa, if a wife gives her zakah to her husband, the zakah is not valid; she must re-give it to another eligible recipient. According to the Sahibayn, it is valid and the obligation is discharged.
This difference directly affects the wife's zakah obligation and liability.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa (prohibition). Hence, a Hanafi mufti should advise that a woman may not give her obligatory zakah to her husband.
However, she may give voluntary charity (nafl sadaqah) to him by consensus.

Source Text

[۵۲۶] (۱۴) اور زکوۃ نہ دے عورت اپنے شوہر کو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ شوہر کو دے۔ (۱) امام اعظم کی دلیل اوپر کے مسئلہ نمبر ۱۳ کا اثر ہے کہ جو کفالت میں ہو ان کو زکوۃ نہیں دے سکتے ۔ اور بیوی شوہر کی کفالت میں ہے اس لئے زکوۃ اس پر ہی لوٹ آئے گی۔ اس لئے اس کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی (۲) شوہر کو دینے سے نان و نفقہ کے طور پر مال خود بیوی پر لوٹ آئے گا۔ اور بعد میں خود بیوی اس مال سے کھائے گی۔ اس لئے گویا کہ اپنی ہی جیب میں زکوۃ کا رکھنا ہوا۔ اس لئے شوہر کو زکوۃ کا مال دینا جائز نہیں۔ البتہ نفلی صدقہ شوہر کو دے سکتی ہے۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ بیوی اپنی زکوۃ شوہر کو دے سکتی ہے۔ (۱) شوہر بیوی کے عیال میں نہیں ہے۔ یعنی بیوی پر شوہر کا نان و نفقہ لازم نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابی سعید الخدری ... قالت یا نبی الله انک امرت اليوم بالصدقة وكان عندى حلی لی فاردت ان اتصدق به فزعم ابن مسعود انه حاشیہ : (الف) ...
And a woman should not give zakāh to her husband according to Abu Hanīfa (may Allah have mercy on him), but the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad) said she may give to him. [526] (14) And a woman should not give zakāh to her husband according to Imam Abū Hanīfa, and the Şāhibayn said that she may give to her husband. (1) The proof of Imam A‘zam is the athar of the previous issue no. 13, that those who are dependents cannot be given zakāh. The wife is a dependent of the husband, so the zakāh would return to her. Therefore giving zakāh to him does not discharge the zakāh. (2) By giving to the husband, the money as maintenance would return to the wife herself, and she would later eat from it, so it is like keeping the zakāh in her own pocket. Hence giving zakāh to the husband is not permissible. However, she can give voluntary charity (nafl sadaqah) to her husband. And the Şāhibayn say that a woman may give her zakāh to her husband. Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding whether a wife may give her zakāh to her husband. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that she cannot, because the wife is a dependent of the husband; thus giving zakāh to him effectively returns the benefit to her. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the husband is not a dependent of the wife, so she may give zakāh to him. The passage provides reasoning for both views. It also clarifies that voluntary charity (nafl sadaqah) to the husband is permissible by consensus.

Key Terms
صاحبین (al-Şāhibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
کفالت (kafālat): Being a dependent; one who is maintained by another.
تملیک (tamleek): Transfer of ownership; a crucial condition for zakah to be valid.

Key Takeaway
A woman may not give her obligatory zakah to her husband according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, because the benefit would return to her due to his maintenance obligation.
