Prohibition of Giving Zakat to Ascendants, Descendants, and Spouse
States the Hanafi ruling prohibiting zakat to close dependents with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which relatives are prohibited to receive zakat in the Hanafi school and explain the legal reasoning based on the obligation of maintenance.

Core Idea
Giving zakat to dependents whose maintenance you owe is like keeping it for yourself; the obligation remains unfulfilled.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam that must be given to deserving recipients with specific conditions. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the zakat payer cannot transfer wealth to those who are already his legal dependents, as the money would effectively return to him. This lesson explores the ruling, its rationale, and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage to find which relatives are explicitly prohibited: father, grandfather, mother, grandmother, children, grandchildren, and wife. Note that the prohibition includes all ascendants and descendants, regardless of degree.
The term 'usul' and 'furu' is introduced; memorize their definitions.
2
Understand the rationale
The text explains that these relatives are within the payer's obligatory maintenance (nafaqah). Therefore, giving zakat to them is like keeping the money for oneself; the zakat obligation is not discharged.
The prohibition is based on the principle that zakat must be a transfer of wealth to someone else, not a circular transfer.
3
Examine the evidence
The passage cites a hadith that zakat is not permissible for the wealthy, and dependents are considered 'wealthy' because their needs are covered. Also, an athar from Ibn Abbas limits zakat to relatives who are not dependents.
This shows the importance of textual evidence (Quran and Sunnah) in establishing fiqh rulings.
4
Recognize the exception
The athar indicates that zakat can be given to other relatives (e.g., cousins, uncles) as long as they are not in the payer's care. The prohibition only applies to the specific categories of usul, furu', and spouse.
The exception confirms the rule: interdependency is the key factor.
5
Apply the rule
Consider a scenario: a person has a poor mother and a poor cousin. Which can receive zakat? Apply the rule: mother is prohibited (usul), cousin is permissible (not a dependent).
Practical application solidifies understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يدفع المزكى زكوته الى ابيه وجده وان علا ولا الى ولده وولد ولده وان سفل ولا الى امه وجداته وان علت ولا الى امرأته. حدیث میں ہے عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله لا تحل الصدقة لغني الا في سبيل الله او ابن السبيل او جار فقير يتصدق عليه فيهدی لک او يدعوك (ابو داؤد شریف، باب من یجوز له اخذ الصدقته وهوغنی ص ۲۳۸ نمبر ۱۶۳۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مالدار کے لئے عام حالات میں زکوۃ لینا جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ مجاہد ہو یا مسافر ہو۔ [ ۵۲۵] (۱۳) زکوہ دینے والا زکوۃ نہ دے اپنے باپ کو ، اپنے دادا کو اگر چہ اوپر تک ہو، اپنی اولاد کو نہ اولاد کی اولاد کو اگر چہ نیچے تک ہو، نہ اپنی ماں کو نہ اپنی دادی کو اگر چہ اوپر تک ہو، اور نہ اپنی بیوی کو ۔ (1) ان لوگوں کے ساتھ اتنا گہرا رابطہ ہوتا ہے کہ ان کا نان و نفقہ بھی اپنے ہی ذمہ ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان لوگوں کو دینا گویا کہ زکوۃ کا مال اپنے ہی پاس رکھ لینا ہے۔ اس لئے زکوۃ کا مال ان لوگوں کو دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے کہ جن لوگوں کی کفالت کرتا ہوا اور اصول و فروع میں سے ہوں ان کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی عن ابن عباس قال لا بأس ان تجعل زكوتك في ذوی قرابتک مالم يكونوا في عيالك (مصنف ابی ابی شیبة ۹۶ ما قالوافی الرجل يدفع زکوتہ الی قرابته ج ثانی ص۴۱۲، نمبر ۱۰۵۳۱ر مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب لمن الزكوة ج رابع ص ۱۲ نمبر ۷۱۶۴ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو قریب کے رشتہ دار ہوں اور اس کی قدرتی طور پر کفالت بھی کرتا ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی نوٹ باپ، دادا، ماں، دادی اصول ہیں اور بیٹا، پوتا فروع ہیں۔
And the one giving zakat does not give his zakat to his father, nor his grandfather even if upwards, nor to his child nor his grandchild even if downwards, nor to his mother nor his grandmothers even if upwards, nor to his wife. Hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Charity (sadaqah) is not permissible for a wealthy person except in the way of Allah, or the wayfarer, or a poor neighbor who is given charity and then gifts it to you or invites you.' (Abu Dawood, no. 1637) From this hadith it is understood that it is not permissible for a wealthy person to take zakat under normal circumstances unless he is a fighter or a traveler. [525] (13) The zakat giver should not give zakat to his father, his grandfather even if upwards, his children nor their children even if downwards, his mother nor his grandmothers even if upwards, and nor to his wife. (1) The relationship with these people is so strong that their maintenance is his responsibility. Therefore, giving to them is like keeping the zakat money with oneself. Hence, giving zakat money to them does not fulfill the zakat obligation. (2) There is an athar that giving zakat to those whom one supports and who are among the usul (ascendants) and furu' (descendants) does not fulfill the zakat. From Ibn Abbas: 'There is no harm in giving your zakat to your relatives as long as they are not your dependents.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this athar it is understood that if the close relatives are naturally under one's support, then giving zakat to them does not fulfill the zakat. Note: father, grandfather, mother, grandmother are usul; son, grandson are furu'.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage states a key ruling in the book of Zakat: the zakat payer cannot give his zakat to his ascendants (parents, grandparents upwards) nor to his descendants (children, grandchildren downwards) nor to his wife. The reason given is that these individuals are within the payer's obligatory maintenance (nafaqah). Hence, giving zakat to them is effectively like keeping the money for oneself, and the zakat obligation remains unfulfilled. The text supports this with a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that zakat is not permissible for the wealthy except in five cases, implying that the dependents of the wealthy are effectively wealthy. Additionally, an athar from Ibn Abbas allows giving zakat to relatives as long as they are not dependents. The text also defines usul (ascendants) and furu' (descendants).

Key Terms
اصول (usul): Ascendants including parents, grandparents and upwards.
فروع (furu'): Descendants including children, grandchildren and downwards.
عيال (iyal): Dependents whom one is obligated to support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Orphan cousin who is not in his care
B) His poor grandfather
C) His neighbor who is a faqir
D) His adult son who is poor but not in his care

Key Takeaway
Giving zakat to one's ascendants, descendants, and spouse does not fulfill the zakat obligation because their maintenance is obligatory on the payer.

Wife Giving Zakat to Husband: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on wife giving zakat to husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a wife giving zakat to her husband, identify the proofs for each, and explain why the relied-upon view prohibits it.

Core Idea
A wife cannot give zakat to her husband because he is her maintainer; voluntary charity is allowed.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi dispute: can a wife fulfill her obligatory zakat by giving it to her husband? The differing views of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), hinge on the nature of the husband's maintenance and the interpretation of a key hadith. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between obligatory and voluntary charity and recognize the principles that govern zakat eligibility.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn each rule regarding a wife giving her zakat to her husband.
Abu Hanifa says it is not permissible (ghayr mujzi); the Sahibayn say it is permissible.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Understand the reasoning: the wife is under the husband's care (kafalah), so giving zakat to him effectively returns the money to herself.
This is based on the principle that one cannot give zakat to those whose maintenance is obligatory upon the giver.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
They rely on the hadith of the wife of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet said 'your husband and child are more entitled to your charity.'
They interpret 'charity' (sadaqah) as including obligatory zakat.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that the hadith refers to voluntary charity (nafl), not obligatory zakat.
This distinction is crucial: nafl sadaqah can be given to anyone, including one's spouse.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to Abu Hanifa, if the wife gives zakat to her husband, her obligation remains unfulfilled; she must give it elsewhere. According to the Sahibayn, it is fulfilled.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

[۵۲۶] (۱۴) ولا تدفع المرأة الى زوجها عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وقالا تدفع اليه. (۱) امام اعظم کی دلیل اوپر کے مسئلہ نمبر ۱۳ کا اثر ہے کہ جو کفالت میں ہو ان کو زکوۃ نہیں دے سکتے ۔ اور بیوی شوہر کی کفالت میں ہے اس لئے زکوۃ اس پر ہی لوٹ آئے گی۔ اس لئے اس کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی (۲) شوہر کو دینے سے نان و نفقہ کے طور پر مال خود بیوی پر لوٹ آئے گا۔ اور بعد میں خود بیوی اس مال سے کھائے گی۔ اس لئے گویا کہ اپنی ہی جیب میں زکوۃ کا رکھنا ہوا۔ اس لئے شوہر کو زکوۃ کا مال دینا جائز نہیں۔ البتہ نفلی صدقہ شوہر کو دے سکتی ہے۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ بیوی اپنی زکوۃ شوہر کو دے سکتی ہے۔ (۱) شوہر بیوی کے عیال میں نہیں ہے۔ یعنی بیوی پر شوہر کا نان و نفقہ لازم نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابی سعید الخدری ... قالت یا نبی الله انک امرت اليوم بالصدقة وكان عندى حلی لی فاردت ان اتصدق به فزعم ابن مسعود انه حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا ز کوۃ حلال نہیں ہے مالدار کے لئے مگر اللہ کے راستے میں ہو یا مسافر ہو یا فقیر پڑوسی ہو اس پر صدقہ کیا جائے تو وہ آپ کو ہدیہ دے یا آپ کو کھلائے پلائے تو حلال ہے (ب) ابن عباس نے فرمایا ہاں جب کہ وہ رشتہ دار اس کے عیال میں نہ ہوں۔ قالت یا نبی الله انک امرت اليوم بالصدقة وكان عندى حلی لی فاردت ان اتصدق به فزعم ابن مسعود انه وولده احق من تصدقت به عليهم فقال رسول الله صدق ابن مسعود زوجک وولدک احق من تصدقت به عليهم (بخاری شریف ، باب الزکوۃ علی الاقارب ص ۱۹۷ نمبر ۱۴۶۲) اس حدیث میں آپ نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی بیوی سے فرمایا کہ تمہاری اولاد اور تمہارا شوہر تمہارے صدقے کا زیادہ حقدار ہے یعنی زکوۃ کا ، اس لئے بیوی شوہر کو زکوۃ دے تو جائز ہے۔ امام اعظم اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ یہ صدقہ نافلہ کے بارے میں ہے جو ہم بھی جائز کہتے ہیں۔
[526] (14) And the woman does not give (zakat) to her husband according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: she gives to him. (1) The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is the athar from the previous issue (13) that one cannot give zakat to those under one's care. And the wife is under the husband's care, so the zakat will revert to her. Therefore, giving zakat to him does not fulfill the zakat obligation. (2) Giving to the husband results in the money returning to the wife as maintenance, and she will consume it. So it is like putting the zakat in her own pocket. Therefore, giving zakat money to the husband is not permissible. However, she can give nafl (voluntary) charity to her husband. And the two (Sahibayn) say that the wife can give her zakat to her husband. (1) The husband is not among the wife's dependents; that is, the wife is not obligated to provide his maintenance. (2) Hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... she said: O Prophet of Allah, you commanded charity today, and I have some jewelry and want to give it in charity. Ibn Mas'ud claims that his child is more entitled to your charity... Footnote: (a) He said: Zakat is not permissible for the wealthy except in the way of Allah, or the wayfarer, or a poor neighbor who is given charity and then gifts it to you... (b) Ibn Abbas said: Yes, when the relatives are not in his care. She said: O Prophet of Allah, you commanded charity today, and I have some jewelry and want to give it in charity. Ibn Mas'ud claims that his child is more entitled to your charity. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Ibn Mas'ud spoke the truth; your husband and your child are more entitled to your charity.' (Bukhari, Book of Zakat on Relatives, p.197 no.1462) In this hadith, the Prophet told the wife of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that her child and her husband are more deserving of her charity, meaning zakat. Therefore, the wife giving zakat to her husband is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa responds: This hadith is about voluntary charity (nafl), which we also allow.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a wife giving her zakat to her husband. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is not permissible and does not fulfill the zakat obligation. His reasoning is that the wife is under the husband's maintenance (nafaqah), so giving zakat to him is effectively returning the money to herself. Additionally, the husband benefits from the zakat as a form of maintenance, which indirectly benefits the wife. Therefore, it is like keeping the zakat for oneself. However, voluntary charity (nafl sadaqah) to the husband is allowed. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that the wife can give zakat to her husband. They argue that the husband is not among the wife's dependents (she is not obliged to support him), and they cite the hadith of the wife of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, in which the Prophet said that the husband and child are more entitled to her charity. Imam Abu Hanifa responds by clarifying that this hadith refers to voluntary charity, not obligatory zakat. The text does not explicitly give tarjih, but Abu Hanifa's view is presented as the main position.

Key Terms
نفلی صدقہ (nafli sadaqah): Voluntary charity beyond obligatory zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, why is a wife's zakat to her husband invalid?
A) Because the husband is often wealthy
B) Because the wife is under the husband's maintenance, so the money returns to her
C) Because the husband is not a relative
D) Because the wife must give zakat to her parents instead

Key Takeaway
A wife cannot give her obligatory zakat to her husband because he is her maintainer, making the payment invalid; only voluntary charity is permissible.

Prohibition of Giving Zakat to One's Mukatab or Slave
States the prohibition of giving zakat to one's own slave or mukatab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that giving zakat to one's own mukatab or slave does not fulfill the obligation and explain the reason based on ownership.

Core Idea
Giving zakat to one's own slave is like keeping it for yourself—the obligation remains.

Zakat must be given to those who are genuinely needy and independent in ownership. In Hanafi fiqh, a slave and a mukatab (a slave under contract of emancipation) remain the property of their master until full payment. Therefore, giving zakat to them is invalid because the wealth effectively returns to the giver. This lesson explores the ruling and its proof from a companion's statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and prohibition
The act is paying zakat; the prohibition targets payment to one's own mukatab or slave.
2
Understand the legal status of the recipient
Both remain slaves; their property and even their lives belong to the master (mawla).
The mukatab is still a slave until the kitabah is fully paid.
3
Analyze the consequence: why invalid
Giving zakat to them is like giving to oneself; the required transfer of ownership (tamlik) does not occur, so the zakat obligation is not discharged.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil)
An athar from al-Thawri states: 'Do not give it (zakat) to your mukatab.' This indicates prohibition and shows the position is based on authoritative precedent.
The dalil is zanni in transmission but supports the principle.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow giving zakat to a mukatab if he is needy, but the Hanafi position is strict due to ownership continuity.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۲۷] (۱۵) ولا يدفع الى مكاتبه ولا مملو که (1) مکاتب نے جب تک مال کتابت ادا کیا نہ ہو وہ غلام ہی باقی رہتا ہے۔ اور غلام کا سارا مال بلکہ اس کی جان بھی مولی کی ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے مکاتب اور اپنے غلام کو زکوۃ کا مال دینا گویا کہ خود کے پاس رکھ لینا ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے مولی اور اپنے مملوک کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی (۲) پہلے ایک اثر گزر چکا ہے جس میں یہ تھا عن الشورى قال ولا تعطيها مکاتبک (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب لمن ؛ زکوۃ ج رابع ص ۱۳ نمبرہ ۷۱۷ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اپنے مکاتب کو ز کوۃ مت دو اس لئے کہ وہ اس کا غلام ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے غلام کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہو گا۔
[527] (15) And he does not give (zakat) to his mukatab nor to his slave. (1) Until the mukatab pays the kitabah (contract) money, he remains a slave. And all the wealth of a slave, even his life, belongs to the master. Therefore, giving zakat money to one's mukatab or slave is like keeping it for oneself. Hence, giving zakat to one's master or one's slave does not fulfill the zakat obligation. (2) There is an athar that has passed: from al-Thawri: 'Do not give it (zakat) to your mukatab.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Book of Zakat, vol.4, p.13) From this athar, it is understood that you should not give zakat to your mukatab because he is his slave. Thus, giving zakat to one's slave is not permissible.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage rules that a person cannot give his zakat to his own mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom) or to his own slave. The reason is that both remain the property of the master. The mukatab is still a slave until he completes payment, and all his property belongs to the master. Therefore, giving zakat to them is like giving it to oneself, and the zakat obligation is not fulfilled. The text supports this with an athar from al-Thawri, who explicitly prohibits giving zakat to one's mukatab.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract of emancipation for a fixed payment.
مملوک (mamluk): A slave owned by the person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a person give his zakat to his own mukatab slave?
A) Yes, because the mukatab is free
B) No, because the mukatab is still his property
C) Yes, if the mukatab is poor
D) No, only to non-relatives

Key Takeaway
Zakat to one's own slave or mukatab is invalid because the recipient's wealth belongs to the giver.

Prohibition of Giving Zakat to a Wealthy Person's Slave or Minor Child
Ruling on zakat distribution with legal reasoning and hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on giving zakat to a wealthy person's slave or minor child and explain the reasoning and hadith proof.

Core Idea
Zakat to a wealthy man's slave or minor child is invalid — the benefit reaches the wealthy.

This lesson addresses a specific yet common question: Can zakat be given to the slave or minor child of a wealthy person? The Hanafi ruling is clear: it is not permissible, because the benefit ultimately goes to the wealthy owner or father. The text provides both legal reasoning and a hadith proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Giving zakat to a wealthy person's slave or minor child. The ruling is that it is invalid (batil).
The text says 'not permissible' (ja'iz nahi), which in Hanafi fiqh equates to invalidity.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith from 'Ata ibn Yasar in Abu Dawood: 'Charity is not permissible for a wealthy person except for five...'
This is a sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut, but accepted in fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? The hadith prohibits giving zakat to the wealthy. Giving to a wealthy person's slave or minor child effectively bypasses this prohibition because the benefit reaches the wealthy person.
The slave's wealth belongs to the master; the minor child's wealth is under the father's control.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow giving to a wealthy person's slave if the slave is personally needy, considering the direct recipient's need.
Hanafi overrides this by considering the legal ownership and benefit.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and from zahir al-riwayah, accepted by all Hanafi authorities.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is reported.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۵۲۸] (۱۶) ولا مملوک غنی ولا ولد. اور مالدار کے ملوک کو اور مالدار کی اولاد کو زکوۃ نہ دے جب کہ وہ چھوٹے ہوں۔ پیچھے گزر چکا ہے کہ مملوک کا مال مولی کا مال ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے مالدار کے مملوک کو زکوۃ دی تو وہ مالدار مولی کے ہاتھ میں پہنچ جائے گی اور مالدار کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں اس لئے مالدار کے مملوک کو بھی زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں۔ ہاں غریب آدمی کا مملوک ہو تو اس کو دینا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ غریب مولی کے ہاتھ میں پہنچے گی۔ اسی طرح مالدار آدمی کا چھوٹا بچہ مالدار کی کفالت میں ہوتا ہے اور گویا کہ باپ ہی اس کے مال کا مالک ہوتا ہے اس لئے مالدار کے بچے کے ہاتھ میں زکوۃ دینا گویا کہ مالدار کے ہاتھ میں مال دینا ہے۔ اس لئے مالدار کے چھوٹے بچے کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) چھوٹا بچہ باپ کی مالداری کی وجہ سے مالدار شمار کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے بھی مالدار کے بچے کوزکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ مالدار کے لئے زکوۃ جائز نہیں ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے عن عطاء بن يسار ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا تحل الصدقة لغني الا لخمسة ( ا ) لغاز في سبيل الله (۲) او لعامل عليها (۳) او لغارم (۴) او لرجل اشتراها بماله (۵) او لرجل كان له جار مسكين فتصدق على المسكين فاهدها المسكين للغنى (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من یجوز له اخذ الصدقة وهوفنی ص ۲۳۸ نمبر ۱۶۳۵/۱۶۳۴) و بڑے بچے باپ کے تحت نہیں ہوتے اس لئے اگر باپ مالدار ہو اور اس کا بڑا بچہ غریب ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ دے سکتے ہیں۔
[528] (16) And nor to the slave of a wealthy person nor to his child. And do not give zakat to the slave of a wealthy person and to the child of a wealthy person when they are minors. It has passed earlier that the wealth of a slave belongs to his master. Therefore, if zakat is given to the slave of a wealthy person, it will reach the wealthy master, and giving zakat to a wealthy person is not permissible. So giving zakat to the slave of a wealthy person is also not permissible. However, if it is the slave of a poor person, then giving to him is permissible because it will reach the poor master. Similarly, the minor child of a wealthy person is under the wealthy person's care, and the father is essentially the owner of his child's wealth. Therefore, giving zakat into the hand of a wealthy man's child is like giving money into the hand of the wealthy man. Hence, giving zakat to a wealthy man's minor child is not permissible. (2) The minor child is considered wealthy due to the father's wealth, so also for this reason giving zakat to a wealthy man's child is not permissible. Zakat is not permissible for the wealthy, as per the hadith of 'Ata ibn Yasar: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Charity (sadaqah) is not permissible for a wealthy person except for five: (1) a fighter in the way of Allah, (2) a collector of zakat, (3) a debtor, (4) a man who buys it with his wealth, (5) a man who has a poor neighbor and gives charity to the neighbor and the neighbor gifts it to the wealthy.' (Abu Dawood, nos. 1634/1635) And older children are not under the father's control, so if the father is wealthy and his older child is poor, then zakat can be given to him.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage rules that zakat cannot be given to the slave of a wealthy person, nor to the minor child of a wealthy person. The reasoning: a slave's wealth belongs to his master. Thus, giving zakat to a wealthy person's slave effectively gives the zakat to the wealthy master, which is prohibited. However, if the master is poor, giving to his slave is permissible because the benefit goes to the poor master. Similarly, a wealthy man's minor child is under the father's care and the father is considered the owner of the child's wealth; hence, giving zakat to the child is like giving it to the father. Additionally, the minor child is considered wealthy by virtue of the father's wealth. The text also cites a hadith listing the five exceptions who may receive zakat despite being wealthy. The passage ends by noting that older children are not under the father's control, so if the father is wealthy but the adult child is poor, zakat can be given to that child.

Key Terms
مملوک غنی (mamluk ghani): A slave owned by a wealthy person.
ولد غنی (walad ghani): The minor child of a wealthy person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases is it permissible to give zakat to a child?
A) If the child is wealthy
B) If the child is poor but his father is wealthy and he is a minor
C) If the child is poor and his father is wealthy but he is an adult
D) If the child is a wealthy person's slave

Key Takeaway
Zakat cannot be given to a wealthy person's slave or minor child because the benefit reaches the wealthy person, which is prohibited.

Prohibited Zakat Recipients: One's Own Slaves and the Wealthy's Dependents
Two rulings on prohibited zakat recipients with proofs and response to objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings on prohibited zakat recipients (one's own slaves and the wealthy's slaves/children) and explain the legal reasoning based on ownership and wealth dependency.

Core Idea
Zakat to your own slave or to a wealthy man's slave or child is invalid because the wealth effectively returns to you or to the wealthy.

In this passage, we learn two specific prohibitions regarding zakat disbursement. First, you cannot give zakat to your own slave or mukatab because their property is legally yours. Second, giving zakat to a wealthy person’s slave or young child is also prohibited, as it ultimately benefits the wealthy person. We will examine the proofs from the Sunnah and the responses to potential objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited recipients
From the text, locate the two categories: one's own slave/mukatab, and the slave or young child of a wealthy person. The ruling is: do not give zakat to them.
The second category includes both the slave and the young child.
2
Understand the rationale of ownership and dependency
The prohibition is based on the legal principle that a slave's property belongs to the master, and a young child's wealth is effectively under the father's control. Therefore, giving zakat to these recipients results in the zakat returning to the payer or to a wealthy person, defeating the purpose of zakat as a transfer to the needy.
The text makes an analogy: it is like keeping the zakat for yourself.
3
Examine the proof from the hadith on charity to the wealthy
The hadith from Abu Dawud states that charity (sadaqah) is not permissible for the wealthy except in five cases. This is used as evidence that zakat cannot be given to a wealthy person, and by extension, to his dependents who are not truly needy.
The hadith uses the term 'sadaqah' which includes zakat in this context.
4
Address the objection from the hadith of Ibn Masud's wife
A potential counterargument arises from the hadith where the Prophet said that one's husband and children are most deserving of charity. Imam A'zam clarifies that this refers to voluntary (nafl) charity, not obligatory zakat. Thus, the ruling on zakat remains unchanged.
This shows the importance of interpreting hadith in context and distinguishing between fard and nafl acts.

۵۲۷ (۱۵) ولا يدفع الى مكاتبه ولا مملوکه [۵۲۸) (۱۶) ولا مملوک غنی ولا ولد وولده احق من تصدقت به عليهم فقال رسول الله صدق ابن مسعود زوجک وولدک احق من تصدقت به عليهم (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الزکوۃ علی الاقارب ص ۱۹۷ نمبر ۱۴۶۲) اس حدیث میں آپ نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی بیوی سے فرمایا کہ تمہاری اولاد اور تمہارا شوہر تمہارے صدقے کا زیادہ حقدار ہے یعنی زکوۃ کا ، اس لئے بیوی شوہر کو زکوۃ دے تو جائز ہے۔ امام اعظم اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ یہ صدقہ نافلہ کے بارے میں ہے جو ہم بھی جائز کہتے ہیں۔
[۵۲۷] (۱۵) اور زکوۃ نہ دے اپنے مکاتب غلام کو اور اپنے مملوک کو ۔ (1) مکاتب نے جب تک مال کتابت ادا کیا نہ ہو وہ غلام ہی باقی رہتا ہے۔ اور غلام کا سارا مال بلکہ اس کی جان بھی مولی کی ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے مکاتب اور اپنے غلام کو زکوۃ کا مال دینا گویا کہ خود کے پاس رکھ لینا ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے مولی اور اپنے مملوک کو زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی (۲) پہلے ایک اثر گزر چکا ہے جس میں یہ تھا عن الشورى قال ولا تعطيها مکاتبک (ب)(مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب لمن ؛ زکوۃ ج رابع ص ۱۳ نمبرہ ۷۱۷ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اپنے مکاتب کو ز کوۃ مت دو اس لئے کہ وہ اس کا غلام ہے۔ اس لئے اپنے غلام کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہو گا۔
[۵۲۸] (۱۶) اور مالدار کے ملوک کو اور مالدار کی اولاد کو زکوۃ نہ دے جب کہ وہ چھوٹے ہوں۔ پیچھے گزر چکا ہے کہ مملوک کا مال مولی کا مال ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے مالدار کے مملوک کو زکوۃ دی تو وہ مالدار مولی کے ہاتھ میں پہنچ جائے گی اور مالدار کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں اس لئے مالدار کے مملوک کو بھی زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں۔ ہاں غریب آدمی کا مملوک ہو تو اس کو دینا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ غریب مولی کے ہاتھ میں پہنچے گی۔ اسی طرح مالدار آدمی کا چھوٹا بچہ مالدار کی کفالت میں ہوتا ہے اور گویا کہ باپ ہی اس کے مال کا مالک ہوتا ہے اس لئے مالدار کے بچے کے ہاتھ میں زکوۃ دینا گویا کہ مالدار کے ہاتھ میں مال دینا ہے۔ اس لئے مالدار کے چھوٹے بچے کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) چھوٹا بچہ باپ کی مالداری کی وجہ سے مالدار شمار کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے بھی مالدار کے بچے کوزکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ مالدار کے لئے زکوۃ جائز نہیں ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے عن عطاء بن يسار ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا تحل الصدقة لغني الا لخمسة ( ا ) لغاز في سبيل الله (۲) او لعامل عليها (۳) او لغارم (۴) او لرجل اشتراها بماله (۵) او لرجل كان له جار مسكين فتصدق على المسكين فاهدها المسكين للغنى (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من یجوز له اخذ الصدقة وهوفنی ص ۲۳۸ نمبر ۱۶۳۵/۱۶۳۴) و بڑے بچے باپ کے تحت نہیں ہوتے اس لئے اگر باپ مالدار ہو اور اس کا بڑا بچہ غریب ہو تو اس کو زکوۃ دے سکتے ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ حاشیہ : (الف) ابوسعید خدری سے روایت ہے کہ عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی بیوی کہنے لگی اے اللہ کے نبی! آپ نے آج صدقے کا حکم دیا۔ اور میرے پاس کچھ زیورات ہیں تو میں چاہتی ہوں کہ اس کو صدقہ کروں۔ عبداللہ بن مسعود کا گمان ہے کہ وہ اور ان کی اولا دزیادہ حقدار ہے کہ میں ان پر صدقہ کروں۔ آپ نے فرمایا عبد اللہ بن مسعود صحیح کہتے ہیں۔ تمہارا شوہر اور تمہاری اولا دزیادہ حقدار ہیں آپ ان پر صدقہ کریں (ب) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا اپنے مکاتب کو ز کوۃ دو۔ غنى اذا كان صغيرا
527 (15) And he should not give to his mukatab nor to his slave. (16) And not to the slave of a wealthy person nor to a child. And his child is more deserving of your charity. So the Messenger of Allah said: 'Ibn Masud spoke the truth. Your husband and your child are more deserving of your charity.' (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on zakat on relatives, p. 197, no. 1462) In this hadith, the Prophet said to the wife of Abdullah ibn Masud: 'Your children and your husband are more deserving of your charity,' meaning zakat. Based on this, it is permissible for a wife to give zakat to her husband. Imam A'zam responds that this is about nafl charity, which we also permit. [527] (15) And do not give zakat to your mukatab slave and to your owned slave. (1) The mukatab remains a slave as long as he has not paid the kitabah wealth. And the slave's entire wealth, even his life, belongs to the master. Therefore giving zakat wealth to his mukatab and his slave is like keeping it with himself. Therefore giving zakat to his master and his slave does not fulfill the zakat. (2) Earlier an athar has passed in which it was: from al-Thawri: he said: 'Do not give it to your mukatab' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter for whom zakat, vol. 4, p. 13, hadith 717). From this athar it is known that do not give zakat to your mukatab, because he is his slave. Therefore giving zakat to his own slave is not permissible. [528] (16) And do not give zakat to the slave of a wealthy person and to the children of a wealthy person when they are young. It has already passed that the property of a slave belongs to the master. Therefore if one gives zakat to the slave of a wealthy person, it will reach the wealthy master, and giving zakat to a wealthy person is not permissible. Therefore giving zakat to the slave of a wealthy person is also not permissible. Yes, if the slave belongs to a poor person, then giving to him is permissible, because it will reach the poor master. Similarly, the young child of a wealthy person is under the care of the wealthy person, and the father is essentially the owner of his wealth. Therefore giving zakat to the child of a wealthy person is like giving wealth to the wealthy person. Therefore giving zakat to the young child of a wealthy person is not permissible. (2) A young child is considered wealthy because of the father's wealth, so also for this reason giving zakat to the child of a wealthy person is not permissible. Zakat is not permissible for the wealthy. For this there is a hadith from Ata ibn Yasar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Charity is not permissible for a wealthy person except for five: one who fights in the way of Allah, or a collector, or a debtor, or a man who buys it with his wealth, or a man who has a poor neighbor and gives charity to the poor and then the poor gifts it to the wealthy.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on who may take charity and he is wealthy, p. 238, no. 1635/1634) And older children are not under the father's control, so if the father is wealthy and his older child is poor, then he can give zakat to him. Because... Footnote: (a) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The wife of Abdullah ibn Masud said: 'O Prophet of Allah, you have commanded charity today, and I have some ornaments; I want to give them in charity. Abdullah ibn Masud thinks that he and his children are more deserving that I give charity to them.' The Prophet said: 'Abdullah ibn Masud is right. Your husband and your children are more deserving; give charity to them.' (b) al-Thawri said: 'Do not give zakat to your mukatab.' A wealthy person if he is a minor.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri presents two rulings on prohibited recipients of zakat. The first ruling (15) states that one should not give zakat to one's own mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) or to one's own slave. The reasoning is that a slave's property belongs entirely to the master, so giving zakat to one's own slave merely transfers wealth from oneself to oneself, which does not constitute payment of zakat. The proof is an athar (report) from al-Thawri who said, 'Do not give it to your mukatab.' The second ruling (16) prohibits giving zakat to the slave or young child of a wealthy person. This is because the property of a slave belongs to the master, so sending zakat to a wealthy person's slave effectively gives it to the wealthy master, which is impermissible. Similarly, a wealthy father is the de facto owner of his young child's property, so giving zakat to the child is tantamount to giving it to the father. However, if the master is poor, giving to his slave is permissible. Likewise, if an older child is independent and poor, zakat can be given to him. The passage also addresses a potential objection: a hadith indicates that one's husband and child are most deserving of charity. Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa) responds that this hadith refers to voluntary (nafl) charity, not obligatory zakat, so it does not conflict with the rulings. Additionally, a hadith from Abu Dawud is cited stating that charity is not permissible for the wealthy except in five specific cases. This supports the prohibition of giving zakat to the wealthy. The discussion emphasizes that zakat must be given to those who are truly needy and not to those who are effectively extensions of the payer's own wealth.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract (kitabah) with his master to be freed upon paying a sum of money.
مملوك (mamluk): An owned slave, fully under the master's ownership.
غني (ghani): A wealthy person who possesses nisab or sufficient wealth to be ineligible for zakat.
ولد (walad): Child, specifically a minor child in the context of wealth dependency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible to give zakat to the young child of a wealthy person?
A) Yes, because the child is a minor and thus needy.
B) No, because the child is considered wealthy due to the father's wealth.
C) Yes, but only if the child is an orphan.
D) No, because minors cannot own property.

Key Takeaway
Giving zakat to your own slave or to a wealthy person's slave or young child does not fulfill the obligation because the wealth effectively stays with the payer or the wealthy person.
